Permafrost

It sounded like typical news: the recovery of the endangered arctic fox. What TV reporter Samantha West and cameraman Dave Candid discovered was a poaching ring that the region's governor, Victor Ulrich, is inexplicably trying to cover up.

With the help of their pet cat Geronimo, two arctic foxes on the run, and an unexpected anonymous source, they find themselves investigating the story of a lifetime...which could be their last.

Updates weekly.

Prologue

Wind howled across the tundra, blowing clouds of snow caught in its unforgiving grasp. They twirled like smoke in the dry, cold atmosphere; like leaping, ancient spirits.

The sound of snow crunching underpaw signaled the arrival of a lone arctic fox, who paused momentarily at the top of an icy knoll. Glancing around the harsh landscape, he plunged down to the flatter yet still snow-strewn land below. Here he stopped again, his small ears pricking up.

Could it be? After so long? Tensing his body, he crouched down into the snow - then leapt headlong into it. He dug around hopefully, then sat up with a discouraged look on his face. "Nothing!" he muttered.

"Did you find anything?" The voice of his mate made him turn; he spied her sitting atop the hill, watching him.

"No..." he replied, then trying to sound optimistic, "But we will."

"This has been one of the cruelest winters we have faced." his mate sighed, as she leapt down to join him. "The lemmings are gone...and now those..." She shuddered, and broke off; the male fox tried to reassure her.

"This will not be the first famine - or the last - that we foxes will have faced. As for the danger, we'll find some way to survive." They touched noses and he flicked his tail as a signal for them to head back.

The pair trudged across the barren territory, silent and uneasy; the stabbing, hollow pain of hunger making each pawstep an effort. They were climbing up a glacier, only a few paces away from their den, when the vixen let out a shrill cry.

"No! They found it!"

Surrounding the den entrance were three dangerous-looking humans who seemed preoccupied with their work. Upon hearing the animals, one whipped around sharply to lock eyes with the male fox.

"There!"

"Run!" the male fox cried, as the human lifted his rifle and fired.

The bullet missed by an inch; the vixen sprung up with a yelp and both dashed away. They could hear the human barking orders to the others and quick footsteps in pursuit.

The two foxes fled across the tundra and skidding at a turn, whipped up snow. A second shot was fired; then a third. The foxes' rapid, terrified run soon found them on an ice sheet. There was a piercing noise as one of the bullets cracked the ice; jagged lines splintered across the glassy reflection. In a matter of seconds, the two foxes leapt to solid ground just before another shot broke the frozen water into pieces with a horrifying crash; then the female fox exclaimed:

"The timberline!"

It was their only hope, their only salvation. The male took the lead as the pair flew towards the faraway line of pine forest. Shots rang out around them, spraying snow into the freezing air...the foxes fearing that every bound would be their last...and then...

The two foxes plunged into the bracken. It shivered momentarily with the impact, and grew still. The foxes panted with fear and exertion as they watched their pursuers approach, searching for them. They prayed their beautiful white pelts, their camouflage in the snow, would not betray them to the humans.

Their hearts pounded as the three men crept up slowly, gripping their rifles in tightly clenched hands. They scanned the bushes and at last, the one who had fired on the foxes first, once again spoke.

"Damn those foxes. We lost them."

As the humans retreated, the critters kept perfectly still until they were out of sight. Finally, the male fox breathed a shaky sigh of relief, then turned to his mate, his voice soft.

"We're safe...for now."

Above, the aurora danced in the dark arctic sky. Celestial beauty, an ironic backdrop to a frozen hell...

Chapter 1 - News Trio

"Breaking News! I'm Samantha West coming to you live from the scene of a raging apartment fire in Estrella City, where - as you can see behind me - firefighters are struggling to put out the blaze. Authorities tell us that the fire started at 10 a.m. this morning, on the top floor, and that everyone managed to get out safely. The cause of the fire is still unknown...We'll be keeping you updated on any developments...For now, reporting live from Estrella City, Samantha West, WCAT 8 News."

~

"And...cut!"

TV reporter Samantha Verity West brushed away the earpiece and glanced over at her cameraman, David Candid. She smiled. "I think that came out pretty good," she remarked.

"You always are," Dave replied. "We'd better start getting ready for our noon broadcast," he added with a glance at his watch. "It's in half an hour."

"You're right," Samantha agreed. "Boy, am I hungry! I wonder if there's any place to eat around here?"

"I packed some ham sandwiches for us," said Dave, as the two strolled toward the back of the van. There was a cool, refreshing breeze coming in from the ocean, typical here in the Caribbean where Tropical Island was located; yet it did nothing to quench the fire, which despite the attempts of firemen, still burned fiercely in the warmth of the tropical sun.

Samantha Verity West and David Candid worked for WCAT channel 8 on Tropical Island. Samantha was a general-assignment news reporter; Dave was a photo-journalist and regularly paired up with Samantha as her cameraman, most especially since they had established a personal relationship.

They were both in their mid-to-late twenties. Samantha was slender, with vivid green eyes and short brunette hair with shaggy bangs, and almost always wore formal office attire. Dave was muscular, with short, tousled dark brown hair and brown eyes, and dressed casually.

"Hopefully they'll have that blaze extinguished soon." Samantha was commenting as her partner slid open the back door. "I'd like to interview the fire chief..."

"Hi guys!" A familiar meow broke into her conversation; reporter and cameraman both glanced down in surprise to see...

"Geronimo!" they exclaimed in unison.

The slim tomcat ignored the disbelief in their eyes. "Man, that was so cool!" he purred happily. "I love the way you can keep your voice so even on the air. I saw it all on your tiny TVs here," Geronimo continued, flicking his tail at the numerous monitors inside the satellite van. "Say, what's the point of having so many TVs?"

"Geronimo, what are you doing here?" Samantha was still in shock.

"So much for lunch," Dave sighed, looking past Geronimo to the crumpled wrappers thrown on the van floor.

"Oh." Geronimo glanced over his shoulder. "That was yours?"

"Geronimo..." Samantha said, trying to maintain calm, "What on earth are you doing here?"

"Oh man, it's so boring at home; you have no idea." Geronimo quickly explained. "I want some adventure; excitement, like you guys!"

"So... you decided to follow us?" Samantha said incredulously.

"Well, yeah!"

"But did you have to eat our food?" Dave asked.

"It was just sitting there and I was hungry" Geronimo protested.

"The sandwiches are besides the point," said Samantha. "You snuck into our van and traveled halfway across Tropical Island with us because you were bored?!"

Before the cat had time to answer, Dave's cell phone rang. "Hello. Dave Candid speaking. Yes sir. I'll tell her. Thank you."

He hung up and looked at Samantha.

"Ted Hughes," she said. Dave nodded.

"Let me guess..." Samantha continued. "We'll be first on the air, right?"

"Sam...I've said it before and I'll say it again. You've got a keen mind to discern possibilities...How did you guess it was Ted?"

Samantha sighed and said, "Easy. What else could happen? Our lunch is gone, we've got a hot story that needs wrapping, and a stowaway cat... Of course Ted will want for us to start first...That way we have no time to prepare."

"Samantha, do you want me to call him and explain..." Dave began.

"Nope" Samantha interrupted. "I do well under pressure. My best stories are spontaneous. Let's go tiger!"

"Yeah! Where to?" Geronimo jumped up.

"Not you kitty...I meant my cameraman" Samantha explained.

"Have I ever told you that your green eyes sparkle when you are eager to do a story?" Dave smiled at the reporter.

"Yes. Often. Especially when we make love." Samantha winked at him.

Geronimo purred loudly. Samantha looked at the cat and said, "Geronimo. You must be quiet and stay here. We don't want you getting lost. After this story, we'll be dropping you off at home. Now, promise me you will stay here."

"I purrr-omise" said the cat. He squinted his blue eyes and stuck his tail up straight.

Samantha stared at the cat for a minute, a little uncertain as to whether he was planning more mischief, but he just sat there looking innocent. "Ok. Dave let's set up over there...I want to get some interviews."

Samantha grabbed a microphone and they walked quickly to a spot not far from the news van.

By now, the fire was under control and Samantha interviewed the fire chief.

Immersed in the questioning and filming, both reporter and cameraman forgot about the cat.

"This is Samantha West...reporting live at the scene." Samantha ended her report.

As the monitor image shifted to the network broadcast’s next story, Dave smiled and said, "That's a wrap; now maybe we can go get something to eat."

As the two were gathering their equipment, a colleague from a newspaper came running over. "Hey guys! I just thought I'd give you fair warning about the picture that'll appear in the morning edition," he said cheerfully.

"What are you talking about, Daniel?" Samantha asked.

"The cat, of course. It's a cute touch...a cat with the news van. Is he some kind of mascot or good luck charm?" Daniel asked.

Dave and Samantha looked at each other, then looked at their station’s van.

It was a white commercial van adorned on its side with the recognizable red insignia of their television station – WCAT ⑧. Underneath the call letters was a slim black parallelogram within which the word NEWS was spelled out in a glowing light-blue design. A microwave antenna was anchored on the roof of the vehicle; it was a tall, columnar fixture that reached to a large height, though it could shrink down to an unobtrusive size when not broadcasting.

There was one more thing atop the roof: a cat. It was a lynx-point Siamese cat which was happily poking the transmitter antenna. It was Geronimo.

"Geronimo!" the two television journalists shouted.

"Well, gotta go!" Daniel excused as he hurried away.

Geronimo, sensing another scolding, flattened his ears and hid inside the car. The reporter and her cameraman got into the van and drove away in silence. On the way to the television station they stopped in front of their home where their other two cats - Tifarah and Butch, Geronimo's parents - were basking in the sunshine.

Tifarah was a purebred Siamese with brilliant blue eyes and Butch was a brown-tabby-and-white tomcat.

Their son, Geronimo, had Siamese points and blue eyes like his mother yet stripes on his tail, legs and face like his father. His tail was kinked like the cats of ancient Siam, and the upward tilt of it was considered a rarity. He was an exquisite looking cat.

Samantha placed the young tomcat on the ground and looking into the eyes of two very perplexed cats, said "Ask your son to explain what he's been up to today. We'll discuss it after I get back from work. Tif, what do you want for dinner tonight? Sardines or Tuna?"

"It's all good, thanks." replied the cat and turned attention to her son, "What have you done, now?"

Before Geronimo could say anything, the news van sped off. Geronimo answered, "I'm not sure what the problem was...either the fact that I ate their ham sandwiches or maybe that guy from the newspaper taking my picture. You know, he said that I photograph well..."

"Wait..." Butch, his father interrupted. "What newspaper guy; what picture?"

"Oh, you know him," Geronimo replied, "Daniel Thompson, the guy from The Gazette."

Tifarah opened her eyes wide and said, "Tangerine's human? He took your picture...for the newspaper?"

"Why would he take your picture, son?" Butch said through slitty eyes.

"I was sitting on top of the news van while Samantha was giving her report. You know there's a great view from up there." Geronimo purred.

The two older cats glanced at each other and then at their young son.

Butch was the first to speak. "As far as cat mischief goes...it's pretty good."

Tifarah added, "The problem is that our humans were working, and you're not supposed to be there at the time. In the future, don't climb onto the roof of the news van while they're reporting."

That evening, after Samantha and Dave arrived home, they explained to Geronimo that he should not be wandering very far.

"You might get lost," Samantha admonished.

"I won't," answered the cat, "I have a good sense of direction."

The next morning, the newspaper was delivered as usual. On the front page was the story of the fire and on the second page was the picture of the news van with the cat sitting atop it. At the news office, Ted, the editor of WCAT News, was very surprised. "West, Candid, could you step into my office, please."

"Here it comes," Dave sighed.

"Don't worry about it," whispered Samantha.

Ted was sitting at his desk when the pair walked into the office. He was a tall, middle-aged man of average build, with brown hair and eyes and a trimmed mustache. He served as both assignment and managing editor in the newsroom, coordinating not only the news stories and personnel who covered them but also representing the news staff whenever the network's CEO chanced to call a meeting of the television station departments. Despite the small chain of command and the corresponding size of the town of Faunaville, where they were based, their station was the headquarters of the WCAT network and staunchly free of any outside influence on their reporting - a testament to Ted's excellent management of the newsroom.

"I always hoped I would be the first to know whenever our station got a mascot. When will I meet this lucky cat?" he said half-jokingly.

"Ted, I'm so sorry. We were really into our story and we didn't notice Geronimo had climbed on top of the van," Samantha explained.

"He even ate our lunch," Dave added.

"What was he doing in the news truck, to begin with?" Ted asked.

"Apparently, he snuck in. It won't happen again; I've spoken to him about it," Samantha replied.

"Well, there's no harm done. The station has actually gotten calls from the public saying the whole thing was a sweet idea. Let's call it an interesting situation, and let it go," Ted said. "I have a new assignment for you two."

Both Samantha and Dave seemed to brighten up. "Great! What's the story?" Dave asked.

"Wildlife conference," their editor quickly explained. "The wire service just sent us a report from the mainland, saying it's going to be taking place the day after tomorrow in Vaharis. It's being organized by the governor of Nortenya to announce the recovery of certain threatened animal species. I'd like for both of you to travel to the mainland to cover this."

"We'll be there," Samantha quickly replied.

"Great. In that case, the two of you will be boarding a charter flight tomorrow, heading for the mainland. Unless something else comes up, that will be the week's top story. There’s talk the governor might soon be running for parliament; a lot of high-ranking politicos see him as a good candidate for prime minister."

Just then, the phone rang; as Ted lifted the receiver, he glanced at the pair. "Ok. You have your mission. Pick up the tickets at the airport before departure. Good luck."

Samantha and Dave walked out of the office as Ted resumed the phone conversation. "We'd better hurry home and pack," said Samantha.

While Dave took the steering wheel, Samantha dialed her sister Leandra on her cell phone. Leandra and Laurence, her husband, were two local veterinarians. Samantha and her sister were close and would often talk; sometimes she even dropped by their practice to say hello.

"Hello, Lee...it's Sam."

"Hi Samantha! What's happening?" said the voice cheerily on the other end.

"Just to say hi...and to ask you to cat-sit."

"Let me guess. You've got an assignment off the island," Leandra deduced matter-of-factly.

"You know me so well," chuckled Samantha.

"No problem with the kitty sitting, Sam. When will you bring the gang over?"

"Tonight. Later, ok?"

"Wow, so soon?"

"Yep. I'm leaving tomorrow. Sorry about the short notice, I just found out today, myself."

"That's ok, but bring over some cat food, because if I remember correctly, Geronimo can be picky about eating, sometimes."

"Sure," answered Samantha, "See you later."

When they arrived home, Tifarah, Butch and Geronimo were all sitting around their dishes staring at them.

A collective hiss rose up when Samantha and Dave noticed, and Tifarah said, "Samantha, I know you lead a busy schedule, but next time please just leave the food bowls full when you know you'll be back late."

"Sorry Tif, I didn't know I would be held up. As it turns out, I'm going on a business trip and all you guys will have to stay with Leandra and Laurence for a few days." As she said this, she poured some dry cat food into their dishes and while the cats attacked the food, she turned to face Dave. "Dave...what do you want to do about dinner?"

"Let's just order a pizza," he answered.

"So where's this trip taking you guys?" It was Geronimo, who had lifted his head up from the food dish and was staring at them with an oddly eager look in his blue eyes.

"Vaharis," Samantha replied.

Geronimo instantly leaped to his paws, eyes shining. "The mainland! Me-ow, now that sounds cool! Can I come with you? Purrrlease?"

"Geronimo..." Samantha started.

"I've always wanted to see the mainland," Geronimo continued obliviously. "Big skyscrapers, tons of people, hot-dog vendors..."

"No." said Samantha.

"But..."

"No. That's final. Geronimo, we can't bring you along!"

"Why not?" The lynx-point feline lashed his striped gray tail. Before either Samantha or Dave could respond, he meowed: "Leandra and Laurence bring their cats to work, sometimes."

"They're vets, we're journalists," Dave said.

"That's no excuse."

"Yes it is," Samantha replied. "How can we be out chasing a story if we have to worry about what you're up to?"

Geronimo flattened his ears, but said nothing.

Samantha glanced at Dave. "I'm going to call the pizzeria."

When the two had left the room, Geronimo turned to see Tifarah and Butch staring at him, stunned.

"Why on earth would you want to go to the mainland?" Tifarah hissed.

Geronimo flexed his claws in frustration. "I want to travel! Everyone else has adventures - why can't I?"

"You'll have plenty of time to prowl around when you get older; at any rate, we shouldn't leave the island," Butch meowed. "I've heard tales about the mainland...Many of the humans over there don't respect critters like they do here."

"Listen to your father." mewed Tifarah. "Here in Faunaville...on all of Tropical Island...people are nice. Off the island, not everyone is."

"I don't care. I want to feel the energy of the big city, the excitement of discovery, the thrill of danger..."

"Geronimo..."

"Like our humans! They're always going places and having adventures...one day they're in town at the hustle and bustle of a cat show, the next - wham! They're half-way across the globe in some war-torn country trying to shoot a live report in the midst of peril!"

As if accentuating his words, he took a gigantic leap in the air and attacked a cat toy nearby. The bell inside the tiny green ball jingled incoherently as he let out a fierce growl.

The older cats glanced at one another, eyes narrowed.

As Geronimo tussled with the toy, Butch spoke to Tifarah. "Don't worry. It's a phase tomcats go through. Once he matures a bit more, he'll realize that it’s not all fun and games out there."

"I hope you're right," answered Tifarah.

Chapter 2 - Stowaway

A rooster crowed somewhere in the distance, heralding the morning.

Tifarah, Butch and Geronimo had been dropped off at Leandra's the night before; and were just leaving the house to go on their morning prowls.

Leandra and Laurence had already left for work and their cats, as well as the visiting felines, were eager to go outdoors. All the cats were dispersing through the cat door and although Tifarah and Butch had taken a right turn, Geronimo took a left. Butch called out to him. "Ger...where are you off to?"

"Not far" answered Geronimo, "I thought I'd prowl around our home base. We'll only be at Leandra's for a couple of weeks and I want to keep up the prowl schedule."

Butch looked at his son proudly. Tifarah said "Be careful. Traffic is busy this time of the morning."

Geronimo bounded off and without looking back answered, "Don't worry."

Tifarah watched as he ran off and thought to herself, I always worry.

About ten minutes later, Geronimo had arrived at his home. He noticed that the window was open where the bedroom was located. "Well...it looks like the humans haven't left on their trip yet. I'll go have a look." Having said that, he took a flying leap, landed right on the window sill and peeked in.

Samantha and Dave were hurrying around trying to get some last-minute packing done, so they didn't notice as the cat snuck into the bedroom and hid under the bed.

"Dave...Have you packed extra camera film? You know sometimes it's hard to find the right kind for our cameras." Samantha's voice was coming from the closet. She was busy retrieving something and emerged with a triumphant look on her face and holding a clothes-hanger on which a peacoat was hung. "Finally!" she exclaimed. "I never get a chance to wear this coat here on the island because it's for colder weather."

Dave walked into the room holding a couple of ties. "I already packed the camera film...I think we've got everything we need."

Dave dropped the ties in his knapsack, zipped it shut and turned to Samantha, "Have I told you today how much I love you?"

Samantha smiled and wrapped her arms around him in a big hug. "Say the words... I never tire of hearing them."

"I love you" answered Dave.

Samantha kissed him and whispered in his ear, "I love you too."

During this time, Geronimo had been analyzing the situation from beneath the bed. He thought to himself, Why not get into one of the bags and go on a real adventure? After all, my Dad has told me many escapades he had when he was a feral cat...He was just a little older than I am...I'll probably be back in time for dinner...

While the humans were still distracted with each other, Geronimo jumped onto the bed and into the duffel bag that was wide open next to the knapsack. It was full of camera equipment and he squeezed into a corner of it. When Dave and Samantha parted from each other she said, "Dave, you forgot your pajamas... here, throw them in the duffel bag. There's still room in there." She handed them over and he answered, "I don't think I'll be needing them much..."

"Dave...we'll be working all day long."

"But our nights will be free..." he winked at her.

Samantha winked back and laughed. "While you're at it, throw in these scarves too, my bags are full already."

Dave took the pajamas and scarves, rolled them into a ball and pitched them into the duffel bag.

The clothing landed right over Geronimo. The cat curled up for a nap and Dave zipped up the bag completely clueless to his little passenger.

A taxicab was waiting for them in front of the house. "Where to?" the driver asked as they stepped out onto the sidewalk.

"Tropical Island International Airport," Samantha replied while Dave locked the front gate. She opened the door to the back seat of the taxi as Dave appeared beside her. He placed the duffel bag and knapsack inside.

Geronimo was flattened as Samantha put her legs up on the duffel bag. He growled.

"What was that?" she asked.

Dave shrugged.

The drive to the airport was swift, and once there, boarding was equally quick. A Pomeranian in a pet carrier started yapping ferociously as Samantha and Dave passed by.

"I'm sorry, I don't know what got into her," the dog's owner apologized.

"That's all right," Samantha replied.

A hiss came from the duffel bag as they left the canine behind, but neither the reporter nor her cameraman paid much attention as they hurried from check-in into Gate 5E.

After showing their press passes and tickets to the stewardess at this point, they went out onto the airfield and walked up the towering steps leading from the ground to the doorway of the waiting charter flight. The duffel bag was placed on the carry-on shelf above their seats and the plane began coursing along the runway. When at last it was airborne, the pair settled in for the long trip to Vaharis.

The nation of Sarrilla was a world power, of which Tropical Island was a commonwealth. Vaharis, the capital of the Nortenya region, was Sarrilla's largest northern city and was located on the outer edges of the Arctic Circle; it could only be reached by train. The Nortenya airport, hence, doubled as a train station and had become the region's main transportation center.

When the reporters' airplane landed in Nortenya, they waited for about 10 minutes before the train pulled into the station and were again en route to Vaharis. The train ride was quiet and scenic, and an hour later they disembarked.

Before stepping outside, the TV news crew changed into clothes suitable for the frozen climate. Samantha retrieved the tawny peacoat that she had packed - it was wool, with an inside lining of rabbit fur that made it the warmest coat she had.

"I can't wait until we can cover that story tomorrow." Samantha said enthusiastically, "Hopefully we can get the governor to say a couple of good sound bites..."

"...and we’ll get a few good camera shots, too," Dave responded with a grin. "I'm hungry - want to go eat somewhere?"

"Once we're settled at the lodge, I'll be able to relax and think about eating. I want some time to prepare for tomorrow's event." Samantha said, settling a matching fedora hat on her head.

"We should call our editor then," Dave considered.

They approached a public phone and Samantha dialed the number. When she got Ted on the other line, he gave further instructions:

"You ought to rest for the remainder of the day - tomorrow you'll head over to the Convention Center, where they'll be holding the conference. I've informed the editor of WCAT's Vaharis Bureau that you guys will be hanging out with them and working out of their office for a while. His name is Devon Gao, we've known each other since college. He told me he would send a car to pick you guys up when you arrived at the train station, so keep your eyes open for a WCAT news van."

"Sounds good" said Samantha.

"Call me periodically and keep me up to date."

"Ok, Ted, will do."

As she finished the telephone call, she heard a car horn at the curb and turned to look. Through the phone booth's glass partitions she noticed one of their network's large white satellite vans with the WCAT logo across its side.

"Samantha, Dave! Nice to see the two of you again!" It was the driver, a man about Dave's age but of a slimmer build, with brown hair and hazel eyes.

"Todd Truitt," Samantha greeted the driver as she joined Dave at the sidewalk edge. "Nice to see you too. How's your wife?"

"She's fine; she loved the trip to Tropical Island and she made me promise that the next time I have to do a report from there, I bring her along" Todd said, opening the door. "By the way, Gao told me to pick you two up and take you to the TV station. He said you can use the news van while you're in Vaharis, since that way you won't have to rent a car."

"Yes, I know. Ted told us" Samantha responded as she and Dave got into the car.

The WCAT affiliate in Vaharis was only two blocks away from the train station, and the newsroom was located on the fifth floor. The facade of the building was different than the Faunaville station. Pressed against the adjoining skyscrapers with only alleyways to divide them, it stood in contrast with the wide, mossy grass fields that surrounded the headquarters. On Tropical Island, the station's news helicopter would land in the back field, the broadcast transmitter was beside the building, and the vast satellite antennas were placed overlooking the clear lake in front of the building and its parking lot. Here, the heliport was atop the building, along with the antennas and transmitter, and the parking space for the cars was underground, accessible by a slope leading from the street into the basement.

The elevator brought them up onto the fifth floor. For any difference the outside might have had, they found the building inside to be the image of the headquarters' offices. Crossing a small, carpeted hallway, they entered a room without a door, with large windows on either side of the entryway - it was labeled 'Newsroom' on the right. It was the picturesque newsroom; as bright and active as the one in Faunaville, with the tapping of keyboards mingling with the rings of telephones, and an atmosphere imbued with unceasing, dedicated energy. Lining the wall was a map of the world and a line of clocks, each set to a different time zone; throughout the office were televisions to monitor both WCAT's and competitors' channels, and to the far end of the newsroom was the studio, open for easy access so that one could simply dash to it to broadcast a breaking news bulletin. Opposite this was the editor's office; the door was marked: Devon Gao.

Devon Gao was about Ted's age, of Asian descent with black hair and brown eyes. He glanced up from his desk as the reporters walked into the newsroom and gestured to them to come over.

As the pair walked into his office, Gao got up and smiling, reached out to shake their hands. "Welcome to our newsroom. Ted speaks highly of you two. Whatever you need, my door is open."

"Thanks, Mr. Gao" said Samantha.

After spending an hour at the newsroom, Samantha and Dave were given keys to a news van and told they could use it throughout their stay in town. They said goodbye and drove to the lodge where they would be living while doing their report.

Nestled in Hammond Forest, the lodge was the seeming antithesis of Vaharis' majestic skyscrapers; yet the city and the wooded area were separated only by aptly-named Whirlpool River.

After checking in, they were given directions that led to a small cabin surrounded by pine woodland. To the left was a white glow that was a frozen lake; beyond that were more pines, but the land seemed to drop off at some point where one could just make out, far behind the trees, a white expanse of barren snow. The reporters had been given the choice of staying at the high-rise hotel in the center of the city, but had opted to stay in the forest area so that they could have a better opportunity of photographing wildlife.

Samantha was delighted with the cottage. "Look how cute!" she said, "It looks like something out of a..."

Dave, dragging the duffel bag out of the back of the news van, squinted. "Well, it's bigger than the hut we got on the African savannah..."

"Very cozy" Samantha added.

"I bet we'll get lots of great pictures out here" Dave said.

The cabin inside was little, but comfortable. The floor and walls were all of a light-tan wood, and the rest of the cabin was decorated in light-green. Upon entering, one was greeted by a large living room area with a sofa, two armchairs and a coffee table. A flight of steps was to the left of the front door. The steps were made of small logs cut sideways and polished to smooth away all the sharp sides. Beyond the living room, was a kitchenette complete with stove, refrigerator, counter and cabinets. A circular wood table with four chairs was in the center and a telephone hung on the wall near it. The second floor was where the bedroom was. It too, was dressed in light-green, with a matching rug laid out on the floor; a night table with a telephone extension was beside the bed. A window was on one side of the bed and a chest of drawers was on the other. The bathroom was also up here. The cabin had modern heating and cooling throughout.

"It is cozy," Dave said, placing the duffel bag on the bed.

"The view outside is great, too," said Samantha, putting her bags next to the duffel bag.

Dave was glancing out the window. "Wouldn't it be great to get a few shots of the forest scenery, right now?"

Samantha appeared interested. "That's not a bad idea!"

Dave reached over and unzipped the duffel bag, retrieving his camera and her microphone without even so much as a second glance inside. "You know," Samantha was saying as Dave walked over and handed her the microphone, "this is rather romantic. We're out in the forest...we have the place all to ourselves..."

"Just the two of us," Dave whispered as he put his arms around her.

"Hi guys!" Geronimo broke in, peeking out of the duffel bag.

There was shocked silence for a moment...then...

"Geronimo!"

"I don't believe it," was the only thing Samantha could say.

Geronimo leaped to the window. "Are we in Vaharis?" His eyes were shining, his ears were pricked, his tail held straight up; the picture of feline excitement.

"Wait a second..." Dave still looked bewildered. "You traveled all the way from the Caribbean to the Arctic...in our camera equipment?"

Geronimo turned back to look at his stunned humans. "Nice! Is that halfway around the world?"

"Why did you do this, Geronimo?" Samantha asked, astonished.

"To travel! See the world!" Geronimo caterwauled happily.

There was another pause as the TV news crew and the cat merely stared at each other; at last, Geronimo broke the silence.

"So...aren't you glad to see me?"

Samantha and Dave glanced at one another but said nothing.

"Oh, come on," Geronimo persisted. "I'm like your feline sidekick!"

Samantha seemed at a loss for words, and Dave tried to explain..."Geronimo...let me put it this way. In filming a TV news story you only need two things. Audio..." - he motioned towards Samantha - "and Video" - he motioned towards himself.

"Right," Geronimo interrupted. "And a kitty..."

"No...wait. Let me start over..."

Samantha broke in at this point. "Geronimo...we love you, but you aren't supposed to be here."

The cat's ears flattened. "Why not?"

"We told you not to come." Samantha scolded. "Your being here is a hassle for us. How can we focus on our work while worrying about you?"

"There's no need to worry about me," Geronimo insisted.

Samantha sighed. "All right. You got to travel. But now you're going back to Tropical Island."

"Damn. Shit!" the cat hissed.

"We're heading out now; we'll get you some cat food and a litter box for the day or so you'll be here." Samantha said. "After that, you're getting on the next plane back to the island." Her gaze softened when she saw his whiskers droop. "Geronimo, I'm sorry, but we're here on an assignment, not a vacation. This isn't Faunaville, where pets are welcome everywhere."

The cat stared into her eyes.

"Listen, cat...I know what you're trying to do. The 'poor kitty' look is not going to work."

The cat continued to stare, his eyes widening.

Samantha stared back. The cat's whiskers twitched.

Dave started counting. "One, two, three..."

"All right, you win" Samantha said. "You can stay, but only if you don't prowl around very far outside. We don't know this area."

She turned around and found a smiling Dave. "He's perfecting his 'kitty look'. It only took him three seconds to talk you into his idea" he said.

"Oh well" she answered. "We won't be in this town very long, anyway."

The couple put their things away and turned to leave.

"Geronimo, we'll be back soon with your supper" said Samantha as she and Dave walked out the door. As soon as they got in the car, she said, "I'm rather tired from the trip. When we get back, I just want to shower and go to bed."

"I agree" answered Dave, "We can call your sister tomorrow and tell her Geronimo is with us."

Inside the cabin, the cat had gone downstairs and leapt up to the window, settling down to scan the scene. He tucked his paws under himself and crouched into a furry lump. Outside, everything was brown except for the evergreen trees and some patches of snow, here and there. Geronimo was falling asleep, when movement outside caught his eye. His ears picked up a faint sound and he fixed his gaze at some holly bushes a few yards away. His cat senses told him there was something out there.

As he stared at the bushes, out emerged two white furred creatures.

Chapter 3 - The Escape

Geronimo had never seen anything quite like these animals - they were about his size, yet looked like fluffy white canines of some sort. They had small paws, big amber eyes, and beautiful bushy tails. One was male, the other female, that much Geronimo could ascertain; but the young tomcat was perplexed as to their species. They look like foxes, he thought, but their fur is white!

The two critters were padding along happily - clearly heading somewhere - when the male noticed Geronimo in the window. He stopped suddenly, ears pricked. Geronimo sat up curiously.

Just then, the male critter leapt up to the window, sniffing at the glass. He said something, but Geronimo couldn't hear him.

Geronimo meowed.

The critter paced on the windowsill outside with his head down and tail twitching. Again he yapped something at Geronimo.

"I can't hear you," said Geronimo, poking at the glass with a paw.

The critters outside couldn't hear the cat either, and after a few tries of communicating to no avail, the female said something to her mate, who hopped down from the windowsill. The two, then scampered off into the woods. Geronimo sighed in disappointment as he watched them leave.

"Hey, glad you're back!" Geronimo purred when his humans returned later that evening. "I saw something really interesting outside..."

Samantha scooped the cat up in her arms without paying much attention. "We got you some food - and a litter box. You didn't do anything while we were out of the house, did you?"

"No...where's the food?" Geronimo licked his lips.

Samantha carried the cat up to the second floor, where Dave had set up the litter box in an inconspicuous corner of the bathroom. She plopped the cat down in the sand and ran his paws through the gravel. "This is where you go."

"Sure, sure," Geronimo meowed, hopping out. "Listen, I saw two critters outside I've never seen before."

"Lots of animals are distinctly northern, just like lots of others are distinctly tropical" Dave reminded him.

"They looked like fluffy white puffs with big eyes." Geronimo purred. "They came right up to the window, and..."

"Oh, it could have been anything," interrupted Samantha. "Many critters here have white fur coats because it helps them camouflage in the snow. Anyway, I got you some sardines."

"Yay, sardines!" yowled Geronimo, running ahead of Samantha to the kitchenette downstairs, and thus ending the conversation on white furred critters.

The next day was foggy with the conference taking place that evening at six. Until then, Samantha and Dave had the day to themselves.

They were having breakfast when the telephone rang.

Samantha answered, "Hello?"

"Hi, sis." It was Leandra.

"Lee, I was just going to call you. What's up?"

"Well..." said Leandra, her voice tense, "I hate to worry you for no reason, but Geronimo is lost."

"I know...he's with us."

"...What? How'd that happen?"

"He hid in our luggage." Samantha explained, squinting at Geronimo as he hopped onto her chair and tried to sniff the bacon on her plate. "We discovered him when we were already at the lodge."

"Are you going to ship him back?" said Leandra.

"Nah." answered Samantha, as she noticed Dave waving the cat away from the breakfast plate and feeding him a piece of bacon. "He might as well stay with us, we'll only be away a couple of days. Tell Tifarah for me, will you? I don't want her to worry" she added.

"Ok...keep in touch."

"Thanks Lee; bye."

As Leandra hung up the telephone, she turned to see four pairs of cat eyes staring at her. Laurence and Leandra's own pets - Lilith the black cat and Tom the orange tabby - were sitting atop the kitchen table with a curious look in their eyes. Butch was curled up on a chair, relaxed, while an extremely worried Tifarah was below the table.

"Tifarah," said Leandra somewhat hesitantly, "I have good news and bad news..." When the Siamese flicked an ear, she went on, "The good news is, we know where Geronimo is."

Tifarah leapt to her paws. "Thank God! Where is he?!"

"The bad news is...he's on the mainland." Leandra finished.

Tifarah switched from relief to dismay. "What?! What on earth is he doing over there?!"

"That's my boy," Butch meowed proudly. "Out there spreading his genes."

"My kitten!" Tifarah wailed.

"He's not a little kitten anymore, Tif," said Butch. "He's growing."

"So how did he get over there?" inquired a very interested Tom.

"It seems he was a luggage stowaway," Leandra explained.

"That is a brilliant idea," meowed Lilith. "How come we never thought of something like that, Tom?"

"Because we never considered leaving this town, Lil" answered her mate.

"Yeah. That's true. Why would we?" Lilith replied thoughtfully.

Tifarah yowled. "I sure hope he doesn't wander very far from the den!"

A hiss arose from Butch's corner. "What's the point of it all, then?" he said. "If you're gonna do something, do it right. He's supposed to venture out and prowl new turf, every now and then."

"Butch" said Leandra, "Keep in mind that Geronimo is in an unknown area."

At this point, Laurence walked into the room, followed by Lilith and Tom's three kittens - a female and two males.

Laurence said, "What's this I hear about Geronimo? A stowaway?"

"Yep," replied Leandra. "He hid in my sister's luggage."

"When can we do that?" squeaked the kittens.

"Never," Lilith meowed. "You stay put with whatever human feeds and cares for you. That's how you stay safe."

Tom spoke up and said, "Sometimes a tomcat has to venture far and explore new territory..."

Lilith hissed at him and he added hurriedly, "...However, I think stowing away is a bit much."

The three kittens looked from parent to parent and then at each other. "I guess that means we'll have to wait 'till we're a bit older to find out," relented one of the boy kittens.

Geronimo was feeling a little frustrated. Samantha and Dave had spent most of the day indoors, planning for the story they were going to cover that evening and to let the cat out to prowl was out of the question for them.

"Ger looks really pissed." Dave said. "He's sitting in the window downstairs with flat ears."

"I know he must feel annoyed," Samantha replied, looking in the bathroom mirror and putting on pearl earrings. "We always let him outside in Faunaville, but we're in the middle of a forest in an unfamiliar place. He's not even supposed to be here." Satisfied with the way she looked, Samantha grabbed her gloves and walked quickly to the stairs. "Ready, honey?"

"Yes ma'am," her cameraman smiled.

They hurried downstairs where Samantha and Dave found their microphone and camera; Geronimo became alert and leapt off the windowsill. "Oh, yeah! We're off on a mission! Going to pester people at that convention-thingy!"

"Hold it, Ger...what do you mean we?" Samantha squinted at him. "Dave and I are going to cover this story. You will remain here."

"I wouldn't be a problem for you." Geronimo entwined himself around her legs, purring. "I'd just sit up high somewhere being real quiet and ambush the waiter when he comes by with seafood."

"That's exactly what we don't want," Samantha informed him dryly.

"It would be great news! That's what you're after, right? CAT ATTACK. Think about the possibilities!"

"Ok, first off, we don't create news to report it, we just report what's already happening." Dave explained. "Secondly, we don't want a repeat of your escapade that day we were covering the apartment fire. Our editor won't be too happy with that."

"Shit, man - come on!" Geronimo was now fluffed up. "You don't expect to keep me cooped up in this tiny cabin forever!"

"As long as you're here, yes." Samantha said.

Geronimo bared his fangs in a hiss.

Samantha and Dave both appeared amused. "Well," said Samantha, "We'll be back in a couple of hours. We're dropping by the news office first, then we'll head to the conference. Try to stay out of trouble."

"I promise nothing," Geronimo meowed.

Without a word in response, the two stepped outside, shutting the door behind them. Annoyed, the cat's innate curiosity finally motivated him to leap back atop the windowsill. From his post there, he watched his humans get into the car, then back out onto the road and drive off.

Frustration was swept away with longing. He wanted to go with them and see what was happening in the city. The tomcat stood up on his hind legs to get a better look outside, wistfully pressing his forepaws on the glass...

Just then, the window jerked open.

Geronimo stared down in surprise. The window apparently had been left unlatched by the previous tenants, and with Geronimo having leant against the window pane, it had opened in the most opportune manner. Turning to look outside again, the cat let out a sly purr; he pushed against the glass with all his strength - the window completely opened, and he toppled out with a meow.

Freezing arctic air instantly blasted him, and instinctually he fluffed up his fur. However, that did little to stop him as he raced off in the direction the car had gone, determined to catch up to his humans. He ran confidently until he reached a large thoroughfare, surrounded by forest and bordered on one side by a railroad line. Old, brittle snow was piled on each side of the street, and cars were zooming past.

Which way could they have gone?

Geronimo turned around, planning to head back to the cabin, but suddenly realized that he had no idea where that was, either. He had run without noticing the territory and now did not know how to get back.

Geronimo looked up into the milky-white sky. Just great. My humans are lost, and the den was misplaced. Now what?

As if in silent answer, snow began to fall.

Chapter 4 - Governor of the Nortenya region

Vaharis was the capital of the Nortenya region. It was a vibrant metropolis as rich in culture as it was in status. This was the city of progress, of activity, and the people who traversed the sidewalks were rushed and alert, their quickness suggesting a matter of great importance beckoned them. The city itself held an energy of enticing power and the sense that something, somewhere was happening, amidst its infinitely towering buildings which created steel, concrete canyons filled with noisily complaining automobiles.

Samantha West and Dave Candid had arrived at the Convention Center, and were met at the entrance by security.

"Good evening sir, miss - may I see your passes, please?"

Both retrieved their press cards. "Right this way," said the guard, escorting them inside.

The room was wide and elegant. Lighting seemed to lend a form of twilight to the ambience; the carpeting was of a red color, and most of the decor - including the stage and round dining tables - were a shiny black, creating an exotic look. An overhead projector was on standby for the event, and a white cloth screen was hung for this use; thick red curtains fringed with gold tassels draped on either side of it. There were a large number of people in the conference hall, dressed in business attire, and the majority were seated at the tables, talking amongst themselves.

Samantha and Dave were shown to the press area. There were tables assigned to each media entity that had declared their intention to attend. Once at the WCAT table, the two set up their camera and recording devices and sat down. Dinner was to be served first; and then the speakers would take the podium and speak in turn.

More people filtered into the room and soon every table, including the ones designated for the journalists, were filled.

The waiters embarked on the difficult task of delivering meals to the guests and making sure that everyone was satisfied. Before long, the tables were cleared of the dishes and tension filled the air with expectations.

A man in a grey suit rose from his seat and approached the podium on the stage. This was the mayor of Vaharis, who began his introductory speech. He spoke for half an hour, mostly about the wildlife and the significant roles they had played in the history of the region, as well as emphasizing the importance of conservation.

Samantha and Dave listened as the Vaharis mayor finished his speech. While Dave focused the camera on him, Samantha's eyes drifted from the stage to scan the audience, and she began a mental selection of potential interviewees. Most of the people here were either political supporters, wildlife experts, or representatives of wildlife conservation groups. One person in particular stood out, wearing the uniform of a park ranger. Him. He looks like a reliable source.

"Hello!" A mew broke into her thoughts. Glancing down, Samantha saw a beautiful longhaired cat staring up at her. It was black and white with a lavender collar studded with amethysts. "You like cats! I can tell."

"Hi kitty," the television reporter smiled, bending down to pet her. "Where's your human?"

Before the cat had a chance to respond, the mayor announced:

"...I'd like to welcome Victor Ulrich, Governor of the Nortenya region!"

Applause resonated through the auditorium, and when Samantha glanced up, the tuxedo cat quickly scampered off.

The governor was middle-aged, with pale blue eyes and auburn hair streaked with white. He had the confident stride of an experienced politician, a man whose charisma and connections had brought him into office. Stepping up onto the stage, he let the applause quiet before speaking.

"Thank you all for coming. I stand here tonight with not just an announcement, but a tale of courage. A tale of heartwarming success set in the most unexpected and harshest of places." The governor clicked a button on the remote control, and the overhead projector displayed an image of glaciers and frozen tundra. As he spoke, he periodically changed the picture. "The Arctic Circle, long regarded as a land both beautiful and vicious. Explorers told of its bountiful wildlife...but where we today see nature's beauty, they saw lucrative opportunity. The land was ravaged, its animals slaughtered. The effects of those careless acts nearly destroyed our northern wildlife. For some - such as the great auk - it was too late. For others - like the mighty polar bear, the symbol of the Arctic - the fight had begun. But among these creatures, one stands out as the picture of triumph, of victory against impossible odds..."

Ulrich clicked the button again, and the image changed to that of a fluffy white canine. "The arctic fox. Known by the scientific community as Alopex Lagopus, this small, endearing animal was the target of trappers who ruthlessly hunted it for its valuable winter fur. At last, with only 1,500 remaining in the wild, it was given protection as an endangered species."

He paused, letting his words settle on the hushed audience, then once again changed the picture on the screen to a line graph.

"Today, our wildlife is thriving!" he announced. "Thanks to the legislation which I enacted to protect them, the once-dwindling arctic fox now numbers more than 150,000 - and is once more abundant and flourishing on the tundra!"

During all this time, Samantha was listening to the speech, but she was also scanning the audience for their reactions. Her eyes caught sight of the ranger, who was shaking his head disapprovingly. He seems a bit upset by what the governor is saying, Samantha thought. She scribbled a reminder of it in her notepad.

Onstage, Governor Ulrich was finishing his speech. "With this wonderful accomplishment, I have begun proceedings to get the arctic fox delisted, to officially crown it a wildlife success story!"

The crowd burst into applause. Samantha glanced back at the ranger and noticed that he was not clapping. This intrigued Samantha, who instantly sensed a story. That's it. I have to interview the guy.

"Sam, I recognize that gleam in your eyes." Dave's knowing voice broke into her thoughts. "What are you up to?"

"Dave...You see that wildlife ranger over there?" asked Samantha.

"Yeah. He doesn't seem too thrilled with the governor's speech."

"Exactly" she said. "Doesn't regional government typically discuss delisting of wildlife with the rangers? I mean...you would think that he would be in agreement with this announcement."

"You're right about that. It seems a little weird," answered Dave.

The speech was finished and the event decidedly over, so the governor was off the stage and surrounded by various members of the media, clamoring for their turn at an interview. Samantha, of course, headed instead towards the park ranger.

"Samantha..." Dave called out behind her. "Sam...I think we're headed in the wrong direction. The governor is to the right of us."

"Yep. I know it," she answered. "The ranger is the first person I want to interview. The governor will be around a while longer, what with all the other reporters trying to get a story. I want to know why anyone would be upset with the news."

The ranger was standing up to leave when they arrived at his table. He was a tall, black man, who seemed a bit surprised to see the TV news crew's quick appearance.

"Hi - I'm Samantha West from WCAT 8 News - my photographer, Dave Candid," the reporter introduced herself and her companion. "We'd like to interview you for our evening broadcast... What are your views on Governor Ulrich's announcement?"

The ranger sighed. "Well, it would be great...any improvement in arctic fox numbers would be spectacular... But I've noticed a population decline, not a rebound."

"A decline?"

"Yes. Fox tracks are becoming even rarer than before, there aren't many traces of the animals anywhere..."

"What do you think is the cause?"

"I have no idea. The fox's usual prey - lemmings - haven't been very abundant recently, and the fox population tends to rise and fall with the lemmings, but never this much. It can't be the lemmings. I thought that it might be a disease, but the few foxes I do see look healthy enough - though they're all skittish lately."

"Did the governor ever contact you before his announcement?"

"No... When I learned about it, I tried to contact his office, but each time my calls went unanswered. Frankly, I didn't think he would go so far as to try to delist the species," the ranger said.

"What's your name, sir?" asked Samantha, "...and may we quote you?"

"Jovan Conway," answered the ranger, "Yes, you may quote me; perhaps that will prompt Ulrich to call me and discuss the issue."

Samantha handed him a card. "Ranger Conway, if you have anything further you'd like to add, or if the governor ever calls you...please call us."

"Sure," he replied.

As Conway left, Samantha and Dave walked over to where Governor Ulrich was responding to questions. "...Certainly," they heard him saying, "but I championed the legislation which helped the wildlife return."

Samantha broke in, "Governor, we just spoke with one of the rangers who says that the arctic fox population is actually declining. Do you have anything you'd like to comment on that?"

Ulrich focused a steely, icy glare on the reporter. "No comment," he replied coldly.

If there was one person who couldn't be intimidated, it was Samantha. In his hostility she saw a secret and in that secret, she saw a story. Her green eyes gleamed like a cat who had cornered prey, and she persisted, "So you don't deny that..."

"Anything else you need to know," he interrupted brusquely, "you'll find in my speech...Thank you, ladies and gentlemen."

At this point, Ulrich turned around and left, surrounded by body guards. The reporters dispersed, some of them comparing notes of the speech and interview.

Samantha was deep in thought as she watched the governor walk away.

"He seemed pissed off with that question."

Upon hearing her cameraman's remark, Samantha turned to look at him. "Yeah...I wonder why? I get the feeling that there's more to this man than meets the eye. He's hiding something; I can sense it."

"Well...I guess this is a wrap," Dave said as he turned to go.

"Know what?" said Samantha "I'd like to add the final words of the report with a shot on the outside of the building"

The reporter and her cameraman gathered their gear and headed out the door.

Meanwhile, within the building's back quarters; there was a VIP lounge where only members were allowed. The governor's wife, Mabel, was seated at a small round mahogany table having tea. On her lap was a beautiful, black and white longhaired cat with green eyes and an elegant lavender collar.

The lady was stroking the cat's fur and speaking to it.

"How's my darling Roxanne? Do you want more caviar?"

The cat purred in contentment and replied, "Non. Je suis content...happy. Merci, Madame."

Mabel Ulrich was a quiet woman of about 35. She had dark brown hair which she typically wore in a bun; and eyes that sparkled when she laughed.

Laughter for Mabel was a rarity, because her marriage to the governor was not a very happy one. Lately, he had not been very attentive to her and she felt unwanted. Disappointment often showed on her face. The cat sensed this and looked up into her grey blue eyes.

The cat spoke. "Madame, what is it? Are you well?"

"Yes, cherie...I'm fine." she answered.

Mabel had no children, although she had tried to coax her husband into parenthood, unsuccessfully. At that moment, Governor Ulrich stepped into the room and went directly to her table.

"Hello, darling" she said.

"Hello, Mabel, dear" Ulrich bent down and kissed her cheek, avoiding her lips.

The lady looked down at the cat, to hide her tears.

"Are you ready to go?" he asked.

"Yes," she answered.

The wind outside was sharply cold and it was snowing; the grey skies were a reflection of Mabel's despondent feelings. The governor and his wife stepped outside to a waiting limousine, where the chauffeur opened the door for them. Just then, Ulrich noticed a man approaching.

"Get in," Ulrich ordered Mabel.

Without a word she obeyed, though Roxanne the cat hissed as he shut the door.

The man halted only a small distance from them. The body guards instantly jumped to send him on his way, but Ulrich coolly gestured for them to stay back.

"Interesting speech, governor."

"You know as well as I, that we can't be seen together in public." Ulrich's voice was taut. "We'll keep in touch."

Across the street, fate had given the camera a direct, unplanned view of the limousine; the harsh shine of klieg lights glittered in the nighttime darkness and outlined in the glow, was the slender figure of the television reporter...

"...Not everyone is happy with the governor's announcement. Park ranger Jovan Conway told us he's seen a decline in the arctic fox population. Conway says the governor's office never contacted rangers before the announcement and that calls he made have gone unanswered. When we asked Ulrich, he declined to comment. Reporting from Vaharis, Nortenya, I'm Samantha West for WCAT 8 News."

As Samantha wrapped up her report, Dave glanced over and saw the Governor's black limousine drive off. "Looks like Ulrich came out in the background talking with someone."

"Did you see who it was?" asked an interested Samantha.

"No, but I suppose it was one of his bodyguards," answered Dave.

"Well, it's getting late," she said. "We'd better get back to the cabin before Geronimo goes shredding something, but first we need to drop by the newsroom. The wind's starting to pick up and it's snowing a lot more now."

The pair packed up all the gear into the news van. They drove to WCAT's Vaharis bureau, and as they walked into the newsroom, Dave said, "I'm going to the viewing room to make a copy of the tape."

"Sure, Dave" Samantha replied, as she sat down at the desk. "I'll place a phone-call back to the island; remember Ted told us to call him after the conference?"

"Yeah, that's right."

Dave went off with the videocassette, and Samantha dialed the number from one of the newsroom telephones. As the phone rang on the other line, she balanced the receiver on one shoulder and began typing her script for the wildlife convention story.

Back on Tropical Island, Ted Hughes was speaking to one of the other reporters when the phone rang. "...I'll need that write-up for the 11 o'clock news... WCAT City Desk." he said, answering the phone.

"Ted, it's Samantha."

"West, good. What's the news over there?" His voice was brisk.

"The conference is over; we're at our Vaharis bureau right now. Dave is copying the tape; the film footage should be in the network system any minute now."

"Excellent." Ted told her, plucking a press release from the fax machine on his desk and skimming through it. "I want that report for the evening news. It'll also be airing on the mainland. Anything else?"

"Yes, as a matter of fact," Samantha said, "We spoke with a park ranger at the conference who said that arctic foxes are becoming scarcer. Yet Governor Ulrich says the foxes are having a population boom and even announced plans to get them delisted."

Ted was intrigued. "Really?" he said, placing the press release to the side. "That's odd. Our governor, here on the island, always consults with the forest rangers before making a statement of that kind."

"I can just feel there's a story here - a good one." Samantha said excitedly. "I would love to stay here a while longer and look into it; dig around and see who's not telling the truth and why."

"Well," Ted considered, "there hasn't been much news around Faunaville or the rest of Tropical Island lately. All right, you and Dave can stay and investigate this, but if you haven't turned up anything else in a week you're both coming back here."

"Ok, that's great! Thanks"

"I want one of you to call me every couple of days," he told her, glancing at the clock on the wall. "This way I can make sure the two of you are ok and keep updated on the progress you're making."

"Will do," she answered.

Hanging up, Samantha instantly spied Dave returning and waved him over.

"Is the script done?" he asked.

"Almost," said Samantha. "Dave, I just got off the phone. Our editor is letting us stay here for another week to investigate the fox story."

"Hey, great!" replied Dave, "...listen, I spoke with the weatherman back there, and he's forecasting a snow storm, tonight."

"A snow storm?"

"Yeah, he says it's blowing in from the tundra."

"We'd better hurry back, then."

Samantha typed the end notation into the script, a 30 bordered by two dashes, and then printed it. As it came out of the printer, she handed it to Dave.

"Don't worry; I'll have the film edited in a jiffy," the photographer declared.

Snow was billowing down already and plows were beginning to emerge, attempting to clear the way for Vaharis' restless traffic. Visibility was very low which made it a hassle to drive.

The full force of the storm hit, however, upon their arrival at the lodge. Samantha and Dave had barely stepped out of the car when a gust of bitter arctic wind seized them; Samantha had to hold on to her hat to keep the gale from stealing it. Trying to shield each other from the brunt of the storm, they hurried to unlock the cabin door and sought shelter in the warmth of the interior.

Dave shut the door behind them, then called out, "Gero, we're home!"

Only silence responded.

"That's funny," he remarked. "Doesn't Geronimo usually come running when we arrive?"

"Maybe he's still sulking." Samantha shivered, leaning against the door. "Dave...is the thermostat turned down? It seems awfully cold in here."

"I'll go check."

He went upstairs; Samantha was about to follow him when her eyes caught sight of movement near one of the windows. Were the curtains swaying...? Approaching curiously, she found that the window was open...open wide enough to permit a cat to escape.

"Dave!"

The cameraman instantly appeared at the stairs. He glanced from Samantha to the open window; in one quick motion, he went to her and shut it. They both stared at each other. At last Dave spoke up, "You don't think..."

Before he had finished his sentence, the reporter was dashing to the door. He went after her. "Samantha!"

She didn't listen, instead flinging open the door. Snow stung her eyes, and the wind blew fiercely at her hair and clothes, but she fought against it and called out, "Geronimo! Geronimo!"

"Sam, it's pointless," Dave said. He gently held her by the shoulders and pulled her inside. "The wind is blowing too hard. We'd never find him tonight."

"I can't just leave him out there..." her voice trailed.

Dave closed the door and hugged her for a long time. He looked in her eyes and said, "Don't worry. Geronimo's a smart cat. He'll be ok. Tomorrow we can go out and look for him if he hasn't come back by morning."

"First thing," said Samantha. She loosened herself from his embrace and silently went up the stairs to the bedroom.

Chapter 5 - Snowstorm

Geronimo had never seen weather like this. Brutal cold seeped into his short fur, violent winds not unlike those of a hurricane lashed out mercilessly - but what kind of hurricane was this? There was no rain, only frigid flakes that whirled at him, clouding his vision in a wall of white.

Snow was unknown to Geronimo, who had lived all his life on Tropical Island. He struggled against it, his paws sinking into the powder at each step. The icy wind singed his whiskers and each time he pushed forward, its force made progress an impossibility. It howled through the forest, like a pack of hungry wolves. Desperate now, he tried to run, yet in that same instant a strong gust of wind blew at him, effortlessly picking up the fighting feline and hurling him backwards.

He extended his claws, catching hold of the trunk of a tree, but his claws just splintered the bark and the storm flung him against a nearby pine. The snow that had accumulated on the needles dropped suddenly with the impact and Geronimo - envisioning himself being trapped underneath - attempted to leap away, only to be jerked back. His collar had caught on one of the branches and suddenly the fight to seek shelter became a fight to survive. Panicking, he writhed around, but the thin strap kept a tight hold, choking him...

"Cat!" Geronimo was nudged suddenly by a white muzzle. Looking up, he stared into the amber eyes of the fluffy white creatures he had observed from the window. The one who had spoken was the male. "Hey, cat! Relax! Don't panic...just pull back slowly..."

Geronimo, dizzy from the hold on his neck and confused from the cold, did as the critter told him; the collar slipped off and Geronimo was free.

"Thanks..." Geronimo mewed, his voice hoarse.

"What are you doing out in this weather?" the female critter asked.

"I can't find my way back..." Another fierce gust howled past and the two white critters blocked it from pushing Geronimo away again. The cat noticed with interest the fur covering their paws, helping them to grip the snow. These critters seem born for this weather.

"We can't stay out here," said the male, "Follow me."

The three quickly made their way through the undergrowth, to a thin trail in the woods. Soon, they arrived at a tall pine tree with a burrow ensconced at its roots. One of the critters, the male, approached the opening and lifted his nose to the air. He sniffed for a minute and seeing that all was clear, beckoned to the other two. They swiftly entered the underground den.

One of the first things that struck Geronimo was how the noise of the snowstorm was muffled by the den walls. It faded to a faint, seemingly distant murmur, leaving the den relatively silent except for the thin crackle of gravel. In the semidarkness Geronimo could just make out the figures of the two animals, sitting close by and watching him.

"It's very cramped," said the female, gesturing with her tail to indicate the burrow. "Our original den was more spacious. It had twenty-one tunnel entrances all across the tundra."

Geronimo, still trembling from the cold, didn't respond. He had never heard of a den as large as what she recounted. The male critter spoke up, "My name is Ivan...this is my mate, Natasha."

"I'm Geronimo," the cat introduced himself. "Excuse me, but...what type of critters are you?"

"We're arctic foxes," answered Ivan.

"I've never seen foxes with white fur."

"Oh, we turn brown in the summertime," said Natasha.

Geronimo still looked perplexed; Ivan explained, "Every winter our coats become white so we can hide in the snow. Come summer, we shed it all and our fur turns short and brown."

"Then we should be safe from..." Natasha stopped abruptly.

Geronimo was looking at her expectantly, so she finished awkwardly, "...the snow...and the blizzards."

"You mean that cold sand everywhere?"

"Cold sand?" she echoed.

"That freezing white stuff falling from the sky."

"Yes, that's snow - and a snowstorm that is really bad is called a blizzard. You don't seem to be from around here," she remarked with interest.

"I'm from Tropical Island." Geronimo responded.

"I've heard of that place," said Ivan. "The warblers fly there for the winter. They tell me it's a very warm place with coconuts...whatever coconuts are. But they say the humans there are nice to animals. Is it true?"

"All the humans I've ever met, are." meowed Geronimo. "The warblers tell stories of the north, too. They spoke of snow, but I never imagined it was like this."

"It's not that bad," yapped Natasha. "Just wait until the snow storm subsides."

"Then you can head back to your den," Ivan added.

"I'm not sure where it is," admitted Geronimo.

The foxes looked at each other briefly and then back at the cat. Ivan spoke up. "You were wearing a collar, so you must have a human companion, right?"

"Oh...yes" hesitated Geronimo.

"So. You probably live in one of those dens just outside of the forest." offered Natasha.

"They call them cabins; a lodging place for humans who are visiting this area. I slipped out the window to inspect the woods and now I'm lost." Geronimo sighed; then continued, "I saw you two wandering around yesterday and since I had never seen white foxes, curiosity got the best of me and..."

"...and here you are now." chimed in Natasha.

"I know where that human settlement is" said Ivan. "In the morning, Natasha and I will show you how to get back."

"Thanks. Really." Geronimo purred.

"You're shivering," observed the vixen. "Ivan...he'll freeze. He doesn't have enough layers of fur, yet."

"Natty, you lie on one side of him and I on the other. He'll be in between us like we do to fox kits, to keep them warm."

And so, as the arctic winds howled outside, the three critters slept warmly and soundly inside the den.

In the heart of Vaharis, oblivious to the storm raging outside, Governor Victor Ulrich was in his office watching the evening news. There was a large television set situated to the left of his desk, which he used to keep up with news broadcasts. Standing in front of the TV, he was focused intently on the screen as he lazily smoked a cigarette. He didn't notice the cat Roxanne slink through the open door and curl up behind a tall, potted plant. It was Mabel's cat. The governor couldn't care less about Roxanne. As far as he was concerned, Roxanne was little more than an annoyance with no appreciable value.

At this moment, however, his mind was on the news story regarding the wildlife convention. His cool countenance scarcely betrayed the fury he felt upon hearing that one of the park rangers had dared speak up in opposition to his statement, and as the reporter signed off, Ulrich murmured, "Troublemaker."

Quick steps preceded the arrival of a lady at the office entrance; she had the tense air of one about to announce something, but noticing the governor's silence and the news broadcast on the television, she smirked instead.

"You've heard," she said, stepping into the office. "I was just coming to tell you."

"That ranger is severely mistaken if he thinks he can interfere," said Ulrich.

The woman wrapped her arms around him. "I trust you'll persuade him to see the error of it?"

"If convenient." A complacent smile crossed his lips. "Let him talk for now. I will get those foxes delisted...and there's nothing he can do about it."

The lady narrowed her eyes. "He can make noise and create trouble. For all of us."

"Denise Ralston," the governor mused, "are you worried this barking dog might actually bite?"

"Only that he'll alert the rest of the pack," Denise replied.

Ulrich turned his attention back to the television. "They'll never find out those statistics were falsified."

From behind the plant, Roxanne let out a hiss. Scoundrel, she thought. Who's worse, she or he?

"I missed you, last night" Denise whispered.

"You know I can't be in two places at once, unfortunately," answered Ulrich, "My wife, Mabel and I had tickets to the opera..."

"Mabel, always Mabel," interrupted Denise. Her face turned red with anger.

"Yes; Mabel is my wife," the governor quickly responded. "You had better come to terms with that issue. She has inherited millions, remember?"

Denise Ralston was treasurer of the region's funds. She was a rather tall woman, approximately the governor's height, with blonde hair, blue eyes and a mean-spirited personality. Denise was all about money. She cared about little else except her looks and luxury. She had first met the governor at his inauguration, about two years ago, and an affair began soon afterwards. Love was not the issue.

Her demeanor softened and her viper instincts took over. She said, "Well, let me leave you with a memory of what you missed."

She kissed him passionately and he responded by drawing her closer to his body. Roxanne the cat was frizzed and fuming mad. I wish I could get my claws on her, she thought. The cat crept out of the office silently.

As Roxanne walked down the hallway, she came across a young man who bent down to pet her.

“Hello, you beautiful feline!” he said. “What’s your name?”

“Roxanne,” replied the cat, “and your name is Luke Theron, isn’t it?”

“That’s right,” he replied. “Do you know where I can find the office of Denise Ralston?”

“Sure,” said Roxanne, “you’re standing in front of it. She’ll be back in a few minutes.”

“Ok, thanks,” answered Theron as the cat wandered off.

Back in the governor’s office, Ulrich said, "Go finish those financial reports. I need them in the morning. Those pesky reporters might show up asking questions."

"Ugh." Denise grimaced. "What is this? Cat hair!" She picked at a couple of fine hairs sticking to her silk blouse. "When will you finally get rid of that annoying animal?"

"Denny, you know she belongs to Mabel. She loves that cat. Why, I'll never know."

"Don't call me Denny. My name is Denise," she burst out angrily.

"Ok. Denise." He stroked her face and she calmed down.

"Let me take care of the cat," encouraged Denise. "This way, we won't have to worry about snoops or snitches."

"That cat is too stupid to care," answered Ulrich.

Denise smiled; turned and walked out the door. Ulrich shut off the television set and sitting down at his desk, started shuffling through some papers.

As Denise approached her office, she noticed a man waiting in front of the door and recognized him immediately.

“What the hell are you doing here?” she asked angrily. “You’re not supposed to come here.”

“Gorgonio and Venancio were getting antsy, and asked me to come and talk to you about…” Theron began.

“I don’t give a damn,” interrupted Denise. “Go back and tell them whatever they have to say can wait till the meeting.”

She went into her office and slammed the door in his face.

Theron took a deep breath, turned and left.

Chapter 6 - The Wildlife Poachers

The snow storm subsided in the morning, leaving the forest still and peaceful under its shimmering cover of snow. Ivan the fox poked his head out of the den and looked around; satisfied, he hopped out and scratched behind an ear. Geronimo scrambled out of the den immediately after, his blue eyes wide with fascination. "Why is it always so dim here? Doesn't the sun ever come out?"

"It's winter," replied Natasha as she emerged from the burrow. "The sun comes out, but it's usually opaque since the snow clouds cover it. It comes out for a much longer time during the summer. Isn't it like that everywhere?"

"Back on Tropical Island, the sun would always shine brightly in the daytime." explained Geronimo.

"Wow, that must be so weird!" Natasha yapped, intrigued. "No snow, constantly-bright sun. How can anyone there tell what season it is?"

"We need to get moving," Ivan interrupted suddenly. "The sooner we can make it to the cabin, the better."

"Hey, there's no rush," purred Geronimo. "If we know where the lodge is, there's no reason why we can't idle on our way. I'm still checking out the snow."

"But don't you want to be reunited with your humans?"

"Well, I am hungry. If I get back before they go out somewhere, they'll feed me."

The three set off down the forest path, Ivan taking the lead. The forest was beautiful blanketed in snow. It glittered as if wrapped in a sheet of diamonds; Geronimo, enthralled by it all, dashed ahead and leapt into the bank. "Meow! I love snow!"

Ivan looked as if he was going to protest, but Natasha pounced on him playfully and the two foxes began sprinting happily, like kits scampering around in the snow until - as if the same thing had crossed their minds - they abruptly stopped, glancing around nervously.

Geronimo ran over to them, his fur fluffed from the cold and his whiskers twitching excitedly. "Something wrong?"

"No...not really" Natasha responded. "But we shouldn't be making so much noise."

"Why not?"

Natasha appeared to be searching for an answer; it was Ivan who replied, "If we make too much noise, we'll scare off all the prey."

"Mice?" asked Geronimo.

"Lemmings," Ivan answered happily.

"They're like fat mice with no tails." Natasha explained, as they continued down the trail.

"They sound familiar," Geronimo mewed thoughtfully. "I think I remember hearing somewhere that they commit mass suicide. Is it true?"

"It's true, all right," Ivan yapped.

"Lemmings are nuts," said Natasha. "They breed like rabbits until one day they all lose it and they run to the Whirlpool River - close by here - to jump. They're bold, too. Heaven help the critter they run afoul of. They've been known to stand up to Musk Oxen and Caribou a hundred times their size! Incidentally," she said, stepping in front of Geronimo and staring at him, her voice becoming ominously serious, "never anger a lemming."

"Uh-huh. Okay..." Geronimo meowed; then, stepping around her, asked, "So, is there anything else to eat around here that's not deranged?"

"Anything you can find," Ivan shrugged.

"Is that why you left the tundra? A food shortage?"

"Mostly," Ivan murmured.

They had now reached a point where the trail veered off, becoming narrower and bordered by dry bracken and pine trees.
