The woods were soothingly tranquil here, the only sound being the brush of their paws through the snow and distant birdsong. "You had mentioned your humans were here visiting," remarked Natasha.

"Oh, yeah." Geronimo meowed, strutting ahead importantly with his tail held high, "They're journalists. The two of them are here covering some kind of a conference."

"Is that so?" said the male fox.

"...And they actually brought you with them on their journey?" added the vixen.

"Well...not intentionally. I hid in their luggage." Geronimo purred sneakily. "Everyone was upset at first, but they got over it quickly and..."

"Geronimo, look out!" Natasha shrieked suddenly.

There was a flash of silver and letting out a screech, Geronimo leapt straight up in the air at the same time that cruel, steel jaws lunged hungrily from the snow like a piranha, snapping together audibly with a crushing force.

Without warning, two gunshots exploded from the bushes; the foxes instinctually ducked and the bullets barely missed their heads. Instead, they hit the bark of a nearby tree, showering them with thin shards of wood. "Run for it!" Natasha barked.

Geronimo - stunned and confused - tried to dash forward, but more sharp teeth barred his way, springing up from the ground uncontrollably and making his ears ring with their harsh snapping noise. "It's a trap line!" Ivan yapped at him, just as another shot was fired. "This way!"

He dove into the bracken, Natasha on his heels; Geronimo threw himself after them, his heart pounding and his mind reeling. They had just emerged from the brush when Geronimo felt his heart momentarily stop. A man stood only a short distance away, aiming a rifle directly at them.

"Missed us?" he sneered to the two foxes.

Ivan turned sharply, kicking up snow. The man fired but misjudging their exact location, failed to hit them as they dashed off. "They're heading that way!" the man shouted to other hunters.

Geronimo could hear gunfire from behind, acutely aware of the dangerous proximity at which each bullet fell. As the foxes bounded a fallen tree, their bushy tails streaming out behind them, Geronimo swiftly took the lead; weaving this way and that, running as fast as his body could withstand, until...

He stopped as he found himself at the edge of a precipice, dislodging pebbles which clattered down the steep rock into the raging water below. As the full image came into view, Geronimo saw that it was a gorge, whose craggy walls divided the forest from the city. Below, the frothy white water spun viciously to a vortex, creating dozens of them, each whirlpool threatening to devour anything that fell in its menacing grasp. To their left, far from where they stood, a large suspension bridge crossed from one side to the other, but the chasm was too wide to jump.

A gunshot from behind startled Geronimo and the foxes.

"Come on!" Ivan yapped to the others, leaping off the cliff. He landed squarely on a rocky ledge jutting out below; from there he bounded to another one. Geronimo - still trying to catch his breath - followed without hesitation, as did Natasha. They leapt from one ledge to another, making a steady and rapid descent, until Ivan halted unexpectedly.

Before them, the cliff wall turned sheer, stranding them on a narrow shelf halfway down.

Ivan turned to Geronimo, dismay flickering in his amber eyes. "Geronimo," he said, "there's something we haven't told you."

"No kidding!" the tomcat hissed.

At that moment, a gunshot from above took everyone by surprise; gravel rained down onto their fur as the bullet missed and hit the cliff instead. Looking up, Geronimo felt his claws unsheathe, scraping the smooth surface of the ledge. Standing at the top of the cliff, his rifle pointed at them, was one of the hunters.

It was only now that Geronimo could get a good look at him. He was slim - slightly older than Samantha and Dave - with sharp features framed by wavy dark brown hair that covered half his ears, and dark brown eyes with a somehow merciless quality. As Geronimo watched, he was joined at the precipice by two other men - one had short blond hair with brown eyes, rather young; the other was heavyset, with blue eyes and hair that was shaved down to stubs. Both were also armed with rifles.

The youngest of the hunters looked over the edge of the cliff. "Forget it, Gorgonio," he said. "You'll never get the pelts back up here. And the cat's a trash kill."

"Theron, I don't care if they fall into the river and drown," Gorgonio, still aiming at the animals, snapped back, "I want to see them dead! Venancio! Take a shot at 'em" he yelled.

The third hunter fired, hitting the ledge the three critters were huddled on. Part of it crumbled into the roaring torrent below; Natasha yelped as she nearly lost her balance.

Gorgonio smiled, his evilness apparent as he reveled in the thought of the torment he was inflicting on the animals. He fired at them again; Ivan growled fiercely at him, though Natasha merely let out a terrified whimper. Geronimo, however, was taking notice of the bridge.

Through their scrambling down the rock face, they had moved nearer to it; Geronimo could somewhat make out the noise from the occasional automobile that crossed the structure. But that was not what had caught the cat's attention. Underneath the bridge was a metal framework that stretched along its length. From there, Geronimo realized, it would be possible to escape onto the bridge!

Geronimo crouched down, tensing his body to jump. From behind him he heard Ivan bark, "What are you doing?!"

"Just follow me!" Geronimo yowled, leaping into the air. For a brief heartbeat, he was over the swirling waters; then he dropped suddenly, barely catching hold of the framework with his forepaws. He could hear gunfire ringing out as he struggled not to lose his grip, his claws screeching on the metal. At last, breathlessly climbing onto the metal bar, he turned back to Ivan and Natasha. The two foxes were pressed against the cliff wall, the shelf they were perched on remarkably thinner than before. "Ivan! Natasha!"

They looked up at the feline, who waved his tail as if gesturing for them to follow his lead. "He's right - that's our only chance," Ivan said, scarcely dodging another bullet.

"Oh...no way!" Natasha shook her head. "I'm not...We'd fall! There are whirlpools..."

"...and if we stay here we'll be shot!" Ivan yapped, nudging her; she leapt - almost in panic - but fell short. She squealed just as Geronimo pounced and seizing the scruff of her neck in his teeth, he pulled her up. Ivan, who was still on the ledge, turned to glare at the three hunters. Gorgonio aimed exactly at him, but in that instant the fox leapt, landing perfectly beside Geronimo; the shot hit where the fox had been standing and what remained of the ledge collapsed into the river.

Safe at last, the three animals crawled along the steel frame and onto the bridge. Gorgonio tried to aim at them, but didn't fire. "They're too far away. Shit!" he snarled, thrusting down the rifle in fury.

Geronimo had by now, managed to catch his breath. The animals looked on as the hunters retreated into the woods.

"That was close," said Natasha.

Ivan didn't say anything, only licking her behind the ear comfortingly. The two foxes then glanced over at the cat, who was roughly trying to smooth down his frizzed fur. Sensing the foxes' watchful eyes, Geronimo looked up.

"We owe you an explanation." Ivan said quietly.

Geronimo flicked an ear. "Who were those people and why were they shooting at us?"

Ivan swished his bushy tail around, so that it curled around his paws. "We are being hunted," he responded.

"It was because of them that we had to flee the tundra," Natasha continued. "My ancestors had built their den here and it had been passed down throughout generations of foxes. Then one day those men found it. They destroyed it."

"We have seen them do terrible things," Ivan said. "Things that are...pointless."

Geronimo stared at them for a moment, as if expecting a further explanation, but both foxes stayed silent. "So what will you do?" he said at last.

"The only thing we can." Ivan replied. "Run."

Chapter 7 - Gotcha

Samantha and Dave had gone into the forest to search for their missing feline. It was still rather early and there were a few trails through the woods where the snow was not very deep, affording relative ease in travel.

Samantha nonetheless felt despondent. Dave - hoping at the least to offer a small distraction - reminded her that they still had not filmed any of the northern wildlife and that it would be an excellent addition to any follow-up reports they did, so they might as well do so now since they were going into the forest anyway. This cheered her up a bit, but her spirits fell once more when they came across Geronimo's collar snagged on the lower branch of a pine tree.

"Well, I guess that's that," she sighed, gently retrieving it from the branch.

"Samantha, I'm sure he hasn't gone far..." Dave's voice trailed off somewhat as she turned her vivid green gaze to him. Neither she nor he, truly believed those words, no matter how much they wanted to.

At last, Samantha spoke, "Now people will think he's a stray."

"Not if they speak to him," Dave pointed out. "He could always tell them he's got humans."

"That's true," Samantha acknowledged; then seeming to cheer up, added, "And if they have a television set all he has to do is point us out."

The pair felt happier after that and decided to continue down the trail.

Winter had enveloped the woodland and as Samantha and Dave were walking along, they made their way to a part of the forest where the pines dissipated and before them was a treeless, snow-covered meadow. The snow here was wind-swept, and although the gale of last night had long since died down, every so often a small gust would blow past and lift a few of the snowflakes from the ground. The land - though mostly flat - would slope in sections, but with the snow cover it was difficult to say at a glance whether these were piles of snow or the territory itself.

As Dave started the film rolling, Samantha narrated into the microphone: "We're at the edge of the forest. Over there is the unchanged wilderness where the foxes live; the backdrop for political debate over whether to delist the arctic fox."

She paused and the two stared out at the landscape, which stretched into the distance. Samantha remarked, "It's strange, Dave...such a desolate territory, and yet it seems ethereal. The silence has a strange beauty all its own."

"Well, I got a shot of it. It is beautiful, though rather barren." Dave said.

"That's the tundra," a familiar voice interjected; the reporter and cameraman both glanced over to see the park ranger they had met at yesterday's conference. "The trees can't grow any farther than this point because the ground over there is frozen solid...permafrost; but come spring when the sun shines warmer the tundra becomes covered in flowers. Those small hills happen as a result of the land freezing and melting."

Samantha smiled. "Ranger Conway...what a surprise, meeting you again, out here!"

Conway shook his head. He went over a few paces to them. "You shouldn't be wandering around alone in the forest like this," he told them. "These woods can be dangerous if you don't know them."

"Oh, we know our way back to the lodge. Right, Dave?"

"Sure, we just head that way," Dave said, pointing left.

Samantha squinted. "No...the lodge is that way," she corrected, pointing right.

"The Crossing Lodge?" When both Samantha and Dave nodded, Conway pointed straight ahead.

The reporter and cameraman chuckled in mild embarrassment. "So...did Governor Ulrich ever contact you about the fox population?" Samantha asked.

"No, he never did," said Conway, thoughtfully. "I suppose he's a very busy man, but I found something rather disconcerting."

"What did you find?"

Conway hesitated and then answered, "Well...since you're here anyway, I might as well show you."

The park ranger led them down the trail, through the pines, to the base of a tree trunk. Here, he bent down and collected a small metal shell lying in the snow; he showed it to them. "See this?" he said, as Dave began filming. "This is a bullet casing. This type is from a rifle mostly used to hunt furbearing animals, because it won't cause much damage to the pelt. Animals like arctic foxes."

"Could they have been hunting some other animal?"

"There are others in these woods...mink, arctic hare. I had thought for a moment they were after one of those, but then I found this." Conway drew back an overhanging pine branch to reveal steel traps buried in the snow. "Fox traps." Conway said. "And not just any fox traps. These are steel-jawed leghold traps, which were outlawed after being deemed inhumane. These few have already been snapped shut, so apparently some lucky animal escaped, but there are more down the trap line that haven't been triggered yet. I believe someone is after arctic foxes for their fur, and doesn't care how they go about getting it. This isn't just a minor violation," he added, turning to look at the reporter and cameraman. "This is poaching."

"Poaching?!" Governor Victor Ulrich appeared shocked.

After their conversation with the park ranger, Samantha and Dave had gone to the governor's mansion to interview Ulrich about the matter. As luck would have it, they found him outside his office, where he showed them in politely. If he had any reservations about speaking with them, he did not betray it, but he took interest when he heard of the discovery in Hammond Forest. "Outrageous!" the governor declared, standing up from his seat. "Rest assured that if this is true, I will not let those poachers go unpunished. I'm ordering a full investigation into this."

Samantha jotted something down in her notepad. "At the conference, you refused to comment on allegations that the arctic fox population was declining. Do you think that poaching could be creating a perceived decline?"

"Absolutely not." Ulrich hurried to say. "The fox population has increased markedly after I enacted legislation to protect them. No poachers are going to ruin the chances of these beautiful little animals getting off the endangered species list and becoming the next wildlife success story. I'll see to it personally." He smiled. "Ms. West, Mr. Candid, thank you so much for bringing this to my attention. You're doing an excellent job" he told them, shaking the perplexed journalists' hands.

"...Thank you." Samantha said, a bit wary of why, Ulrich - who had just yesterday seemed so aloof with them - now seemed to be so talkative and friendly. She sensed an icy animosity in his tone of voice. She didn't trust him.

As the two were leaving, Samantha had an afterthought, "Ranger Conway had been hoping you would contact him regarding this."

Ulrich replied smoothly, "I can assure you, Ms. West...he'll hear from me."

Samantha still had the uneasy feeling there was something strange about the way Ulrich had acted as she and her companion stepped out of the office.

No sooner had the TV news crew left, however, that Governor Ulrich began quickly dialing the telephone on his desk. "Gorgonio? ...You three are the most incompetent people I have ever hired! I don't pay you to do sloppy work and let your trap lines get discovered by park rangers! Now I've got the media in here asking questions and...damn right it concerns you!"

At that moment, the governor's cell phone rang. "Hold on!" he screamed at Gorgonio. He recognized the number on the phone's screen and answered with a friendly demeanor. "Well, hello...nice hearing from you, Ambassador Qiang."

The voice on the other end answered quickly. It was a man who spoke with an Asian accent.

"Ulrich. Tonight we have the meeting. 11 o'clock. Same place. You have the goods?"

"Yes, of course." responded the governor, "I assume you have the cash?"

"As usual" the voice answered.

"Later, then" said Ulrich. He hung up the cell phone and returned to the telephone call.

"Gorgonio, you idiot. You and your men had better get on the ball. I don't pay for mistakes. That nosy ranger Conway found traps. He's a problem and I want him taken care of. That's an extra three percent of the cut for each of you; and don't forget the meeting tonight at 11 p.m., same place. Got it?" Ulrich didn't wait for a response; he just hung up the phone.

On the other end of the line, Gorgonio also hung up the telephone. He turned around and faced the other two, Theron and Venancio; with a smirk on his face.

"It's all set. He's got another job for us, though." he said.

"Different type fur?" asked Venancio. "We'd need different traps."

"No. We'll be hunting human," answered their leader.

Theron jumped in, "Hey. I'm not sure about that. Human?"

Gorgonio grabbed him by the collar and yelled in his ear, "Three percent extra! Are you sure about that!?"

He released him and continued talking. "We need to be more careful, Ulrich said that some reporters were asking questions and that's really got him pissed off."

"Who exactly are we supposed to deal with?" asked Venancio.

"Conway" said Gorgonio. "That ranger has been a pain in the ass since the start. Theron, you're good with electronics. Rig up a gadget that we could put to his car. You know what I mean."

"Yeah boss... No problem." replied Theron hesitantly.

Gorgonio announced, "Listen to me. Think of the money. People kill each other in wars all the time and nobody really gives a damn. It's not our problem. It's our gain."

Back at the governor's mansion, journalists Samantha West and Dave Candid stepped into the hallway where the elevators were. Dave tapped the button and they waited for an elevator heading down. "So, that was it," said Dave. "Poaching. No wonder there was that misconception about the fox population. Well, I guess all stories can't make headlines."

"I don't know. I just can't shake off the feeling that there was something weird about the way Ulrich was behaving back there." Samantha replied pensively. She sighed. "Maybe I'm just being cynical."

The elevator doors opened and as they stepped inside, Dave said, "Don't be too hard on yourself. They say cynicism is one of the best traits for the investigative reporter."

Suddenly her eyes flashed with thrilled realization. "Of course...why didn't I think of it before!"

"Think of what?" Dave asked.

"What I should have done from the beginning." Samantha responded as the elevator reached the bottom floor. "Check the file cabinets."

The regional Capitol was across the street from the governor's mansion; so the two of them got there swiftly. The clerk at the Records office was a young woman with reddish hair whose name tag read 'Jane'.

She greeted them, "Good afternoon, may I help you?"

"Yes, I'd like to see the population reports for the arctic fox, please"

"Which years?"

"The past five."

The clerk turned and disappeared into a door in the back, then reappeared a few minutes later with some papers. She handed them to the reporter.

"Thank you, Jane" said Samantha.

The TV news crew began looking though the documents.

"Aha!" Samantha smiled. "All of these documents say that the fox population is extremely low...nothing about any sort of comeback."

"So why would the governor be saying something else?" Dave wondered.

"Yeah...and why would he want the arctic fox delisted?" Samantha glanced up from the documents to meet her companion's eyes. "This might make headlines after all."

They copied the population reports and headed out of the Capitol building.

Governor Ulrich was seated at his desk, reading a letter, when his secretary appeared at the office door. "Governor, the television news crew from WCAT is back; they'd like to speak with you."

Ulrich thought for a moment before laying the letter to the side. "Show them in," he answered.

Only a few moments passed before Samantha appeared at the doorway. "Governor Ulrich?"

"Back so soon?" he asked.

"We have a few follow-up questions based on some new information we've received," Samantha explained, as she and Dave stepped inside.

"Oh, really?" Governor Ulrich leaned back in his chair, staring intently at them.

"You're saying that the arctic fox population has increased...?"

"Yes," Ulrich quickly spoke up. "They've made a stunning comeback."

"Do you have anything supporting that?"

There was a long moment of silence; eventually, Samantha went on, "We checked arctic fox population reports filed at the regional Capitol, and they all say that the fox population has not made any..."

"They were done before this new study," Ulrich interrupted.

"What study?"

"The study saying that they've rebounded."

"Who did that study?"

"Well...I don't remember right now"

"How long ago was it done?"

"It was done recently," said the governor, now seeming a bit flustered.

"How recently?"

"No...comment."

"No comment?" Samantha tipped her head to one side. "Governor, aren't you worried that not commenting might make it look as if you don't know what you're talking about? ...As if the numbers you cited at the convention were pulled out of thin air?"

Ulrich was visibly angry. "What you're doing has a name. They call it Gotcha Journalism."

Samantha smiled and answered with a whisper, "Gotcha."

Ulrich met her gaze steadily. "Get out of my office. Now!"

The pair knew they had overstayed their welcome and without saying another word, turned around and left the office.

They encountered the park ranger, Conway, speaking with Ulrich's secretary.

"I'm sorry, he's unavailable right now," the secretary was saying. "In fact he's all booked for this month."

"Couldn't I make an appointment to speak with him next month?" Conway asked her.

"We don't schedule appointments that far in advance," the secretary answered.

The ranger glanced towards Samantha and Dave, nodded in greeting and they in turn nodded back. The reporter and her cameraman walked out into the hallway, away from the secretary's desk, turned the corner and stayed there with the camera rolling.

At the same time, Mabel was turning the corner at the opposite end of the hallway. She noticed the reporters and the ranger and thought to herself, I wonder what's happening? She decided to hide and observe.

Unexpectedly, at that moment, Ulrich walked out of his office. He seemed in a hurry, but stopped short in his tracks when he saw the ranger.

Ranger Conway turned to face him and said, "Governor, I came to speak to you about the issue of delisting the arctic foxes."

Ulrich interrupted him. "There's nothing to talk about. I've made the decision."

"Based on what information?" responded Conway, anger rising in his voice.

"I don't have to explain myself to you," Ulrich replied.

"Perhaps not to me, but in an election year you do have to explain yourself to the voters."

Ulrich was visibly annoyed at this statement and answered quickly. "I suppose you think you have the power to make me lose the election? I'm ahead of my opponent according to the polls. I suggest, Ranger, that you go back to your cabin and stick to what you know, keeping track of the squirrels and the rabbits."

"Governor Ulrich, I don't know much about politics or whatever it is you're getting out of this - but I do know that if you delist those foxes now, you're sentencing an entire species to extinction. Their numbers are so low they'd never be able to withstand having a bounty on their pelts, which is exactly what'll happen when the department stores hear open season declared on arctic foxes."

Ulrich focused his icy blue eyes on the park ranger. "I'll decide when they can be delisted."

Samantha leaned forward to hold the microphone closer to the sound. It was then that the microphone cable, which had gotten tangled on her heel, tripped her; she fell and Dave caught her before she hit the ground, but not before Ulrich had glanced up at the commotion out in the hallway.

"I thought I told you fucking journalists to leave!"

Samantha was trying to unravel the cable from her legs, while still holding the microphone out. "Governor, do you mean to say that you don't care whether or not there are enough foxes to safely delist them?"

Ulrich ignored the question. "I won't stand for this any longer. Get out of my office before I call security."

Ranger Conway spoke up again, distracting the governor. "Is there some reason you don't want the press here?" By this time, Samantha had gotten her legs free from the cable, and together with Dave had made their way towards the ongoing quarrel.

"Are you in cahoots with the press?" Ulrich retorted.

"No. But the more I hear, the more I realize that you stink," said Conway.

"Your opinion is of no concern to me."

"You should value my opinion, Governor, because I'm not just a ranger. I'm a concerned citizen and I vote."

"Your one vote is not going to decide the election. Get out of the building before I have you arrested..." Ulrich paused and gave an irritated look to the TV news crew. Dave was recording the spat, while Samantha was in between the ranger and governor, shifting the microphone alternately from one to the other. "...and shut that damn camera off!" Ulrich added to the photographer.

Dave did not. Samantha was the one who replied, pointing the microphone back to Ulrich after her question: "We're in a public building, funded by public dollars. Don't we have the right to film here?"

"Not when a publicly elected official tells you to leave," he retorted. Before Samantha could dispute the legality of this, he grabbed her firmly by the arm and half-led, half-pushed her back out into the hallway; Dave followed, still filming. "I have had enough of your sensationalized, unscrupulous excuse for journalism. The elevators are that way. And as for you..." he turned with a glare towards Conway.

"I'm leaving," said Conway. "Fuck you."

A look that was both indescribable and unexplainable to the journalists crossed Ulrich's eyes for a fleeting second, but it was gone almost instantly. Ulrich shrugged his shoulders and said nothing in response.

Conway walked off, and Ulrich turned to head back into his office. He stopped at the entrance and murmured something to his secretary, who nodded. The reporters chased after the park ranger.

"Ranger Conway!"

Conway stopped and let Samantha and Dave catch up with him. "Hi guys." He appeared disenchanted.

"Do you have any comment for our viewers?" asked Samantha.

"I made a mistake," he said. "I thought that maybe the governor didn't know what was going on, but I think it's clear now that what happens to the foxes just doesn't matter to him. Why he would be so hell-bent on delisting them is beyond me." Conway glanced from the reporter to the cameraman. "When I met you two in the forest earlier today, I started thinking about how Governor Ulrich never called me back and decided that with poachers after the foxes, I couldn't let this be ignored any more. Now I see it makes no difference."

"The Ministry of Wildlife gets its numbers on animal populations from the rangers, doesn't it?" asked Samantha.

"Yes, and also from biologists stationed in different areas where the animals are located. They sort through the info and then the Minister of Wildlife signs saying whether or not the animal is scarce or abundant."

She showed the ranger the population reports she and Dave had copied. "Well, the Wildlife Ministry records agree with you. They say arctic fox numbers are so low, they can't be delisted."

Conway gave her a surprised look. "But if that's the case, then the foxes can't legally be delisted. The governor can only delist them when the Ministry of Wildlife says the population is strong enough to be able to thrive."

"Why would the governor make the show of announcing plans to delist the fox if he can't do it?" Samantha asked.

"Maybe he wants the publicity," Conway said. "Although wouldn't a lie that ostentatious, harm more than help in an election year?"

Unless there's something we don't know, Samantha thought.

Samantha thanked the ranger for taking the time to speak with them and finished the interview. When the TV news crew had left, Mabel, who had been hiding and listening, approached Conway.

"Ranger," Mabel called out to him, "may I have a word with you, please?"

Conway looked at her with surprise and said, "Mrs. Ulrich, how may I help you?"

"I couldn't help but overhear the conversation you had with my husband," Mabel began. "Dare I say that I agree with you. It seems that not so long ago, our region's wildlife was better protected from poaching."

Conway looked at her without saying a word. He was speechless.

Mabel continued, "It is my sincere wish that the truth come out, regardless of who's right or wrong."

"Thank you very much, Mrs. Ulrich; I hope the governor will come to think the way you do," responded Conway.

Mabel turned the corner and was gone; Conway proceeded to the elevator, thinking, That is a very graceful and beautiful lady. How did she end up with a guy like Ulrich?

Meanwhile, Ulrich had gone back into his office and began dialing the telephone. The other line rang three times before a man's voice answered:

"Washburn speaking."

"Why the hell haven't you changed those documents?" Ulrich was furious.

"I've had time to think about it, Ulrich. I want nothing to do with the matter." Washburn answered. "You know how fast our careers would be destroyed if we falsify those records and people found out?"

Ulrich scoffed. "What makes you think people would ever find out? Or that if they found out, they would even care?"

There was silence on Washburn's line for a moment before he replied: "I'm not signing those documents. The foxes are endangered."

"You'll sign those documents within 48 hours," Ulrich told him, and hung up the phone.

On the other end of the line, Washburn set the phone receiver down; he felt a sudden moment of fear.

What did Ulrich mean with that last sentence? He wouldn't dare do anything to me; I'm in a superior position than he is. Still, I wonder if I should talk to somebody about this.

His thoughts were interrupted by the telephone ringing, and still in shock, he lifted the receiver and simply said hello.

The voice on the other end of the line was cheerful and came through clearly. "Why the change in your usual greeting? Is everything okay?"

"Oh, yes, I've just been very busy," he answered, "but never too busy to speak to my beautiful wife."

"Well," she continued, "if I remember correctly we had a lunch date today. I'm waiting at the restaurant at the corner."

Washburn straightened up in his seat and said, "Yes, you're right. I'll be there in five minutes" and he hung up the phone.

He grabbed his coat from the back of the chair and walked out of the office.

When Samantha and Dave reached the news van, they played back the tape they had recorded, watching it on the camera's viewfinder. "We got some great footage," Dave said happily.

"Yeah, and some good quotes too." The reporter turned to her cameraman. "But this just seems to be the tip of the iceberg. Ulrich is lying. But why?"

"It certainly doesn't look like it's against his will," Dave analyzed. "Maybe he was bribed, or he's getting kickbacks from whoever's poaching the foxes. Sam, we seem to have stumbled across one hell of a story..."

Dave opened the back door of the news van while Samantha began reviewing her notes. "So, where are we off to now?" asked Dave.

"The newsroom," Samantha answered. "I've got to call up the wildlife minister, Mr. Washburn, and see if he'll comment on what the governor's saying. We've also got to fill our editor in on what's been happening. What time is it?"

"Almost 11."

"Maybe we can get it on the News at Noon."

They suddenly heard a distinctive meow; they both glanced over and saw, sitting a small distance away from them in front of an alley, their missing cat.

"Geronimo?" Samantha couldn't believe it.

Geronimo took a big leap and landed in her arms, purring.

"You get around, don't you!" the cat meowed. "What are you doing all the way here?"

"We could ask you the same thing!" laughed Samantha.

"Hey, Ger, about time you turned up." Dave petted him on the head. "We were beginning to get worried."

"Guys, there are some critters I'd like you to meet." Geronimo turned his head, angling his ears towards the alley. Samantha looked in the same direction and stared in complete surprise. Sitting where only moments before Geronimo had been, were two arctic foxes.

Samantha was speechless; Dave quickly brought the camera back up to his shoulder to film. The foxes jumped when the camera's spotlight washed over them. They turned and fled back into the alley.

Geronimo let out a hiss as he leapt out of Samantha's arms and ran after them. "Wait just a minute," he told his humans before they could react.

In the alley, Ivan and Natasha were sneaking away, back the path they had come, until Geronimo got in front of them.

"Where are you off to?" a perplexed Geronimo inquired.

"Back to the forest." said Ivan. "We're glad you found your humans, but we've got to leave already."

"I was hoping you could meet them," said Geronimo.

The two foxes exchanged looks. "We don't think that's a very good idea," said Natasha.

"Why not?"

"One of them pointed a gun at us." Ivan yapped, his ears flat.

"A gun? What...no, you're mistaken. That's a TV camera," Geronimo explained. "My humans like critters. They'd never harm you."

"Are you sure?" Natasha said.

"Positive!" Geronimo asserted. When the foxes still seemed doubtful, he added, "At any rate, if anyone can help you with your plight, it's them."

"How?" asked Ivan.

"Well, I bet a lot of humans here don't know the anguish you foxes are going through. Maybe if people know, they'll do something about it. If you want to get rid of those hunters, this is your chance," Geronimo purred.

Geronimo emerged from the alley with the two foxes following him. They were still obviously distrustful of being out in the open and hesitated only a few paces away from where the TV news crew was.

Geronimo walked over to his humans. "These are my humans - Samantha and Dave" Geronimo introduced them.

Samantha crouched down and extended a hand, trying to coax the foxes closer. "Hello" she said.

Ivan crept forward, not taking any notice when Dave resumed filming. Natasha remained at a distance as her mate stood directly in front of Samantha...and snatched her hat.

"Hey!" Samantha tried to grab it back, but the male fox dashed away and hid under their van. Samantha hurried after him and glancing underneath it, found a grinning Ivan with the fedora. "That's my hat," said a clearly amused Samantha.

Natasha, now confident, leapt over and put her forepaws on the reporter's lap. "I'm Natasha," she yapped.

"...and I'm Ivan," the male fox said, emerging with the hat which he dropped at Samantha's feet.

The foxes then ran over to Dave. He had been filming throughout, but now bent down to stroke them.

Geronimo hopped up to sit just inside the van. The back door was still open so he sat down on the floor here, tucking his paws underneath him.

"So this is what you've been up to, befriending endangered species," said Samantha.

"They're endangered?" Geronimo's eyes grew wide. "But they're being hunted."

"Geronimo said you could help us stop the hunting," Ivan barked.

"We've been looking into it," Dave admitted.

"You already know?" mewed Geronimo.

"A source told us this morning." Samantha explained.

"We have to head back," said Natasha. "It was very nice meeting you both."

"You're welcome to drop by the cabin," Samantha told them. "I'll set out dishes of cat food on the porch, tonight."

The foxes opened their eyes wide in surprise and looked at each other happily.

"Thank you. We'll be there," said the male fox.

Ivan and Natasha ran off. As the arctic foxes vanished down the alley, Samantha turned to Dave. “This was fortunate! Dave, did you get all that on camera?”

The cameraman grinned. “Yep! We got some great footage of the foxes.”

Suddenly, a loud explosion resonated from across the street and Geronimo leapt up with a surprised meow; smoke filled the street and sirens began blaring through the air.

"What the hell was that?" Dave said.

"A car exploded! Let's get over there," Samantha answered, adding to the cat crouched on the news van's floor: "Geronimo, stay put...please!"

Flames were spouting out of the front of a car that was parked a short distance away and people were running away from it.

The reporter and her cameraman were running towards it, of course. Dave stood as close to it as he could and started filming.

Samantha noticed that on the side of the vehicle were the words "Park Ranger." She looked around and saw Ranger Conway hurrying over from the governor's mansion.

He stopped where they were and said, "My dog! Where's my dog, Zachary?"

They all stared at the car, which by now was engulfed in a ball of fire. At that point, they heard barking and turned around to see a Siberian Husky dog running towards them. It was Zachary.

Dave filmed the joyful reunion as the ranger knelt down and hugged the dog. "Man, am I glad you've got a mind of your own. I'll never tell you to stay in the car alone again."

His canine companion answered him, "Having a sixth sense is a life saver!"

The firefighters arrived and after they had put out the blaze, not much was left of the car. Samantha had a chance to talk with the ranger before the police approached him with questions about the situation.

"Are you all right?" she said.

"I'm just stunned..." he responded, staring at the wreckage with complete shock reflected in his eyes.

"Were you having any car trouble before?" Samantha asked.

"No, I wasn't." Conway turned back to her, puzzled. "That's just it - the car was fine."

At that moment, a man came up to them. "I'm Detective Hartcourt. I'd like to have a few words with you," he said to Conway.

"Excuse me," the park ranger told the reporter. He went a small distance away to speak with the detective.

Samantha turned to Dave. "We'd better call this in to the city newsroom, this needs to get on the air; also, we need to call Ted and fill him in."

When she called their affiliate, the editor, Gao, requested that they do the initial report since they were already at the scene. As they began setting things up for the live broadcast, Conway returned.

"What's up?" Dave asked.

"The detective said they found that an explosive had been put to the car," said Conway. "Thankfully, it was placed in a way to give enough time for anyone in the car to get out, so whoever put it apparently just meant it as a threat. He asked if I had any known enemies, to which I responded no. But between you and me, I think it could be retaliation for what I said about the foxes."

"Do you suspect someone in particular?" Samantha inquired.

"Not all poaching is done on a small scale." sighed Conway. "The person who ordered this, is probably behind the poaching, but as for who it is, honestly I have no idea." The park ranger suddenly seemed exhausted, as if the transpired events were now taking their toll.

From the governor's mansion, the plume of smoke was visible. Standing at his office window, Ulrich smiled.

Chapter 8 - Intrigue

"Our reporter, Samantha West, is live at the scene...Samantha?"

The image on the television screen flipped to the news reporter. Ulrich wasn't sure whether to be relieved or worried that Samantha was not broadcasting the 'gotcha' moment that had happened today only a while earlier.

His secretary walked into the office. "Excuse me, Governor, I have called the news editor and the appointment has been set up for tomorrow at 10 a.m. His name is Ted Hughes. I was told he'd be flying in from Tropical Island."

Ulrich looked at the calendar on his desk and then wrote the information down in his personal planner. "Thank you," he said without looking up, and closed the booklet.

As the secretary walked out the door, Ulrich looked at the television set in time to hear Samantha finish her report.

"No one was injured in the blast. They're calling this a threat - not an attempt - against Ranger Conway's life. Reporting live, Samantha West, WCAT 8 News."

Ulrich was stupefied. "Damn it!" he yelled. "Those inefficient morons!"

Outside, Geronimo was sitting in the back of the news van watching as Samantha and Dave began taking down their broadcast equipment.

"We never got a chance to call Mr. Washburn for comment, what with all that fuss of Conway's car exploding," Samantha remarked to Dave. "Hopefully he's still at his office."

"Yeah. I wonder why he didn't respond to the governor's announcement about delisting the foxes," Dave said.

"Maybe he's got something to hide," Geronimo meowed.

Dave took the tripod and monitors to the van's trunk as Samantha climbed into the back of the news van. Besides the broadcasting and editing equipment, they also had a mobile phone here.

The reporter sat down at the table, and Geronimo leapt up next to her. Samantha spread out the arctic fox population records and opened the latest one to its last page. There was a signature here approving the report's conclusion that the foxes should remain listed as an endangered species, and below this the words:

Mr. Landon Washburn, Minister of Wildlife

Below this, in turn, was the wildlife minister's contact information. Samantha took a pencil and began dialing the telephone.

She got his secretary on the line. "Hello, I'm Samantha West with WCAT 8 News. I was hoping to schedule an interview with the wildlife minister. ...It's just a few questions about the arctic fox population. ...Yes, I'll hold."

Only a few moments had passed before a man's voice answered the phone. "Mr. Washburn speaking."

Samantha re-introduced herself and said, "I'd like to schedule an interview with you for our newscast."

"Regarding the foxes?"

"That's right. Would you be available around noon tomorrow, perhaps, or...?"

Washburn immediately answered, "I can meet with you at 11:30 in the morning. There's something about the fox population I think your viewers should know about."

"What is it?" asked the reporter, grabbing her notepad.

"I'd prefer to speak with you in person. Do you know the Chinese restaurant on Brook Avenue?"

"The one on the corner of Stanford Street, with big red letters?"

"Yes, that's the one," said Washburn.

"All right," said Samantha. "11:30 a.m. I'll see you then."

When he hung up the telephone, she did so as well. "He'll meet with us around 11:30 at a Chinese restaurant here in Vaharis." Samantha said to Dave. "He said there was something our viewers should know about the fox population."

"I wonder what that is," said Dave.

The phone rang, and interrupted their conversation. Dave answered. It was their editor.

"I was looking for you guys to let you know that you can take the rest of the day off," he said. "You've been working straight away since you got here."

"Thanks Gao," said Dave. "I'll tell Samantha."

He hung up and before he could say another word, Samantha said, "We've got the day off, haven't we...Ok. I'll be working on questions to spring on Washburn."

"Sam...I'm always amazed by your uncanny ability to perceive stuff."

"You do it too, Dave" Samantha replied. "It's a cat thing."

Dave smiled at her. "Rrrrrr" he growled playfully.

Samantha smiled back at him. "Let's go home," she said.

Hidden on a dead-end street in the outskirts of Vaharis' warehouse district was a weather-worn red brick building, situated on an asphalt plot of land. It was surrounded by overgrown holly bushes and numerous storage containers piled one atop the other as if awaiting transport. Towards the back, a wide alleyway divided the warehouse from Hammond Forest; a street lamp beside the building shed a harsh yellow light across the territory.

Hung to the side of the building was a rusty sign that read:

NO TRESPASSING
PROPERTY OF THE NORTENYA REGION

A thin sleet was falling as Governor Victor Ulrich drove up to the warehouse building and parked his car in the alley. The warehouse district was nearly desolate by nightfall.

The asphalt was covered with a mix of snow-melting salt and slush. Ulrich pushed open the unlocked door and stepped inside.

In the dim lit interior of the building, he could see gray figures of five people. He beckoned to them and they followed him down a long corridor, between rows of empty storage units, until they reached an abandoned corner office. They all gathered around a table here. There was a drafty window in this room but since it only looked out onto the back alley and the forest, they felt it was relatively secure to conduct their business transaction.

"I was thinking, you would not come," Ambassador Qiang was the first to speak. He was Asian, dressed in business attire and wearing a red diplomatic sash over one shoulder; he was in his 60's, with neatly combed gray hair.

"Since when have I ever failed to?" Ulrich responded. "Traffic is backed up near the mansion."

"Where is the merchandise?"

Ulrich glanced over at Gorgonio, who snapped his fingers at the other two. "Get them," Gorgonio ordered. Theron and Venancio slipped out into the corridor, leaving Ulrich, Qiang, his bodyguard and Gorgonio temporarily alone in the office.

“You look worried, governor,” observed Qiang. “I hope it is nothing that might affect my business interests.”

"A liability," Ulrich answered. "It seems the wildlife minister, Mr. Landon Washburn, is reluctant to sign the paperwork needed to delist the foxes."

"To be effective, one must learn to eliminate the problem," Qiang said.

The governor thought for a moment. "I believe you're right, Qiang. ...Gorgonio, you'll arrange to bring Washburn here tomorrow so I can discuss the matter with him."

"Done," said Gorgonio.

Ulrich turned his attention back to the diplomat. "And how is the market in Longguo?" he inquired.

"Vibrant," Qiang replied. "Demand is very high among upper class..."

"Well," said Ulrich, "that's good to hear."

"Extremely," Qiang continued, "to the point that my associates in Longguo have requested a greater supply. Of course, it means higher payout for you."

"Consider it done," Ulrich responded.

At this point, the other two hunters returned with a large crate, which they placed atop the table. They proceeded to open it and then stepped back; revealing the contents to Qiang.

Reaching into the crate, Qiang retrieved one of the many arctic fox pelts and ran his fingers along the fur. He glanced up at Ulrich. "Excellent quality." He then lifted the suitcase he had been carrying onto the table, turned it towards Ulrich, and opened it. Inside the suitcase, neatly aligned in rows and in batches, was what appeared to be thousands of dollars in cash.

"Count if you like," said Qiang.

"No need," responded the governor, glancing up from the open suitcase, "You always come through precisely." Taking the suitcase, he smiled and shook Qiang's hand. "Ambassador Qiang, nice doing business with you."

"As always," Qiang replied. "But before I go..." He turned to his bodyguard and said something in a foreign language. The man, who had been carrying a brown cardboard box, handed it to Qiang who in turn handed it to Ulrich.

The governor, appearing a little surprised, opened it and withdrew an arctic fox stole. It was one of the full-length fur stoles with the head and tail attached. There was a clip below the jaw so that it could be fastened.

The ambassador said, "A token of our gratitude for your generous business with us."

When Ulrich nodded his head in thanks, Qiang left the room.

Ulrich placed the stole back in the box and glanced at the hunters, who were standing in silence. He retrieved a manila envelope from the inside of his coat and tossed it onto the table. Gorgonio snatched it and began counting the money inside. Before long, his eyes narrowed and he shoved the cash back into the envelope. "Where's our extra three percent?" he demanded.

"You'll get it when you stop screwing up!" Ulrich retorted. "That damn ranger is still alive. If you can't handle the job, I'll get someone else; I pay for results!"

Venancio spoke up, "We can do it, boss. We'll try again..."

"It doesn't look as if you dimwits even tried!" Ulrich interrupted him. "The news media is saying only half the car was on fire at first and anyone in it would have had plenty of time to escape!"

"Is that a fact?" Gorgonio turned a suspicious, irritated gaze on Theron, who glanced down at the floor. "I'll get the ranger to have a more precise accident."

"Forget that for now," Ulrich answered. "We have more important matters to attend to. I want the number of pelts doubled by next week! Not to mention you have another problem to handle if you expect to redeem yourself. And you had better not mess up..." Giving them a final glare, Ulrich turned around and left.

Outside, padding through the territory, were Ivan and Natasha. The two foxes halted in front of the storage building.

"I bet we can find lots of prey here," added Ivan. "This looks like a place where rodents would..."

"Ivan!" Natasha said, suddenly jerking her mate underneath one of the nearby storage containers, just as three familiar people walked past...

"I can't believe he could have survived!" Gorgonio yelled. The foxes nearly jumped as they recognized him.

"It's just as well," Theron said. The foxes could pick up a sense of relief from him. "We're trappers...we're supposed to be after animals, not people."

Gorgonio turned around to face him. "As far as I'm concerned, there's no difference" he said, "except that there's more of a thrill to big game."

Venancio broke in. "We'll have to make sure we get the job done right, next time, or we won't get paid."

"We'll have to make sure Theron gets the job done right, next time," Gorgonio corrected, with a seething look at the younger hunter. "What's this bullshit about only half of the car being in flames?"

"It was a mistake! It won't happen again," Theron said.

Gorgonio suddenly whipped out a switchblade and held it to Theron's throat. Theron tried to back away, but he found himself pushed against the storage containers. The foxes, hidden underneath, flattened themselves even more to the ground. "Theron, I have had it with your hesitation! Maybe Venancio's right about you being soft. Let me just tell you that it's in your best interest to put your electrical know-how to practical use...!"

It was at this point the sound of snow crackling and a very faint squeak was heard. The hunters glanced down to see what appeared to be a tiny round puff of orange-brown fur beside Gorgonio, looking up at him with black eyes and twitching cream whiskers. It squeaked at him.

With one swift movement, keeping the knife at Theron's throat, Gorgonio kicked the little rodent so hard that it was knocked into a nearby snow bank. The pile of snow fell on top of it.

Gorgonio turned his harsh glare back at Theron. "Do I make myself clear, Theron?"

Theron found himself nearly breathless from fear, but he managed to say, "Yeah."

Gorgonio closed the switchblade and glanced at the snowbank where the rodent had vanished. "Fucking lemmings," he muttered as he walked off.

The sky had a white appearance, as if it were going to snow, and the two older hunters walked away. It was apparent that the head of the group was Gorgonio, who seemed to enjoy bullying the other two and was the meanest. Venancio seemed money hungry and Theron was the quietest, speaking only when absolutely necessary.

"What are they doing here?" Ivan whispered, staring towards the gate. "Could they also be using this territory to cross from the forest into the city and back?"

"I'm not sure," answered Natasha, "but I don't want to stick around any longer. Come on."

Quickly, the two foxes fled into the woods.

Theron, lingering behind, did not notice the critters. He felt as if he were in a daze. It was not merely the futility of his protest; it was knowing Gorgonio was more than capable, entirely willing to carry out his threats, as if cruelty were his thrill. Theron felt sorry for the lemming Gorgonio had kicked. Trying to ignore it, he slowly walked after the other two hunters.

As Theron left, the lemming hopped out of the snow bank, its whiskers still twitching. Watching the hunters leave with an inscrutable gaze, it let out another squeak.

Samantha stared out the cabin window at the falling sleet, which was gradually turning into snow. Behind her she could hear Geronimo, who was atop the table chatting about his adventures. "...we were dangling off the edge of the cliff with these huge, raging whirlpools in the water below, and..."

"You were dangling off the edge of a cliff?" Dave repeated incredulously. "Ger...we know you like to exaggerate, but come on."

"It's true!" Geronimo hissed. "And we were being shot at!"

Samantha turned around. "Shooting at you? ...how on earth did you manage to get out of that situation?"

"We took a gigantic leap to the nearby bridge!" Geronimo pounced off the table with a happy growl.

"I know what area he's talking about...the Whirlpool River. And the bridge must be the one we cross every time we're going into the city." Samantha said.

She glanced out the window and sitting outside were the two arctic foxes. "Our guests have arrived...be right back." Samantha got some cat food and opened the cabin door. "Hi Ivan, Hi Natasha. You like seafood, don't you?"

"We love it!" replied Natasha.

"Thank you," Ivan said.

Samantha placed the dishes on the porch and then turned to head into the cabin, when she stopped and looked back at the two foxes. They were watching her with big amber eyes.

"It's very cold out here," Samantha said at last. "Would you like to..."

Before she could even finish, the foxes zipped into the cabin.

Samantha couldn't suppress a smile as she picked up the dishes and stepped back inside. She closed the door and Geronimo said, "Ask them about it... Ivan! Natasha! Tell them about us being trapped on the edge of that cliff with those hunters shooting at us"

"Absolutely true." Ivan said. "We only managed to escape by leaping to a bridge that was close by."

"What a day!" exclaimed Dave.

Geronimo purred.

"So, then, did you recognize the people that were after you?" asked Samantha.

"It's always the same three," Ivan explained. "We saw them again at the storage place we crossed through to get here."

"...storage place?" Samantha looked interested.

"A regional warehouse," said Ivan.

"They didn't see us, though" Natasha yapped, "but we've seen them so many times, I'd recognize them anywhere."

"Where is that storage place? ...I imagine it's in the warehouse district, but you wouldn't happen to have an address, would you?"

"No, sorry...we critters use landmarks."

"I guess we'll have to look it up," Samantha said, taking out her notepad and pen.

The foxes stuck their noses into their food dishes and gobbled up the meal. It was obvious that they were very hungry.

"Look how starved they are," Dave remarked to Samantha on the side. "This must be the first good meal they've had in a while."

"Yeah, I feel sorry for them," Samantha replied. "Nevertheless, I bet they have tons of info about this poaching problem that no one else does...or that no one else wants to say."

"We just need to figure out, how to verify what they're telling us," Dave told the reporter.

"Of course Dave," Samantha replied. "But, I do feel a sense of urgency with this investigation, although I can't quite put my finger on the reason...there seems to be a missing piece to this story."

When the arctic foxes finished eating, they all gathered around the coffee table to talk about the day's events. Ivan and Natasha told the humans what they had heard the hunters say that evening.

"Did they actually say they were going after 'people'?" interrupted Samantha.

"Yes," answered Ivan, "What's more, they mentioned getting money, which if I understand correctly, is important in human society."

"Yeah, it's important" Dave jumped in, "Unfortunately, some people place more importance in it than it merits."

Geronimo leaned against Samantha's legs and purred. She stroked the cat's head and said, "Kitty, I never doubted your story...I just thought maybe you embellished it a little."

"Yeah Ger," added Dave, "You've got to admit, your life has been quite exciting."

The cat purred even louder and squinted his eyes.

Samantha and Dave noticed that the snow outside was beginning to come down harder and the temperature was dropping to sub-zero levels; feeling reluctant to let the two foxes out to face the arctic weather, they invited them to spend the night at the cabin, to which Ivan and Natasha readily agreed.

Everyone slept soundly that night. The foxes started out sleeping downstairs, until Geronimo told them about the bed upstairs, and the whole lot of critters piled onto the bed with Samantha and Dave.

The next morning, the weather was clear. After breakfast, the two arctic foxes returned to the woods.

"That was the best meal I've had since last summer!" Natasha yapped as they walked back to their den.

"I must admit, it's hard to believe how different Geronimo's humans are from those hunters," said Ivan.

"There's good and bad of everything, I suppose," Natasha replied.

As they were emerging from the bracken, Natasha gasped suddenly. Pawsteps away was their den...encircled by the three poachers. Venancio and Theron tore through it as Gorgonio stood on the side, ordering them around.

The foxes backed away quietly and hid in the bushes to observe them.

"Tear it up, completely!" Gorgonio said. "This'll flush them into the open again."

Watching from behind the bushes, Natasha repeated, despondently, "Good...and bad."

"My God," said Ivan, "If we hadn't been at Geronimo's den last night..."

"Let's get out of here" Natasha interrupted; and the two scampered off into the woods.

Gorgonio briefly turned away from what had been the foxes' makeshift den, to notice a line of small prints in the snow. He snapped his fingers at the other two hunters, then bent down to get a closer look. He was very good at identifying pawprints; these, with their dainty, catlike trail and doglike marks, were unmistakable to a seasoned trapper. Gorgonio's eyes glittered.

"Arctic fox tracks."

He glanced up. They led halfway to the den, then turned to retreat back into the bushes.

Venancio peered over his shoulder and said, "We must've scared them off."

Ignoring the statement, Gorgonio swung his rifle over his shoulder and said, "Come on. We'll catch up to them."

As he and Venancio set off after the foxes, Theron was bringing up the rear. He dragged his feet through the snow, silently thinking.

Their home is destroyed again. How must they feel?

Theron was having second thoughts but shook his head and marched on; he was very deep into this and didn't know how to get out of it alive.

Chapter 9 - Integrity and Humanity

Last night's snowfall had been cleared from the roads already, so the drive into the city was swift. As the WCAT news van was crossing over the Whirlpool River bridge, the reporters chatted about their options for the day.

"Damn it. I miss my morning cup of coffee. If I hadn't gotten up late, I would've had time to make it." commented Samantha.

"That’s ok." answered Dave. "I'm sure they have coffee ready at the station. We can grab it there."

"Purrrrrrr..." A sound arose from the back of the van and drew closer to where the pair was.

Both journalists turned to see Geronimo perched in between their two seats, purring loudly.

"Geronimo!" Samantha exclaimed.

Dave had turned his attention back onto the road. "Well, we'd better figure out how to explain Geronimo's presence in the news van and hope Gao is as understanding as Ted."

When the journalists and their cat walked into the newsroom, they found Gao had called a meeting of the affiliate's news staff. There was someone familiar there, too...

"Ted!" Samantha cheerfully greeted their editor.

"West and Candid," Ted replied. "I was hoping you two would drop by."

"When did you arrive on the mainland?" Dave asked.

"Last night. I got a call from Governor Ulrich's secretary," said Ted. "It seems the governor has something he urgently wants to discuss."

"Related to our investigation?" Samantha questioned.

"Maybe. Speaking of which, how goes the digging?"

"Turns out there's a poaching problem going on with the arctic foxes," explained Samantha. "We asked Ulrich what he thought about it, but all he said was that he'd order an investigation."

"So basically, it's just the ranger says this and the governor says that," Ted said.

"Not exactly. We checked fox population records to see who they'd agree with."

"And..."

"The records show that the species population is extremely low. On the verge of extinction."

"That sounds suspicious."

"Cover-up?" Samantha straightforwardly asked.

"Perhaps. Have you gone back to ask Ulrich?"

"We did. He started out by saying that another study had been done which said the foxes had recovered, but then became evasive and threw us out of his office. It looks like the entire thing about a fox population explosion was a lie."

"That's what's so weird," added Dave, "Why would Ulrich go through that whole shit of even calling a conference, to announce lies?"

"Bribery, methinks" said Samantha.

"I saw your report on the car explosion," Ted acknowledged. "It looks like organized crime, but you can't prove that yet. You've got a story about Ulrich's apparent disagreement with the records, though. What's the Ministry of Wildlife say?"

"We've got an interview with the wildlife minister scheduled for today at 11:30," Samantha announced.

"Good. You need to get a statement from him on this fox thing. Also, you two are covering Ulrich's re-election campaign; if he is corrupt, it's a good excuse to keep an eye on him."

"Right," Samantha answered. "I'd like to get that investigative report about the foxes on the News at Noon."

"Only if you can get a statement from the wildlife minister by then," cautioned Ted.

"Until the interview, both of you should brush up on the governor's campaign," Gao added. "There's footage in our archives about both candidates that should bring you up-to-date on Nortenya politics."

"Who's on the follow-up to the car explosion?" Dave asked.

"We are," chimed in another reporter, gesturing to herself and a photographer.

A whirring noise suddenly ended with the whack of a paw against paper, and they all looked to see Geronimo, his back arched, hissing at a fax machine.

"Geronimo, stop notarizing those press releases!" Samantha exclaimed. She gave a quick glance to Gao and a small smile. "We can explain," she said.

"You don't have to," Gao brushed it off. "Ted has told me anecdotes about our unofficial mascot."

The meeting ended, Samantha went over to Geronimo and retrieved the paper from the fax machine. It had five small rips where Geronimo's claws had punctured the paper.

"I don't blame you Ger...I get frustrated with all that PR shit too," Dave spoke up.

Todd, one of the other reporters, looked at it over Samantha's shoulder. "Hey, this might make a good feature story, though. Maybe I can convince Gao to let me cover it for the broadcast, if you guys aren't interested."

Samantha handed him the press release, and as he walked to the adjacent desk, Samantha remarked, "We've got a lot on our plate with the arctic fox story. What are you covering today?"

"Some theft of chloroform from the Vaharis hospital... I wonder what they're naming the baby panda," he added off-topic, still reading through the press release.

Samantha could not contain her surprise. "Chloroform? Why would anyone want that?"

"I don't know, but a source of mine at the police station says in the wrong hands that stuff can be dangerous," said Todd. "What I find more interesting is the fact that someone can just walk into a hospital and make off with a controlled substance, and apparently not even get caught on camera."

"What's chloroform?" Geronimo mewed.

"A general anesthetic," answered Samantha. "It makes you pass out if you breathe it."

"Sounds like you've got a mini expose," Dave said happily.

Todd filed the press release away and began typing out a preliminary report at his desk. "They're all going to point fingers and blame each other."

"They always do," Samantha replied.

The reporter and her cameraman walked over to the coffee machine, followed by Geronimo. "Can I have coffee?" he purred.

"No, you're a kitty," said Samantha.

"Humans hog all the good food," Geronimo hissed. "No coffee, no chocolate...only canned and dry kibble for us critters."

"If it was up to you, you'd have a mocha drink," Samantha replied, pouring out the coffee into one of the mugs with the station's logo. "Leandra says this stuff isn't healthy for cats."

"Excuses," Geronimo flattened his ears.

Dave was watching the television next to the coffee machine. It was set to one of their competitors, Channel 13, and their morning news program. However, they were currently on a commercial break; one of Ulrich's political advertisements came on the screen. It was criticizing his opponent in the election, and extolling what Ulrich promised to do if re-elected.

"When's the election?" asked Dave.

"In two months," replied Samantha.

The advertisement ended with the governor's campaign slogan: "Re-Elect Governor Ulrich! Integrity and Humanity!"

Landon Washburn arrived at his office around 9 in the morning and spent about an hour or so there before leaving for the TV interview. From his office at the Ministry of Wildlife's headquarters in Sarrilla's national capital, it would be at least a one hour drive to arrive at Vaharis.

On the way out, he told his secretary, "I'm leaving for the day. Take all my messages...oh and by the way, if you like, you can leave at 3."

"Oh, thank you sir," she replied.

When he exited the building, the air outside was freezing cold and sparse snowflakes carried on the wind. He walked to his car and as he was fumbling around with the keys, a hand came up from behind with a handkerchief and covered his nose and mouth. As Washburn reached up, another hand emerged and grabbed him by the neck. He struggled but felt himself getting weaker and weaker as the sweet scent of chloroform took effect. It took only a moment for Washburn to pass out.

Meanwhile, back in Vaharis, Ted drove up the driveway at the governor's mansion. A security guard met him as he got out of the car and Ted showed him his press ID. "I have an appointment with Governor Ulrich."

"That's fine, sir." said the guard, "Right through those doors, straight down the hall you'll find elevators. Go up to the second floor."

Ted took the elevator up and walked down the hall to an entryway. There was a secretary here, seated at a desk.

As the lady looked up at him, Ted introduced himself. "Oh, yes, Mr. Hughes" the lady replied, "The Governor has been waiting for you. Just one moment and I'll let him know you're here."

Having said that, she got up and walked through a doorway that was behind her.

About five minutes passed and she returned. "You may go in now, sir" she said smiling.

Ted crossed a small foyer and saw another door that was ajar. "Come in," a voice said.

As Ted walked in, he saw Ulrich seated at a desk. "Have a seat." he said to Ted. "Thank you for coming, Mr. Hughes."

Ted sat down. "Yes, well, I sensed some urgency on your part, governor."

"I'll get straight to the point." Ulrich said. "I presume that you are the top news editor at WCAT Channel 8?"

"Yes, I am in charge."

"...and Miss Samantha West is one of your employees?"

"She is."

"How long have you employed her?"

Ted gave him an annoyed look. "What did she do?"

"She tried to pressure me to answer questions and when I refused to answer, she turned my statements out of context to make it seem as if I was a liar! Then, when I told her and the photographer to leave, she argued they had a right to stay; with the camera rolling no less!"

"Anything else?"

"I've told you plenty!"

"Governor Ulrich," said Ted, "all you've said just confirms what I've always said about Samantha West...she's an excellent reporter, devoted to her work..."

"If you're condoning this kind of sensational, ratings-hungry journalism, Mr. Hughes, I'd remind you that I have the option to sue your station in court if that film is aired."

"True...you do have that option, however, as a public figure you would never win. Why don't you want the film aired?" Ted asked, taking out a notepad.

"I didn't call you here for an interview, Mr. Hughes."

"What did you want to say?"

"No comment," Ulrich said. "The door's behind you. Leave."

"Gladly," responded Ted as he got up and left the office. "There was no need for me to travel such a long distance."

Ulrich didn't answer. He was shuffling through several papers that were in front of him.

Ted was so angry, that he didn't notice Mabel passing by. He bumped into her.

"I'm so sorry, madam...I was in a hurry," Ted said.

"That's quite all right, it has happened to me too," Mabel smiled at him.

"I was on my way out. I guess I'm having a busy day," Ted continued.

"Well, if you just met with the Governor, then I'm not surprised that you feel tense," answered Mabel.

"Oh? Do you work for the governor?" asked Ted.

Mabel had a surprised look on her face when she realized that he had not recognized her. She smiled and said, "Actually...I'm his wife."

Ted looked at her for a while, not knowing what to say. "I work for WCAT News; I'm the editor on Tropical Island. He said he wanted to speak with me, but as it turns out it was just a complaint."

"Victor does that sometimes. He forgets that people have other things to do." Mabel countered.

"I apologize, Mrs. Ulrich... I didn't want to upset you."

"Oh no...it's ok."

They shook hands and Mabel turned to go up the stairs. "Have a good day," she said.

"You too," answered Ted.

As Ted walked down the hallway and to the elevators, he thought about Mabel and mumbled to himself, "What a remarkable looking woman. It's hard to believe that such a gentle soul is married to such an arrogant man like Victor Ulrich."

The office of the regional treasurer was on the same floor as that of the governor. Denise Ralston crossed with Ted as she was exiting the elevator, and she walked over to her office. She got a call a while later from Ulrich's secretary.

"Hello, Ms. Ralston?"

"Yes? What is it?"

"Governor Ulrich would like to see you in his office at your earliest convenience."

"I take that to mean today?"

"Yes, that's his preference."

"Very well. I'll be there within an hour."

"Thank you Ms. Ralston; I'll let him know."

Denise hung up without any further conversation. "Fuck," she muttered, "and I was hoping for a short work day. What could he possibly want?"

Forty-five minutes passed and Denise headed towards Ulrich's office.

When she walked through the door, Ulrich was standing behind his desk with a large gift box wrapped in plain brown paper, and fiddling a cigarette between his fingers.

"I think you might like this," he said, handing her the box and sitting down.

Denise grabbed the box and without hesitation, tore off the brown paper and opened it.

"Why Victor, it's stunning!" Denise Ralston swung the arctic fox stole about her neck. "And arctic fox! Won't the other women at the country club be so envious..."

"You can't tell anyone it's real arctic fox fur," Governor Ulrich reminded her.

Denise gave him a quick, almost affronted, glare. "Victor, you really don't think I would wear anything but real furs, do you?"

"Well, then, say it's dyed red fox, but don't let anyone know it's arctic." Ulrich insisted. "Remember, we haven't gotten those animals off the endangered species list yet."

"We're going to," Denise said, "All right then...dyed red fox."

The phone on Ulrich's desk rang and he answered it. "Ulrich speaking."

Gorgonio was on the other line. "It's done."

"I'll be there right away," Ulrich replied, putting out his cigarette in the ashtray.

He hung up the phone, grabbed his coat from the coat rack and headed towards the door.

"Where are you going?" asked Denise in surprise.

"I'll be back later, I've got things to do," he answered, and left.

To Roxanne, the entire city of Vaharis was her territory. A domain so vast, of course, could not be patrolled in one day - and especially not now in the wintertime, when the weather could be both fickle and unrelenting - so she did so in parts, varying her distance and pace according to her own and the climate's whims.

It happened that today she was prowling around the warehouse district, a section of the city that not only had plenty of hiding-places for cats but was also prey-rich. She was stalking a mouse when a car pulled up. This scared the rodent off; Roxanne hissed and looked up to see who had spoiled her hunt.

She saw two men who she recognized to be Gorgonio and Venancio half-carrying another man towards a warehouse; but she was really interested when she saw Governor Ulrich arrive in his car.

The cat crouched down flat, but Ulrich had not noticed her. He got out of the car and went into the building.

Roxanne padded across the alley from the forest and stopped at the 'No Trespassing' sign. It was the regional warehouse. Roxanne knew this place - she knew the history and inside layouts of most of the region's property. The warehouse had been left to fall into disrepair, yet officially was still in use. She could only surmise what Ulrich could be doing here. Roxanne crawled underneath one of the holly bushes near the door and pawed at the snow here until she found an opening that led into the building. She snuck in.

She emerged into one of the abandoned storage units and observed Ulrich walk by, crossing with Venancio who was leaving. Neither one said anything, and no one saw Roxanne.

The cat followed Ulrich at a distance. They walked down the grey, dungeon-like corridors until he turned and entered one of the storage units here. Roxanne paused for a moment, but decided to creep forward and see what was going on.

Her eyes glowed in the darkness, and she saw the man Gorgonio and Venancio had brought seated in a chair here. Gorgonio stood beside the chair.

Washburn began to stir, and Ulrich reached up, turning on a lightbulb that hung from the ceiling. The blinding glare made the wildlife minister flinch and shut his eyes again, but his eyesight began to focus slowly and he began assimilating his surroundings. The sight of Gorgonio and Ulrich, coupled with the shadowy, windowless room he was in, made a sudden terror come over him.

"Where am I?" he questioned.

"Nowhere you can ever be found," responded the governor. "You're here because you've been reluctant to sign these documents," he added, laying the falsified fox population documents on the table before Washburn.

"What you're asking me to do is illegal," Washburn protested. "The foxes can't be delisted. They'd never survive."

"On the contrary, Mr. Washburn," Ulrich said coldly, with a gesture to Gorgonio who proceeded to pull out a revolver, "the foxes will be delisted, with your signature, or else you die."

Roxanne, watching from out in the hallway, flattened her ears as Gorgonio held the gun to Washburn's head; the wildlife minister began pleading.

"No, Ulrich, please! I'll do whatever you say!"

"Sign the documents, Washburn."

Washburn took the pen, but then hesitated fearfully. "...Then, you'll let me go?"

"I give you my word that I won't kill you," Ulrich promised, his voice impassive.

Washburn proceeded to sign the fraudulent documents. He had to steady his hands from shaking. Once he had done so, he handed the paperwork back to Ulrich.

"With this the arctic fox can be delisted?" Ulrich prompted.

"Yes," Washburn answered. His voice sounded defeated. "One copy must be filed at the Capitol records office."

Ulrich looked up and with a sharp nod towards Washburn, said to the hunter, "Kill him."

Ulrich turned to leave, and an astonished, horrified Washburn sprang up, only to be pushed back down into his seat by Gorgonio. "But you said...!"

The Nortenya governor glanced back at him and evenly replied:

"I said I wouldn't kill you."

Washburn was stunned, and just stared at him.

Ulrich nodded a farewell. "Goodbye, Mr. Washburn," he said, and walked out of the room.

"Ulrich, don't do this to me!" the wildlife minister implored.

Roxanne was about to back away when Ulrich came into the corridor. He gave her a mildly curious look and said:

"I hadn't noticed before, but if we dyed your fur white it could pass for fox."

A gunshot made Roxanne jump. Washburn had fallen silent.

"I don't think I'll ever understand human cruelty," she hissed at Ulrich. "You slaughter your own kind."

"You're just a dumb animal," he responded, and walked away. Roxanne, casting one final glance into the storage unit, followed Governor Ulrich outside to his car.

Chapter 10 - A Question Mark

Samantha and Dave arrived at the restaurant where Washburn was supposed to meet them. When they opened the back door of the news van to get their equipment, out jumped a happy Geronimo, tail held high.

"Geronimo!" they both shouted.

"Meowrr, that's me! Prrrrrrrr..." purred the cat.

"How in the world were you able to get in here?" Dave said, surprised. "I barely turned my back when I loaded the cameras."

"It's a cat thing," answered Geronimo.

"Geronimo, try to stay out of trouble...we're in a rush, so we'll meet you here after the interview," said Samantha as she walked away with Dave following close behind.

The Chinese restaurant was one of the upscale establishments on Vaharis' luxurious Brook Avenue, situated alongside elegant casinos and department stores that Samantha could easily imagine might be behind a black-market trade in fox furs. Inside, the journalists were led to their table - they had called to reserve one beforehand - Dave placed the camera on the extra chair and they sat to wait for their interviewee.

The interior of the restaurant was decorated in red and gold, with delicately painted drawings of flowers and legendary Asian animals on the walls. After some time had passed without Washburn arriving, Samantha and Dave decided to go ahead and order their meal. The waiter bowed and left.

"Well, if we have to look at the bright side of this, it has been a while since our last dinner outing," reasoned Samantha.

"That's true," agreed Dave. "We've been so busy lately. Still, I wonder what could be keeping Washburn." He thought for a moment, and then added, "You don't think he went to the competing stations, do you?"

"Damn, I bet Channel 13 is scooping us on this fox thing," Samantha said.

There was a crashing sound from the kitchen, and moments later the cook appeared at the kitchen entrance quarreling with the manager in Chinese. Samantha and Dave both observed the spat from their table; the language, spoken swiftly and fluently, was melodious but nonetheless incomprehensible to Dave. "Sam, you speak Chinese, don't you? What's going on?"

"The rice pot fell on the floor," Samantha easily translated, "and the manager is telling the cook not to be so clumsy; the rice costs money. The cook says he's overworked and the manager is answering that if he doesn't do his job right he'll fire him. The cook says the manager will never find anyone who can cook Asian food better in Nortenya."

Dave seemed pensive but said nothing. He drank a sip of water from one of the goblets, then gave Samantha a questioning look. "How many languages do you know?"

"Oh, several," she brushed it off indifferently.
