The waiter arrived shortly with the main course - General Tso's Chicken - but minus the rice. "Very sorry, the rice will take a bit longer," he told them.

"That's all right," said Samantha.

As soon as the waiter left, Samantha and Dave began eating.

Samantha picked up the chopsticks with a smile on her face. "Hey!" she exclaimed. "Chopsticks! It's been a while that I tried these. ...Dave, you're going to use a fork?"

"Yep, I'm sticking with the tried-and-true...besides, last time I tried chopsticks I could barely pick up anything," replied Dave. He lifted a goblet of water and said, "A toast to my Samantha, the most beautiful, intrepid reporter in Sarrilla. I pledge my eternal love to you."

Samantha grasped her goblet, clicked it with his, and replied, "And to my Dave, I pledge my love to you and I am forever yours."

They continued eating and eventually the waiter brought the rice. A few minutes later, Dave noticed several men enter the restaurant. One of the men seemed strangely familiar.

"What is it, Dave?" asked Samantha, looking in the direction that Dave was.

Dave looked back down at his plate. "One of those guys looks like someone we've seen before, somewhere."

Samantha looked back to Dave, "We've gone so many places and talked to so many people..."

"I know where..." interrupted Dave pensively. "He appears in the background of the closing shot we took outside of the wildlife convention...he was talking to Ulrich."

"Well, well..." said Samantha, "The story seems to be getting better and better."

They finished their meal, paid the bill, and left to head back to the news studio. Washburn had never shown up for the scheduled interview, but now the reporters were intrigued by the person they had seen in the restaurant; and they were determined to find out who he was.

Meanwhile, Geronimo had wandered down the block to a nearby public park. The long stretch of grassland, which was presently snow-covered, was situated near an icy stream that gradually cascaded into the gorge.

The lynx-point tomcat was padding around the park when he heard bushes rustling, and he crouched down. As he listened to the sound, however, he realized that the rustling was not the typical sort that came from prey scurrying about; it was more frantic in nature.

He crept towards the holly bush where it came from and found a small, orange-furred critter clutching a piece of chopped celery. The celery piece was nearly the same size as the pudgy little rodent.

Geronimo watched the critter in bewilderment. The rodent was stuck between two branches and unwilling to drop the celery. It had been struggling to get free, but upon seeing the feline it froze.

On a whim, the cat leaned forward to bite at the branches; the rodent began struggling again until Geronimo hissed, "I'm trying to get you loose! You need to drop the plant."

The rodent gave a muffled squeak; nevertheless, it released its hold on the celery, which allowed Geronimo to gnaw at the branches until it was free.

Now loose, the critter gave another squeak, picked up its piece of celery and ran off without saying anything more. As Geronimo watched it vanish under the roots of a pine tree, he was still utterly perplexed.

A yap cut through his thoughts. "You let food get away!"

Geronimo turned to see Ivan and Natasha standing nearby, their eyes wide.

"I wasn't hungry," Geronimo explained. "Besides, that looks like some kind of hamster. It might be a lost pet."

"That's a lemming," said Natasha.

"That's a lemming?" Geronimo was surprised. "They don't look so vicious."

"They're vicious," Ivan replied simply.

"It's a tiny fluff ball. Imagine that little thing attacking deer. The way you two were talking about them, you'd think they were animals thrice our size." He changed the topic, "What brings you into the city?"

"The hunters," Natasha answered. "They destroyed our den."

"Again?" meowed Geronimo.

Natasha nodded.

Ivan growled, "Survival has become a struggle for us."

"Geronimo!" The cat pricked up his ears when he heard Samantha calling him, and he hurried over with his tail waving; the foxes followed him.

He found his humans at the news van, packing up their camera equipment.

"Come on Ger, we're heading back to the newsroom," said Dave.

"What did the wildlife minister say in the interview?" Geronimo asked eagerly.

"He never showed up. It's odd," Samantha answered. "He seemed to want to talk with the press..." She glanced over at the foxes. "Natasha, Ivan, how are things in the forest?"

Geronimo leapt into her arms before the foxes could reply. "The damn poachers destroyed their den again," he said.

"When?" asked Samantha, with an inquisitive look at the foxes.

"This morning," Natasha explained. "We were going back to our den and found the hunters there. They must have spied us, because the next thing we knew we were on the run again. We managed to lose them at a riverbank."

"Couldn't they come live with us at the cabin?" Geronimo mewed.

"Well..." Samantha hesitated. She and Dave looked at each other, and then at the critters. All three animals were giving them a wide-eyed look. The reporter smiled. "All right, as long as we're in Nortenya."

Geronimo purred and rubbed his head against her face. "See, didn't I tell you they were good humans?" he told the foxes.

The three critters piled into the back of the news van, and as Samantha and Dave got into the vehicle they all peeked out happily. "This has got to count as some kind of conflict of interest," Samantha remarked to Dave, "We're taking care of two critters involved in a plight we're covering."

Dave shrugged. "What else can we do? Besides, the hunting is illegal; there's not much that can be disputed about that."

"That's true, and it's also true that in many respects they've been acting as sources. I guess we should find some way to help them," Samantha considered.

The critters were ambivalent to their dilemma. "Let's put music!" purred Geronimo, pawing at the car radio.

"What's that?" asked Ivan.

"A radio," said Geronimo. "It's like a TV without pictures."

"I'm hungry," yapped Natasha.

"We're going to the office; there's food there," said Dave.

Governor Ulrich had arrived back at the governor's mansion. Roxanne had returned in the car with him, sitting in the passenger seat, to the governor's vocal chagrin.

"You worthless animal." Ulrich's scorn was undisguised. He parked the car, and as he opened the door and stepped outside with Roxanne hopping out after him, he continued uncaringly: "If this wasn't an election year I might just tell Gorgonio to do away with you. You're not even a purebred animal. The only reason I tolerate you is for my public image."

"Not even for Mabel?" questioned Roxanne.

"You know fully well I only married Mabel for her inheritance," the governor dismissed her.

"Is that why you spend nights away with Denise?" Roxanne growled.

"None of your fucking business," he replied.

He walked off quickly and the cat sat in the pathway, watching as he stepped into the building. Mabel shouldn't be with him, thought the cat, that poor human of mine seems to be stuck and she's so kind to me. I should do something to help her. An idea crossed her mind, and she began to purr.

There must be a reason why Denise never wants anyone to go into her office, she thought.

Roxanne went inside the mansion and went up to the regional offices. She found Denise's office and strolled in.

Denise’s office was past her secretary’s desk, and down a corridor. It was neat, though not as expansive as the governor’s, with a window behind the desk and bookshelves full of financial reports to the left of the doorway. Denise was not here.

Roxanne caught sight of something white and fluffy draped over the back of the treasurer's office chair and she hopped up on the desk to inspect it.

It looked like a fox, but it was limp. Roxanne extended a paw and poked it. She sprang back, her back arched, as it fell onto the chair in a heap.

It was still motionless, and she sniffed it carefully, finally jumping on the chair next to it. Confirming that it was a fox skin and not a live animal, she grabbed it and hopped down from the chair. "Just wait until Mabel sees this," the cat mewed, her voice muffled through the plush fox fur.

As Roxanne padded out of the office, the fox stole dragging behind her, Denise was coming up the hallway. She saw the cat.

"Why you, thief!" Denise exclaimed.

Roxanne flattened her ears and ran off, still carrying the fur. Denise chased her and turning the corner, nearly collided with none other than Mabel.

Roxanne, still not letting go of the fox stole, spun around and hissed.

"Roxanne...What do you have there, dear?" asked Mabel.

Before the cat had a chance to answer, Denise spoke up. "Your little dear took my fur stole. I wonder how many more things she's taken."

"My cat never steals...unlike some humans," said Mabel, taking it from her cat. As she handed it over to Denise, she noticed it was real fur. Fox fur. Denise practically snatched it from her and replied, "What's that supposed to mean?"

"If the shoe fits, wear it," answered Mabel.

Denise felt enraged but said nothing as she left curtly with the fox stole. Who cares what she thinks, she thought. She hasn't got any power to do anything.

When Denise had gone, Mabel addressed the cat. "Okay, what's going on, Roxanne? Why were you carrying around that fur stole?"

"That's just it, madam. Fox. Now that the governor is so hell-bent on delisting them, that bitch starts wearing fox fur? I hate to be the bearer of bad news, but...Victor has been cheating on you with Denise. I bet he gave her that piece of fur. Damn them both," concluded the cat.

Mabel sighed. "I've known about the affair for quite a while and I've been thinking about my options. I can either divorce him or not, and if I do, should I do so before or after the elections? But...this thing with the fur is strange, and knowing Victor, I wouldn't be surprised if he's doing something illegal."

"All the more reason to get out of this marriage, the sooner the better," meowed Roxanne.

"Well," said Mabel, "Try to stay out of her way. Come on, let's go have a snack."

"I'll be with you in a few minutes," answered the cat.

"Ok," replied Mabel. She wondered why the cat wasn't eager to go after a meal, but she didn't worry. "Don't take too long," she smiled at the cat, and the cat purred.

Meanwhile, Denise had returned to her office and no sooner had she gone in, than Ulrich appeared at the doorway.

"You're back soon," she mentioned.

“I’m coming to get those reports that I asked you for three days ago,” replied Ulrich.

Denise gathered some papers and held them out to him. Ulrich walked through the doors, took hold of the papers and turned to leave.

“You certainly are rushed,” remarked Denise. “I wondered where you had gone to earlier. You didn’t have anything listed in your planned schedule.”

"I had someone eliminated. One less problem to worry about," he said.

"Who?"

"Washburn. He was the wildlife minister."

Denise took out a cigarette from a small wooden box on her desk and lit it. She took a puff and said, "Let's see how long before it gets on the news."

Ulrich took the cigarette from her lips, took a long drag on it, and returned it to her.

"I have paperwork to finish," he said plainly, and walked out of the office.

Chapter 11 - Discovery

Samantha and Dave walked into the newsroom with the cat and the two foxes parading proudly behind them. This elicited no reaction from their editor, Ted. He was used to the unpredictable, especially from these two.

"First Geronimo and now two arctic foxes?" Ted wryly said.

"Ted, there's an explanation..." Samantha began.

Ted didn't let her finish. "Good work, both of you. An interview with two of the poaching victims will make for an interesting segment." He gestured to the foxes. "How did you find them?"

"I met them in the woods," Geronimo piped up.

Samantha felt slightly embarrassed that she hadn't thought of interviewing them for the broadcast. "In full disclosure, their den was destroyed and they're going to be living with us at the lodge."

"That's fine; they're critters," said Ted. "How'd the interview go?"

"Washburn didn't come," Samantha responded.

"We saw someone there who looked familiar, though," Dave added. "We're going to look through the archives and see what we can dig up on him."

"While you're at it, look for verifiable and still-newsworthy dirt on Ulrich," Ted told them. "The son of a bitch called me all the way over from Tropical Island to complain about your news coverage."

Samantha and Dave left Ivan and Natasha in the newsroom, where the foxes were being petted and fed by their colleagues, and went in search of the tape. Geronimo tagged after them.

They found it swiftly and went to the viewing room to play the tape back. They paused the film at Samantha's sign-off and, zooming in on the monitor, were able to clearly see Governor Ulrich speaking with the man they had seen at the restaurant.

"I wonder who he is and what they were discussing," Samantha said.

"That sash he's wearing looks official," Dave considered.

The mainland editor, Devon Gao, came over to them and handed them a paper. "Press release from the governor's campaign office; it's his speaking schedule."

"Thanks," said Samantha, and then asked, "By the way, were trying to figure out who this guy is. Would you know?"

"That's the ambassador of Longguo, Qiang Xue" Gao answered, and hurried on his way.

Samantha and Dave stared at the screen, neither one saying anything, until at last Geronimo broke the silence.

"So what? He's a foreign official; aren't they sometimes guests at these types of conferences?"

"That's the thing - he wasn't at the conference" Dave answered.

Samantha, her green eyes locked on the screen, whispered:

"Dave, this is bigger than we ever could have imagined."

They walked back to the desk, still astounded. "It's international news," Dave stated.

"The fact the diplomat was speaking to Ulrich outside, where supposedly no one would notice, instead of coming into the convention center means something." Samantha sat down at the desk. "If we can just prove the connection between Ambassador Qiang and Governor Ulrich..."

"You might even win an award!" Geronimo purred. "What's that journalism award they give out called?"

"The Ribbon of Truth," Samantha replied, "and the point of investigating isn't to win awards. The point is to let the truth be known."

"But if you can get a ribbon even better," Geronimo squinted.

"You just want a ribbon," smiled Samantha.

"A ball of yarn would be great too," added the cat.

The phone rang just then and Samantha answered it. "WCAT news office. Samantha West speaking."

"Hello, Ms. West?" A female voice came on the other line. "You're investigating the arctic fox poaching, aren't you?"

Samantha motioned to Dave, who asked, "What's wrong?"

She did not answer him, but continued with the telephone call.

"Yes...do you know any information about it?"

"I know enough," the lady replied.

"Like what?"

"Ms. West," said the lady, "I could give you the year's biggest expose and start an international incident."

By now, Dave had moved to Samantha's side and was listening right along with her at the telephone receiver. He could barely believe what he was hearing. Samantha was more motivated than ever to get to the bottom of things. "An international incident with who?"

When the other line remained silent, Samantha asked, "Longguo?"

"That's right," the lady spoke up. "I'm glad to see the free press doing its job well."

"We try. Are the furs being shipped abroad?"

The lady hesitated. "I want to tell you everything...but I don't know if I should."

"Why?"

"I...won't tell you over the phone. I'll meet you at the Black Fox Casino, at 2 in the morning."

Samantha was jotting this down in her notepad. "2 in the morning? That's rather early."

"I'm usually out at that time. I'll be near the roulette wheel."

"How will I recognize you?"

"I will say a password...it will be 'Some warm milk on a chilly night like this might be good.'"

"All right. Who am I speaking with, please?"

"A concerned citizen. I work in the governor's mansion."

"Are you worried about losing your job?"

"I'm worried about losing my lives," said the lady, and she hung up.

"'Lives'?" Samantha wondered aloud as the foxes came scampering over.

Samantha had an idea. "Ivan, Natasha, do you think you could show us the warehouse where you saw the poachers last night?"

"Well..." Ivan hesitated.

"Oh, it'll only take a minute," insisted Samantha. "I want to see if there's anything there that might give us more info."

"Like what?"

"Who knows! That's exactly why we should go over and investigate," Samantha declared, her green eyes shining. "Why were the poachers there? What were they doing...?"

"...and who else was involved?" added Dave with a smile.

The foxes sighed. "Geronimo, why did you teach your humans how to give a critter look?" Ivan complained.

"Not my fault! They picked it up themselves," explained the tomcat.

Ted was heading out his office door when his two top reporters caught up with him.

"Ted," said Samantha, "Dave and I are going to see this warehouse building where the poachers were spotted."

"That's fine," replied the editor, "You've got my number if something comes up."

Samantha and Dave got into the news van with the critters and drove off.

Park Ranger Jovan Conway was in the city, shopping for a few items. He felt hungry and noticed a cafeteria, so he headed towards it. As he approached the cafe, he noticed a lady coming from the opposite way. She looked familiar and as she got closer Conway recognized her. She was Mabel, the governor's wife, who he had met earlier. Mabel recognized him too, and smiled.

"Fancy meeting you again," she said.

"Just getting something to eat," answered Conway, letting a smile cross his face. She is a beautiful woman, he thought, opening the door for her as they arrived to the front of the restaurant.

Once inside, the place was crowded. This was a small, cozy place that had been in business for many years and had a reputation for good food.

Mabel heard a meow and looked down. It was Roxanne, her cat.

"Roxanne! I was wondering where you were," she exclaimed, picking her up.

"You have an elegant cat, Mrs. Ulrich," said Conway. "She's really beautiful."

Roxanne purred. She liked him. He would be purrrrfect for my human, she thought.

"Please, call me Mabel," she said. The cat purred louder.

"Only if you call me Jovan," he replied and smiled.

They looked around the place and all seats were occupied, except for one table in the far corner. It was far from the big windows that faced the street but it had sufficient lighting and seemed comfortable. "There's a spot," pointed the cat with her tail.

The cat leapt out of Mabel's arms and ran to it, lying across the top of the table. "Rrrreserved," she growled at anyone who dared approach.

Conway and Mabel placed their food orders at the counter, paid and went over to the table. Roxanne the cat happily jumped down to one of the seats to allow them to place the food on the table. The cat gave Mabel an especially intense look that prompted the lady to say, "Yes kitty, I got you a fish sandwich, minus the condiments."

The cat got immediately to eating, while the pair talked and ate.

Conway and Mabel found that they really got along well, and had a lot in common. They both liked the same music, they both enjoyed taking nature walks, and they were both lonely at times. Mabel confided in Conway that she was considering getting a divorce from the governor, and that, if so, it would most likely be finalized after the election.

An hour went by and the two got up to leave. "I hope I will see you again," said Conway.

"Me too," answered Mabel.

As they left the cafeteria, Conway turning towards the east and Mabel towards the west, they were both thinking about how special the other was, and wondering if destiny had any plans in common for them.

The regional storage facility was a long drive from the TV station. The warehouse district was on the opposite side of the city.

Geronimo, perched on Samantha's lap and watching the outside through the window, silently figured the travel time for a cat by paw to be a few hours. Ivan directed Dave as he drove into the blighted territory, with its shabby factories and abandoned storage buildings. Even in the afternoon, the place was still desolate.

"You turn down this lane here, past the bridge," explained Ivan, gesturing with a paw to the highway that towered above the side of the street. The cars could be heard overhead, but underneath the grey pillars, a long patch of asphalt was shielded from the snow. "The building should be all the way at the end of it."

"Watt Street," observed Dave.

Samantha suddenly noticed something lying motionless under the bridge. "...Dave!"

Her photographer looked over and stopped the news van. The three critters gave perplexed mews and yaps as the reporter and her cameraman jumped out of the car. Dave grabbed his camera and ran after Samantha who by now had reached the man lying on the ground.

Samantha looked at him with surprise. "Mr. Washburn!"

"He looks like he still might be breathing," said Dave.

The police and an ambulance arrived swiftly and as they placed Washburn on a gurney for transport to the hospital, police officers questioned the two journalists. Samantha and Dave decided to follow the ambulance to the hospital, but first they dropped off the critters in front of the TV station.

"Geronimo, you know what floor the newsroom is on," Samantha told the tomcat. "You three go there. We'll be back as soon as we're done with our report."

"Ok," meowed Geronimo.

Samantha had called their editor shortly after finding Washburn and at the WCAT television station their colleagues ran to get the information on the air; before long the competing stations picked up on it. Breaking news bulletins pre-empted the shows that were typically playing at this time, and reporters in the nation's capital were waiting for a statement from the Sarrillian prime minister, James Tresser.

Mr. Landon Washburn, as the Minister of Wildlife, was on the same level as the ministers in charge of defense, commerce, and so forth; in his position, appointed by the prime minister, he oversaw all of Sarrilla's wildlife and natural resources, hence his being found severely injured was the lead story in newspapers and newscasts everywhere in the nation.

Samantha and Dave were the first journalists at the hospital, so they got the best location to park the news van and set up their camera equipment. Ted arrived soon after, as they were waiting for their cue.

"Hi Ted," said Samantha, waving at him.

"West, Candid, you two go ahead with the broadcast," Ted quickly directed. "I'm going inside to keep an eye on what's happening with Washburn. I'll come over if there are any new developments."

Watching them from his car was the police chief, Carson Meadows, who had taken a lunch break. The media frenzy had not yet arrived, besides Samantha and Dave, and they were too immersed in their live report to notice him at the moment.

When his cell phone rang, he checked the caller ID before answering it. It was Governor Ulrich.

"Meadows, it's Ulrich. I saw the news on Washburn."

"Yeah," answered the police chief, "It's terrible, isn't it?"

"Do you know where the two journalists who found Washburn are?"

"Sure, I can see them standing over there. I think they're televising right now."

"Chief Meadows, I want that television reporter and her cameraman arrested on charges of attempting to murder the wildlife minister. When he dies, charge them with murder."

"The TV reporters?" Meadows was flabbergasted. "Those charges will never stick on them. It's ludicrous."

"They were going to interview him, weren't they?"

"Yes..."

"They met him, only instead of interviewing him they shot him. She wanted a story that would make her famous, so she concocted this cruel scheme and her photographer went along with her. Work with it."

"I thought I would just proceed with the usual investigation."

"Not this one."

There was uneasy silence. Ulrich spoke again, "You will get your set price."

"Done." answered Meadows, and hung up.

Samantha had finished the initial half of her report and was standing in front of the camera, watching the footage she and Dave had taped and edited earlier play on the monitor screen.

"I hope Washburn will be ok," Dave said.

"So do I," agreed Samantha. "I wouldn't be a bit surprised if this has to do with the arctic fox poaching. He did say he had info about the foxes."

Samantha pressed her hand against the earpiece as the police chief came over.

"You two are under arrest for the attempted murder of Mr. Landon Washburn," Meadows announced.

Samantha and Dave both appeared confused, and Samantha briefly glanced at the camera before she asked, "What? What evidence do you have?"

"If you don't shut up, I'll have you incarcerated for disrespecting authority as well!" he snapped.

Still appearing confused, Samantha removed the earpiece and handed the microphone to Dave, only to have Meadows seize her with handcuffs.

"I'm coming along. Is this necessary?" she evenly asked.

"I told you to shut up and do as I say," he retorted and looked over at Dave. The photographer was still standing behind the TV camera, which he had turned to point at them. Meadows pulled him away from the camera and put handcuffs on him as well, before happening to glance down at the monitor. It displayed the image of the three of them; Meadows and the captive Samantha and Dave. He glanced from the monitor to the camera and then at the journalists.

"Why are we on there?" was the only thing Meadows could say.

"Because you're arresting us in the middle of a live broadcast," Samantha answered, holding herself back from adding, stupid.

Over at the governor's mansion, Ulrich covered his face with a hand disapprovingly. He was watching the news on channel 8.

"First Gorgonio can't kill him and now Meadows can't arrest these people without publicizing it," the governor muttered. "Why am I surrounded by morons?"

Chapter 12 - Jailed Journalists

The sight of the TV reporter and her cameraman being dragged into the police station was enough to make everyone in the hectic place do a double-take. The secretary was particularly astonished. "Isn't that Samantha West, from TV?"

Someone there who was also arrested gave a wolf-whistle and shouted, "Extra, extra!" but when Samantha whipped around with a glare the room hushed.

"Don't we get a phone call?" asked Dave.

"This is an outrage," Samantha said. "It's an infringement on our rights as press under the Sarrillian constitution..."

"Tell it to your lawyer because not even the judge'll care," Meadows responded and ushered them to one of the holding cells.

"When do we get our lawyer?" asked Dave.

"We didn't hurt Washburn," insisted Samantha. "We never even got to meet with him! Who told you to arrest us? It's because of our investigative reporting, isn't it?"

"You journalists always want to think it's retaliation, don't you? You think too highly of yourselves," Meadows snapped.

"Aren't you going to remove the handcuffs?" asked Dave.

"When you're taken out to be photographed and fingerprinted," Meadows answered, pushing them into the cage and adding smugly, "There's an hour-long backlog."

"Our television station is going to have a field day with you!" Samantha hissed.

"Don't think your being a celebrity is going to save you from the firing squad if Washburn dies," Meadows scoffed and walked away.

"'Celebrity'?!" Samantha exclaimed. "The nerve, as if I were a commercial spokeswoman or something!"

"Chill, Sam," Dave tried to soothe.

"I have a headache," Samantha said, sitting down on the bench.

As Chief Meadows was walking away, Detective Hartcourt came walking in. He took one look at the jailed journalists and turned disbelievingly to the police chief. "Those people are press," he told him.

"What of it?" asked Meadows.

"What in the world did they do?" Hartcourt inquired.

"Who cares?" Meadows defiantly responded.

"You're going to have members of the media everywhere in here once they hear their colleagues are jailed," Hartcourt pointed out. "They're going to be saying the Vaharis police force is like the Longguo state police."

"I'm the police chief," Meadows said, "not you."

Hartcourt didn't respond, but when Meadows walked off the detective told Samantha, "Please don't villify the whole department. There are a lot of honest, decent police officers working here."

"Is Chief Meadows neither honest nor decent?" asked Samantha.

"Off the record?" asked Hartcourt in a whisper.

Before anyone could say anything more, Ted walked in.

"Ted!" Dave said.

"One of our producers called me, and said you two had been arrested on the air," Ted said. "I had to see it for myself, because I couldn't believe that the Vaharis Police Department would be so stupid."

"Who might you be?" Meadows snapped.

"Ted Hughes, the managing editor of WCAT-TV," Ted replied.

"Mr. Hughes, your employees are facing some serious charges," Meadows said.

"Please tell me why West and Candid would try to kill the Minister of Wildlife," the news editor demanded.

"Simple," Meadows glared at the TV news crew. "She wanted a story so big it would give her national fame, perhaps even make her anchorwoman, so they lured him to an interview meeting only to kill him."

"That's ridiculous!" Samantha exclaimed.

"Starting with the fact she turned down the anchor position some time ago," Dave added with clear annoyance towards the police chief.

"Your charges are baseless, and Washburn's not dead, he's alive and awake," Ted said. "I just came from the hospital. He woke up and told all the reporters and doctors standing around that he never met with Samantha and Dave. In fact, he gave a description of the person who shot him."

"He woke up?" Meadows replied incredulously. "Last I heard, doctors weren't even sure if he was going to make it!"

"If you don't believe me, turn on the TV," Ted answered. "All the networks have it on film; in the meantime remove those handcuffs and release my employees or face a lawsuit."

Reluctantly, and with visible disdain, the police chief unlocked the cell door and motioned for the journalists to get out. He then proceeded to remove the handcuffs. This accomplished, Meadows stepped aside.

"When will you be speaking to Washburn?" Samantha asked, retrieving her notepad.

"You can wait for the official statement later today," Meadows responded curtly.

"I hate covering PR releases," Samantha remarked to Dave, "They always leave out the information they'd rather not see on the air."

"You people always put more than you ought to on the air," answered Meadows angrily.

"West, Candid!" Ted called sternly. The reporter and cameraman duo hurried after their editor.

Once they were outside, Ted turned to the pair and said, "You two should go back to the hospital and talk to Washburn, regardless of the fact that our competitors got a head start in airing a report. I don't know whose bright idea it was to jail you two as if Sarrilla were some kind of dictatorship; but we can't let that succeed in censoring our newscast."

Samantha nodded. "Ok Ted, we'll talk to you later."

Samantha and Dave arrived fairly quickly at the hospital and went straight to Washburn's room, where they found him awake. He greeted them first.

"I have to thank you, both of you. I owe you my life," said Washburn, weakly. "I also wanted to apologize."

"Apologize?" asked Samantha.

"For missing our first interview meeting," he explained, "and for requesting that you not air this one."

"We won't air it," she told him. "But why?"

"I didn't tell the police or the other members of the press what actually happened," he said. "I was ambushed in the Wildlife Ministry parking lot by the person I described to them, and he put a handkerchief over my nose and mouth...after that I passed out...I'm guessing it must have been chloroform; I remember hearing in the news that someone had stolen some from the hospital. That much was true. When I woke up, I was inside what looked like a warehouse...I was sitting in a chair, in front of a table...and standing there was the man from the parking lot, and Governor Ulrich."

"Governor Victor Ulrich?"

"Yes." Washburn replied. "Two or three weeks ago, he contacted me and said he wanted to delist the arctic fox. He offered me half a million dollars if I would replace the population records on file with ones saying that the arctic fox was making a come-back and the Wildlife Ministry was authorizing its delisting."

"Did he say why he wanted them off the endangered species list?"

"No, he didn't...and for half a million dollars I wasn't about to ask. But I wasn't sure about doing it...I spent all that time before the wildlife conference mulling over it...and I finally decided it wasn't worth it. I couldn't do it. Those animals can't survive off the endangered species list, at least not yet, in their current state...and I was afraid what would happen if I went along with the corruption and people found out."

"So you never switched the documents," Samantha said.

"When Ulrich found out, he called me and demanded to know why. I told him I didn't want to do it and he responded that I had 48 hours to sign the papers."

"When was this?"

"Yesterday...so when I woke up at the warehouse, I must admit, I was afraid for my life."

"What happened?"

"The governor put the fraudulent paperwork in front of me...the other man with him held a revolver to my head...and Ulrich told me to sign the documents or else I would die."

Washburn fell silent, and Samantha didn't say anything; he continued eventually, almost pleadingly:

"What could I have done? I signed the documents. I was terrified. I begged him not to shoot me. Ulrich said he wouldn't kill me if I signed the papers...and when I did, then he turned around and ordered the other man to do away with me anyway. He said he had told me the truth...he wasn't going to kill me."

He shuddered. "The next thing I remember was waking up here in the hospital. They told me you two were both incarcerated on suspicion of having shot me. Ulrich was probably behind that as well. He likely learned somehow that you were investigating this fox matter...and planned to frame you two for killing me. I imagine he'd have to bribe someone else though...I can't imagine what judge and jury in their right minds would believe a television news crew plotted such a crime."

"He knew what we were up to," Samantha acknowledged. "We went to confront him about the discrepancy in the records, and why he was saying he could delist the foxes when the records said another thing. We just never got to air the report because there was a car explosion in front of the governor's mansion..." Samantha's voice trailed off.

If Ulrich tried to kill the wildlife minister...then he could have been behind Ranger Conway's car exploding, too...and if all this is true, the Nortenya region has a gangster in its highest government office, she thought.

"You see why I don't want this reported," Washburn said. "I'm concerned that Ulrich may try again to do something to me, or my wife."

"But then the documents on file are false," Samantha pointed out.

"They'll stay there," Washburn answered, "and Ulrich will succeed in delisting the arctic fox. I can't do any more. I'm sorry for those animals, they've done nothing to deserve being wiped out as a species...but it's my own life, and the lives of my family at stake."

"Will you tell the prime minister?"

"I don't know," he said, pensively. "I don't think anyone else would believe me." He studied the pair and then said, "What are you planning to do now?"

"We're going to continue investigating and bring out the truth about the arctic foxes," declared Samantha.

"Don't do it," Washburn told her. "If Ulrich doesn't mind trying to murder one of the men in the prime minister's cabinet, he won't stop at journalists. I don't want to be partly responsible for you two getting killed."

"Thank you for taking the time to speak with us, Mr. Washburn," answered Samantha. "We hope you feel better." Then, Samantha and Dave walked out of the room, into the hallway.

Samantha turned to Dave and said, "I'm going after this story, regardless of the risk."

"We are going after this story," her cameraman replied.

Chapter 13 - The Anonymous Source

That night, the reporter and her cameraman arrived at the casino. They left Geronimo and the two arctic foxes at the cabin, took a taxi part of the way, then walked a block or so to the Black Fox Casino on Brook Avenue in their elegant evening attire. They had hurriedly bought the outfits for the casino meeting. Samantha was wearing an evergreen silk dress that had sequins about the collar, and a mink fur stole; while Dave wore a tuxedo. The wind was sharp and the two journalists were freezing by the time they arrived at their destination.

They approached the roulette table and found many people standing around it as the present game ended, as well as the croupier - the man directing the game - but there was one creature there who stood out: the beautiful longhaired tuxedo cat with the amethyst-studded collar who was sitting regally beside the roulette wheel.

"Faites vos jeux," the man said, and players began to place their bets.

Samantha placed some casino chips on the square for 8 and she and Dave looked around, trying to figure out who the caller was.

"Some warm milk on a chilly night like this might be good," a voice purred.

Samantha glanced down to see the cat, who had wandered over to where she was standing. Trying to use discretion, they all watched the roulette wheel spin. "You were at the wildlife convention," said the reporter. "The governor's cat, Roxanne?"

"That's me-ow," replied Roxanne.

"What do you know?"

"No. I'm not even sure I should have called you."

"Why?"

"The corruption is pervasive...and the only thing that seems to determine whether one's the hunter or the prey anymore is lacking."

"Which is?"

"Luck," replied Roxanne, leaping off the roulette table and scampering off. Samantha turned but before she could say a word, the croupier announced:

"Eight. The lady wins."

Samantha and Dave cashed in the casino chips and looked for Roxanne. They found her sitting on a table in the nightclub dining area. A band here was playing music, while some people were dancing.

Samantha sat at the table, taking out her notepad. "I remember you said on the telephone that you work in the governor's mansion," she smiled.

"Yes, I'm their resident mouse-catcher." Roxanne flattened her ears. "I changed my mind about talking to the press."

"Roxanne, you're one of our only leads on this story," Samantha confided. "We'll never get to the bottom of this without someone willing to talk."

"It's not worth my pelt," hissed Roxanne.

"You're worried about retaliation?" Samantha asked. "Surely the governor wouldn't harm his own pet?"

"The idea that I'm the family housecat was conjured up for the voters," Roxanne told her dryly. "Mabel's really my human, and Victor is my human only by association."

"Even so, would he really hurt you if Mabel cares about you?"

"Yes," Roxanne stated bluntly.

Samantha and Dave glanced at each other; when her cameraman shrugged, Samantha turned back to Roxanne. "We'll keep your name secret. We won't say you told us the information."

"Do you really understand what you're promising?" Roxanne meowed.

"Yes," said Samantha.

"How do I know you'll keep your promise?"

"You have our word as journalists."

"That's noble but impractical," the cat replied with a wave of her tail.

"How so?" asked Samantha.

"Victor Ulrich can make anyone do what he wants." Roxanne answered.

There was a pause, with only the music from the band in the air; finally, Samantha spoke:

"I will never reveal your identity, no matter what."

"That counts for both of us," interjected Dave.

Roxanne flexed her claws thoughtfully. Just then, a meow chimed in.

"Geronimo?" Samantha said.

"We came in a taxi!" Dave was surprised. "How...?"

"If a kitty can sneak into a news van, a kitty can sneak into a taxi," Geronimo said matter-of-factly. "Come on, you don't think I would miss out on a real conversation with an anonymous source?!" he purred, swishing his tail.

"Are these your humans?" Roxanne asked Geronimo.

"Yep. My name's Geronimo. My humans take this 'protect your source' matter very seriously," Geronimo meowed. "It's one of their sacred ethics things. If they promise to keep your name secret, they will."

Roxanne studied Geronimo, then turned back to the two journalists who were waiting with a tacit expectation. "The poaching ring is being run out of the governor's mansion," Roxanne began directly. "It's really only a small group of people involved, but they have half the region terrified of them, or else bribed into complacency. Those people are Governor Victor Ulrich, and his treasurer-slash-mistress Denise Ralston." Roxanne ended this statement with a short hiss.

"How does the whole racket work?" asked Samantha.

"It's fairly simple. The Longguo ambassador was the one who started it," Roxanne growled.

"Qiang Xue?"

"Yes. He approached Victor one day with a business proposition. He had heard Victor was party to this sort of stuff and naturally Victor was very interested in any new and profitable enterprise, no matter how illegal or unethical. At Victor's order, the poachers hunt arctic foxes and turn the pelts over to him; Victor sells the furs to the ambassador. Denise takes money out of the regional treasury and gives it to Victor; he uses the money to pay the poachers. Denise gets kickbacks from Victor's selling the furs."

"How much is Ulrich getting for the furs?"

"1 million Sarrillian dollars from each sale," replied Roxanne.

At that moment, a waiter walked over. "Are you ready to order?"

Samantha, immersed in the interview, had half-forgotten that they were in a dining area. She glanced quickly at the menu, then looked over at their source.

"Lobster, please," Roxanne purred.

"A whole lobster or just the meat?" asked the waiter.

"Meat, please, thank you," responded Samantha.

When the waiter left with the order, Samantha asked the cat:

"How many pelts are usually sold at once?"

"About 100 furs, from what I've heard. It used to be 50, but Qiang wanted the number doubled on account of how lucrative the market is. At that rate you can imagine how quickly the species will be decimated."

"What does Ambassador Qiang want with fox pelts?"

"What I've heard is that the dictator in Longguo is the owner of a syndicate that has a large stake in the fur trade. Qiang gives him the furs, and his corporation makes fur garments and things which are sold domestically...arctic fox fur is some kind of a status symbol there, and having a fox coat is apparently highly coveted among the wealthy."

"It was the same in Sarrilla once," said Samantha, "until the foxes were hunted to near-extinction. ...Who are the poachers?"

"Their names are Seth Gorgonio, Luke Theron, and Virgil Venancio," Roxanne declared. "Gorgonio is the leader of the poachers; he tends to have frequent chats with Victor over the telephone. I saw them once at the governor's mansion, complaining to Denise that they hadn't been paid the previous week and I saw Victor hand them an envelope and throw them out of the office. He told them they should never go there again and should only meet at the appointed place."

"...the appointed place?"

"Where the fur exchange happens. It's always held at the same place."

"Where do the fur sales take place?"

"That I don't know," said Roxanne. "All I know is that they're typically held Fridays at night."

"Is that when the poachers are usually paid?"

"Yes."

"Does Denise go to the meetings at all?"

"Never. She just withdraws the cash and Victor goes wherever-it-is for the actual transaction."

"How does she write off their payment?"

"She does fraud on the books. How exactly, I'm not sure, but she makes it look legal enough so that the auditors overlook it."

"Maybe the payroll?"

"Could be." Roxanne was still unsure.

Samantha looked down at her notepad momentarily. She had been taking thorough notes throughout the interview, and the page was already half-covered in abbreviated scribbles of black ink.

"There's one more thing I noticed," added the cat. "One of the men, the younger one they call Theron...he didn't seem too happy to be in the company of the others. I sensed he felt trapped and wishing for a way out. He is a kind-hearted human, actually. I met him once."

It was at this point that the waiter arrived with the food. Roxanne and Geronimo pawed at Samantha and Dave for lobster, which they readily provided. As they ate, Roxanne continued speaking, recounting to the journalists the tale of political conspiracy and corruption.

"Victor got the bright idea to delist the foxes. He figured it would make his image look good in an election year; he'd be able to say that the arctic fox recovered under his administration. Whether it's true or not is besides the point, of course. With the foxes delisted, they can hunt more in the open," meowed Roxanne. "Anyway, he made a deal with the Minister of Wildlife, Mr. Washburn, to falsify documents and make them say the foxes could be taken off the endangered species list, but Washburn had a change of heart. Victor was furious when you two arrived at his office with the legit documents. He told Washburn over the phone he had 48 hours to sign the paperwork, and Washburn still refused to. So Victor ordered Gorgonio and Venancio to kidnap Washburn. They held him at gunpoint and forced him to sign the documents. Then they shot him. Gorgonio actually did, on Victor's orders." Roxanne appeared disgusted with the thought. "When you two found the wildlife minister, Victor called Chief Carson Meadows and told him to charge you with attempted murder. The police chief is one of the people Victor pays on occasion to do small jobs, mostly overlooking things Victor and his cronies do."

"That verifies Washburn's story," Dave said to Samantha.

"You're right...although..." Samantha turned back to the cat, who was licking her fur. "How do you know this?"

"I was at the warehouse when it happened." Roxanne answered.

"Which warehouse?"

"It's a regional warehouse on the outskirts of the city. I don't know the exact street address, but it's on Watt Street," said Roxanne, lifting a paw and inspecting her sharp claws. "It's a brick building, looks half-abandoned..."

Samantha and Dave looked triumphantly at each other with the same thought; it was Geronimo who stated it. "It's probably the same warehouse where the foxes saw the damn poachers!"

"What foxes?" asked Roxanne.

"Two arctic foxes," Geronimo purred. "They're my friends. My humans are letting them stay at our den temporarily because of the poachers."

Roxanne was interested. "I was right to call you," she purred, "People who care that much for a critter's plight are trustworthy."

"I'm wondering if that warehouse is where they're storing the furs," Samantha considered. "It would explain why the foxes saw the hunters there."

"It might be," Roxanne seemed thoughtful, "but again I don't know. They could just be storing them where they live."

"Where's that?"

"Land tract A-4," purred Roxanne.

This elicited a questioning look from Samantha. "A-4?"

"Yes."

"How do you know it's tract A-4?"

"I overheard Victor discussing it with Gorgonio over the telephone when they were first starting the poaching scheme," said Roxanne. "Apparently the place is situated on the tundra, away from most streets, and has an old hunting lodge there from before the foxes were classified as endangered. That area of Hammond Forest is the perfect, isolated place for them to prepare pelts and store their illegal traps--"

"Who gave them the traps?" Samantha interjected.

"Qiang did," answered Roxanne. "Speaking of illegal stuff, Denise has this fur stole which I'm sure Victor gave her. It's a complete fox, with white fur."

"Could it be a red fox pelt?"

"I don't think so. I've seen a few other humans wearing such things at fancy events I've attended. This is fluffier than the ones I've seen before."

Samantha reviewed her notes. "What part of the warehouse did you say Washburn was shot in...?"

"One of the storage units," Roxanne explained. "The only thing in that entire building are abandoned storage units; except for an office room, with a window overlooking the back alley. That's abandoned too."

Samantha scribbled the description down in her notepad. Roxanne stood up and stretched, arching her back. "Well, I've got to return to the mansion," said the longhaired cat. "My human, Mabel, will be wondering where I am."

"If we want to contact you for any more questions, how should we go about doing so?" Samantha asked.

"I can go find her!" Geronimo piped up. "Purrrr-lease? No one would expect a kitty!"

"That makes sense," Roxanne agreed. "If you want to meet with me, send Geronimo to the governor's mansion by noon." Roxanne turned to Geronimo and said, "There's a big tree that grows on the side of the mansion. It reaches all the way up to the top windows. I'll pass by around noon and if I see you on sitting one of the branches, I'll take that to mean your humans want to meet with me." Turning back to Samantha and Dave, she added, "If I want to meet with you, I'll call your office like I did this time."

"All right," said Samantha. "I'm curious...How did you call us?"

Roxanne purred. "I push the receiver off, and hook one claw onto the dial in order to call zero. Then I let the operator connect me to the channel 8 newsroom."

"Clever!" meowed Geronimo. "I should've thought of that!"

"Ok, here's my last question," Samantha told her. "What prompted you to come forward?"

"If I said it was purely for the sake of my fellow critters, I wouldn't be very honest," Roxanne admitted. "Really I was getting irritated by Victor because he's cheating on Mabel with that bitch Denise. Also, when Victor saw me at the warehouse he threatened to dye my fur white," she added with a growl.

"Dye your fur white?" Samantha asked, perplexed.

"He said it would make it look more like fox fur," Roxanne hissed.

Samantha and Dave were speechless; Geronimo looked horrified. Roxanne lashed her tail. "Victor isn't the paragon of 'Integrity and Humanity' everyone believes he is," said Roxanne.

She leapt down from the table, and as she was padding away Samantha said, "Thank you for the interview, Roxanne."

"Don't forget to keep my identity a secret," the cat replied before scampering off.

Chapter 14 - Arctic Tundra

The early-morning winter sky was still dark when Samantha and Dave - along with Geronimo - caught a taxi from the casino and headed directly to the TV station. Once there, Samantha went to her desk and within five minutes had typed up a report based on the information from Roxanne.

"I'll go get Ted," said Dave, and hurried off to find their editor.

Geronimo was analyzing the computer screen. Below the script, which was divided neatly into two halves - the left with video notations, the right with Samantha's report - was a number 30 bordered by two dashes. "Why do you always put a number thirty at the end of your scripts?"

"Oh, that's a journalist thing," Samantha answered. "It means it's the end of your story."

"Why not just put 'The End'?"

"A very long time ago," she explained, "during wartime, a newspaper reporter was using telegraph to report on the war. He uncovered an important story and managed to get the news out, but they shot him at his post. He used to sign off at the end of his messages with the number thirty...so, ever since then, reporters put a thirty at the end of their reports."

Geronimo was silent. This statement, and the information Roxanne had given them about the extent of the corruption, somehow made the tomcat realize that this was not as much of a carefree game as he had imagined. "This job does have a history of danger, doesn't it?"

Before Samantha could answer, Dave returned with their editor following. "What's this I hear about you two having the expose of the year?" Ted asked.

"Just that," said Samantha, pulling the paper from the printer as it emerged and handing it to Ted.

Ted took it and, in turn, handed her a manila envelope. "...This came from the governor's office, to your attention."

Samantha opened the envelope. Inside was a copy of Washburn's signed 'correction', and a cover letter, printed on the Nortenya region's official stationary, which read:

Miss Samantha West,

I come to you by way of these lines to address the issue of whether the arctic fox can be removed from the endangered species list.

Pursuant to our interview, I took the liberty of inquiring at the Capitol records office and found that a correction to the arctic fox population document was issued by the Ministry of Wildlife two months ago, but mistakenly was never filed by the clerk.

I have enclosed a photocopy of the aforementioned document in the hopes of clearing up any misunderstanding that may have occurred.

Sincerely,
Governor Victor Ulrich

Ted was reading through the news story, and only stopped to glance up at Samantha and Dave once he had finished. Both the reporter and her cameraman were studying the letter; Samantha was sitting down and Dave stood behind her. Geronimo had leapt onto Samantha's lap. They glanced up at their editor's expectant gaze.

"This anonymous source close to the governor's mansion..." Ted said finally, "how reliable is he?"

"We haven't checked it out yet," said Samantha, "but we think we were told the truth."

"Just thinking you have the truth isn't good enough," Ted said. "This person is saying the governor is party to attempted murder and national treason. You've got to have something to back it up. Especially now in an election year. Is there any chance this source is making this up just to lower Ulrich's ratings in the polls?"

Samantha considered Roxanne's admission that Ulrich had been cheating on Mabel, and wondered briefly if that might have made Roxanne exaggerate things even slightly. The sparrows on Tropical Island, Samantha knew, were famed for doing this when used as sources. She recalled one instance, shortly after a hurricane, when they flew to them claiming missiles were falling on the far side of the island. Samantha and Dave went to investigate and found it was only a tree that had fallen after being weakened by the storm. The story of birds now having to find another tree for their nests had made for an interesting human interest report, but it was certainly not war breaking out and definitely not the lead in their broadcast.

"I don't know," Samantha at last admitted.

Ted looked over the report once again. "This says the governor is corrupt, the treasurer is corrupt, and the ambassador of Longguo is doing something that would destroy all diplomatic ties with Sarrilla. If this is true, it's a damn good story." He handed the report back to Samantha with a smile.

"Verify it."

Samantha couldn't help but smile back.

The next few weeks were hectic for Samantha and Dave. Samantha researched Roxanne's tips and called up various people she thought might provide more information. Most of the people she called would fearfully hang up the phone as soon as she identified herself, or else they would yell at her and say, "No comment." The only film clip they had where the governor and the ambassador appeared together was the one in front of the wildlife convention, and it didn't prove anything.

In between, the TV news crew would go to the Capitol records office and search for any compromising documents. They would spend lengthy hours sifting through file cabinets that turned up nothing, scanning rows and rows of large numbers in microfilmed payrolls to no avail. A few times they brought stacks of documents they copied back to the newsroom to look through. Once, Geronimo unintentionally leapt up onto the table where the documents were neatly placed, scattering them on the floor and causing the journalists to spend another hour or so, putting the papers back in order.

All through this, Samantha and Dave had the election to cover. They would go out and do interviews for the election stories, giving live reports on whatever developments arose in the campaigns. Ulrich's opponent in the election was the Vaharis mayor Egan Irving, who accused Ulrich of mismanaging regional funds and being in the employ of special interests. This could be said to be the truth but he had no way to prove it, and Ulrich scoffed back that his opponent wanted to raise taxes and stifle corporate growth. Ulrich also took every opportunity to extol how his administration had succeeding in bringing arctic foxes back from the brink of extinction. No one spoke anymore about the arctic fox population discrepancy. Washburn remained silent, as he had said he would. Conway had not spoken since the incident at the governor's mansion, preceding the car explosion. Week after week elapsed to become a month, and despite the determined efforts of the reporter and her cameraman, all the tips from their anonymous source seemed to be unprovable.

So, that cold Friday at noon, Samantha stood in front of the governor's mansion before the camera, signing off her report:

"...Controversy or not, tomorrow night Governor Ulrich will sign the papers to officially delist the arctic fox. It'll go into effect a week from now - the day after the election. Reporting Live, Samantha West, WCAT 8 News."

Roxanne the cat was watching from a window in the governor's mansion, and she glanced up as Governor Ulrich appeared behind her, holding a cigarette up to his lips. The governor gazed outside at the news van, with its thin, tall antenna raised into the air and the two journalists broadcasting beneath it. He took a puff from the cigarette and stepped away from the window indifferently just as Denise burst into the office, wearing the fox stole slung over one shoulder.

"Victor this is unbelievable," she declared. "Those TV news people have been going through tons of documents at the records office. If they keep up like this, sooner or later they'll find something..."

"Denise, you're paranoid," Ulrich brushed aside her concerns. "These reporters relish a game of cat and mouse, something that they can pull out and pretend that they're looking out for their audience, holding people accountable, and all of that pretentious shit. That's why that TV reporter Samantha West has stayed with this so long. TV is a very fickle business, however. She won't have the time to stay chasing this mouse for very long."

"Suppose she gets the time?"

"No doubt she has her price," Ulrich said dismissively, "and curiosity does have a way with cats."

From the window, Roxanne hissed at him.

Outside, with the news report finished, Dave began dismantling the camera equipment. "Looks like our investigation deadline is election night, if we're hoping to prevent the foxes from going extinct," Dave said.

"Hopefully we can uncover what's going on sooner," Samantha answered. "I can't believe it! All those leads we've been following, and we still can't confirm the info!"

"Where's Geronimo?" asked Dave suddenly.

A meow from above made both the reporter and her cameraman look at the top of the news van. The cat was perched here, staring up delightedly at the microwave antenna.

"Geronimo, get down from there!" said Samantha.

"It's awesome the size of this antenna!" Geronimo purred. "It's like a huge tree!"

"We're going to lower it, Ger," said Dave. "Come down here."

Geronimo leapt off the news van. "How does that antenna work?"

"Oh, it transmits our signal out," Samantha explained briefly, and changing the subject said to Dave, "You know, we should drop by the ranger station. I have a few questions I'd like to ask Ranger Conway."

"Yeah, he hasn't spoken since the car explosion," Dave remarked.

Geronimo was bouncing around. "How do you make the antenna big and then little again? I want to see!"

"Ger..." Dave started, but Geronimo was so excited and purring loudly that the two journalists relented. "Ok. Over here," Dave explained, showing Geronimo a switch in the back of the news van with the broadcasting equipment, "is the lever which raises the antenna mast. When it's up, then air can go into the antenna tower and raise it."

"Yay!" Geronimo purred.

"But you shouldn't poke at this, Geronimo," Samantha cautioned. "The antenna should only be up when we're going to broadcast. It puts the news van in lock, meaning you can't drive with the antenna up."

"Also, you have to make sure there aren't any power lines overhead before you raise the antenna," Dave added. "If the antenna gets tangled in power lines and you touch the van, you won't be reporting the news, you'll be the news."

"That's where we have the saying, 'Look up and Live,'" Samantha informed the cat. "It's happened to other reporters before."

"Hiss," a wide-eyed Geronimo said. "You don't just have dangerous stories you cover, you have dangerous equipment."

"As long as we're careful setting up for broadcast, we don't have anything to worry about from that," Samantha told him more cheerfully. She looked at Dave and said, "Let's get over to the ranger station and see if Conway is there."

Geronimo was talkative throughout the drive out of the city. "You know what that reminds me of? That helicopter crash you were in that happened the day I was born."

"That's different," Samantha said. "The pilot didn't do anything wrong. The rotor on the tail just malfunctioned."

"Spinning...!" Geronimo mewed, chasing his tail in the back of the news van.

"There was nothing fun about it," Dave pointed out. "It was dizzying."

"...and painful," Samantha added, seeming to wince at the memory. "We all ended up in the hospital. My leg was dislocated at the hip."

"Why do TV news stations have choppers?" Geronimo asked, hopping in between the driver and passenger seats.

"Sometimes you can spot something newsworthy from the sky," Dave explained. "You can get some great camera angles from up there."

"Also, it means you don't have to rely on police traffic cameras for aerial shots and traffic info," Samantha continued. "It shows viewers that we're going out and digging stuff up ourselves, verifying what we're told instead of just blindly broadcasting it."

"I'd like to ride in a helicopter, one day," purred the cat.

A light diamond-dust of snow was drifting down when they reached the ranger station. It was a cabin with a wood sign that identified it as the Hammond Forest ranger station, with a clearing in front that had space for about three or four cars to park. Ranger Conway was the only park ranger staffing this northernmost outpost, and the cabin doubled as his living quarters.

"Hi, Ranger Conway!" Samantha happily greeted him.

"Samantha, Dave." Conway did not look surprised to see them; he seemed rather indifferent, as if he had expected the pair to show up sooner or later. "Why don't you come in? I'll get you some hot chocolate," he said, although rather half-heartedly.

The interior of the ranger station had a fireplace and a sofa, where the journalists sat. Geronimo jumped onto the wood coffee table. Zachary, the Husky, came over with his tail wagging. "The news-people! ...and a kittycat!"

"Hello Zachary," smiled Samantha, petting him on the head.

Conway came over with the hot chocolate. "I imagine you're wondering why it's been a month, and I've stopped talking about the foxes," he said directly.

"Why did you?" asked Samantha.

"The car explosion was bad enough," explained Conway, "but shortly after that I got a phone call threatening to harm Zach if I continued to protest the arctic fox's delisting." The park ranger was blunt. "They said if they could shoot a little fox, then it would be an easy matter to shoot a big dog...and then afterward it would be me."

"So you're going to sit back and let them delist the foxes?" Samantha was astounded.

"I'm still removing whatever traps I find," Conway said. "Just no more protesting. It's too much of a risk. I know you guys probably wanted some kind of a controversy to cover..."

"Well, a picket line in front of the governor's mansion would have made some great footage," said Dave.

"You've got to understand," Conway insisted. "I don't want to see those foxes go extinct, but I don't want myself or my pet getting hurt either. As a matter of fact, I would prefer it if you didn't air this that I'm telling you at all."

Samantha gazed at her notepad, tapping her pen against it. Somehow, she had expected more dedication from Conway. His fear now reminded her of Washburn, cringing and conceding to the brutality of Ulrich and his minions. A sly thought occurred to her, and she glanced up at him. "We won't air it," she accepted.

"Thank you," he said.

"...on one condition," the reporter added. "You give us a tour of the tundra."

"Why do you want a tour of the tundra?" asked Conway.

"We want some wildlife footage," said Samantha. "Specifically some shots of the foxes in their natural habitat. They've been exceedingly difficult to get...isn't that right Dave?"

"But Sam, we..." Samantha nudged him, and he agreed rapidly, "Yeah, very difficult!"

Conway looked suspicious, and the two journalists - plus the tomcat - gave him a wide-eyed look. Zachary broke in with a bark: "Yay, the tundra! I want to run!"

"All right," he agreed, "I suppose if I don't come to show you around, you'll go yourself and get lost or attacked by a bear."

"That's right," said Samantha proudly.

"Why are you people from the press so persistent?" he questioned, though not angrily.

"Because we're the press," Samantha responded.

Fifteen minutes later, they were trekking through the snow-covered meadowland. Zachary bounded ahead, like a wolf running through the snow. As they walked, Conway pointed out the arctic wildlife. "You see how rare the foxes are," he mentioned after a while. "We haven't seen a single one yet. Maybe we'll have better luck near the riverbank."

"Sam, I don't get it," Dave whispered to his companion as they followed Conway. "Why are we wandering around the tundra?"

"Roxanne said the hunter's cabin is on land tract A-4," replied Samantha with a grin. "By my estimate I'd say we're nearby. Conway knows the tundra territory; we might have gotten lost if we tried to make it here ourselves, but here we are! Now, all we have to do is sneak over there..."

"We're going to get into trouble," meowed Geronimo, who was sitting on Dave's shoulder.

"Oh, don't worry," Samantha declared.

Zachary circled back and barked. Conway stopped and gestured a distance away, where a mother polar bear was watching her two playful cubs. "Polar bears, over there. Did you know that sometimes the foxes follow bears for food? They'll eat scraps of seal meat that the bears catch."

Dave was filming the polar bears, but when Samantha motioned to him the two journalists quietly snuck away.

Conway, his gaze on the polar bears, continued his explanation without realizing. "Polar bears typically hang around the water, because that's where they can find their prey. Speaking of which, the river's close by, although it's probably still frozen over."

Zachary barked, but Conway went on, "I know this bear; I remember seeing her when she was pregnant with her cubs. This is actually her second time rearing cubs..."

Zachary barked again, more incessantly. "Yeah, Zach?" Conway turned to find that he and the dog were alone.

"The news-people are gone," Zachary pointed out.

Conway looked around. They had vanished. "Fuck," he muttered.

Not far away, Ivan and Natasha were padding into the tundra. "I don't know if this is safe, Ivan," said Natasha. "I know the lemmings are coming back to the tundra, but last time we were here we nearly got shot."

"We saw the hunters back there in the woods," Ivan reasoned. "If they're searching the forest right now, then all we have to worry about on the tundra is not stepping in any traps."

"Look, a lemming!" Natasha sprang ahead. The lemming had noticed the foxes too and made a run for it with the vixen in pursuit. It disappeared with a squeak under a stack of firewood, beside a small cabin in the center of the desolate, icy landscape.

"Damn!" yapped Natasha. "I almost had it!"

"Hey Natty," Ivan barked suspiciously, "wasn't this place an abandoned human den? How come there's fresh-cut wood here?"

Natasha looked upward. "...There's smoke coming from the chimney." She hopped up on top of the firewood and peered inside, only to yelp. "Ivan!"

Ivan leapt up next to her and snarled. Hung inside to dry on flat boards of wood were arctic fox pelts.

"This must be where the hunters live," Ivan realized. "We've got to get back and tell Geronimo's humans."

"I'm going to be sick," said Natasha, her ears flat.

Suddenly a net slammed down on them, toppling them off the wood pile and trapping them underneath its mesh. It was Gorgonio.

"No," the hunter answered the fox with a sneer, "you're going to be dead."

Samantha and Dave, meanwhile, were walking up a hill of snow. "The hunting cabin should be around here," Samantha said.

"Shouldn't we have told Conway what we were up to?" asked Geronimo.

"Are you kidding, Ger?" said Samantha. "He might erroneously decide that it's too dangerous for a reporter and photographer to look into themselves, and insist that the authorities handle it. There goes our scoop."

"What happens if we actually find the poachers?" Geronimo meowed.

"That would be something!" Dave said excitedly. "If we could get an exclusive shot of the poachers with all those fox pelts... Sam, do you think Ted would have us lead our five o'clock broadcast?"

"I think we'd lead at five, six, and eleven and still be in the first block of the morning news tomorrow," an equally excited Samantha answered. "Hey, that must be the hunting lodge!"

"What's a block?" asked Geronimo.

Around the corner of the cabin, Gorgonio had stepped on one corner of the net and pinned the other against the wood pile to be able to aim his rifle.

"How could you be here?" Ivan asked him. "You were in the forest."

"Theron and Venancio were in the forest," Gorgonio corrected. "All those times you two kept escaping from us, and now you've been outfoxed. You're going to wind up as someone's fur coat."

He snapped back the rifle's safety catch...and without warning, a flash of light caught the barrel of the gun, momentarily blinding him. He stepped back in a startled reaction, and saw, standing a few paces behind him, a lady who he recognized as the channel 8 reporter Samantha West, and beside her a man who was the photographer, holding a TV camera - with the light on and pointed straight at him. A cat with Siamese markings was standing at their ankles with his back arched.

"What the..." Gorgonio's voice cut off with a gasp as Ivan leapt up and sank his fangs into his arm. He had inadvertently released the foxes from the net.

At a yap from Natasha, the male fox released the hunter and the two critters ran away. Gorgonio seized the rifle, which he had dropped, but instead of chasing the foxes he spun around to face the journalists. They were standing there, the camera still focused on him. "Give me the tape," he ordered, just as Samantha grabbed Dave's hand and they turned and ran in the opposite direction.

Gorgonio was furious. Ignoring the pain from the fox's bite, he fired two or three shots at them. Geronimo, who had leapt back onto Dave's shoulder, let out a surprised meow.

"Those damn poachers don't even respect the press," he hissed.

"The corrupt never do!" answered Samantha.

They half-tumbled down a mound of snow to a frozen river. There was a waterfall here, which had transformed into an icy cliff from the cold. As they tried to race across the ice, Samantha lost her balance; Dave caught her.

Gorgonio appeared at the top of the snowbank. He lifted his rifle and fired at them again, sending zigzagging cracks along the ice, but missing his targets as they hid behind the waterfall.

As he hurried down the slope towards them, barking made him stop in his tracks. Zachary the Husky came bounding over and got in his path, growling.

Conway was right behind Zachary.

Gorgonio frowned. "I was shooting at a rabbit when your dog came running over. He scared it off."

"Is that so? Sorry about that. ...May I see your trapping license?"

The hunter handed over the card for the park ranger to inspect, and when Conway was satisfied he handed it back. He noticed the blood on Gorgonio's sleeve. "How did you get hurt?"

Gorgonio had half-forgotten about the injury. "...oh, nothing."

Zachary was whining at the waterfall, and Conway noticed. "Hey Zach, what's over there?"

The dog ran over, and as Conway followed him, Gorgonio took the opportunity to escape.

Zachary had stopped at the entry to the small cave behind the waterfall. His tail was wagging. "The news-people!"

Samantha and Dave, along with a fluffed Geronimo, were sitting on a rock here. The cave ground was covered in a sheet of ice, which made it difficult for them to move, but the three of them were well-hidden from outside view. "Hi, Zach! ...and Ranger Conway! Not a moment too soon," Samantha smiled.

"...and we saved our tape," added a happy Dave, ejecting it from the camera.

Conway looked befuddled. "Honestly guys, you do realize that you nearly got yourselves killed for a couple of minutes of TV footage, right?"

"We were hiding from that guy you were just talking to. We filmed him trying to kill a couple of foxes and he wanted to destroy the evidence," replied Samantha.

"It's going to be difficult to catch him, but after the tape airs, his picture will be all over the territory. Maybe someone will phone in a tip," said the ranger with a sigh. "When will it be on the news?"

"Tonight," answered Dave. "Maybe that will make him stop hunting for a while."

They all heard a rustling in some nearby bushes, and out came the foxes, Ivan and Natasha.

"Those are the foxes," said Dave.

"Are you all right?" asked Ranger Conway, facing the foxes.

"Yes. Just a little nervous," replied Ivan.

"Maybe you two should go to the cabin, to avoid running into the hunters again today," said Samantha. "Dave and I will go later and we'll all have dinner."

"I like that idea, Ivan," said Natasha. "I don't want to be out here if that bad human returns."

Having said that, the foxes ran off in the direction of the cabin, and the little group, composed of the ranger and the reporters with their cat Geronimo, went on their way.

Eventually, they were back at the ranger station and the reporters and their cat drove off. Conway felt restless, looked at his dog and said, "Zachary, what say we go into the city and see what's happening?"

The dog jumped up and down, wagging his tail.

"All right, then," said the ranger.

Chapter 15 - The Hideaway

In the city, Mabel was shopping at a department store. "Mewrrr" her cat Roxanne half mewed and half purred. "Are you sure you can carry all those packages, Madame?" she asked.

"I'll manage, Roxy" answered Mabel, "You know this is the best distraction from my loneliness. Without you, kitty, I really would be depressed."

As Mabel and her cat were walking out the store onto the street, a gust of wind blew fiercely and Mabel lost her balance and the grip on her packages, all of them falling to the ground.

She felt a sudden pang of sadness and covered her face with her hands. Suddenly she felt the cat placing a paw on her leg, so she looked down and saw Roxanne looking straight at her with worry. She also noticed someone gathering all the strewn bags. It was Ranger Conway and his dog.

He walked over and they both looked at each other without saying a word, until Mabel found her voice and simply said, "Thanks, friend."

Conway thought she was beautiful. He reached down, helped her up, and smoothed Mabel's hair away from her face. Mabel felt a shiver. She had rarely been treated with such gentleness and she felt a sense of love. Her cat, Roxanne, purred.

Mabel just stared back at Conway, who looked deep into her eyes and whispered, "You are beautiful, Mabel."

Mabel studied his face, partly because it had been such a long time that anyone had said those words to her and partly because she felt a deep attraction to him.

Conway remembered the time they had spent talking in a cafeteria, some weeks ago and he also remembered that he had been thinking about her a lot. Conway was in love with Mabel and he wasn't the type to hide his feelings. He took her face and framed it with his hands, then he kissed her mouth, gently. Mabel let him. She wanted him to kiss her. She had fallen in love too.

The two of them walked off arm in arm, with their cat and dog following behind.

That day, they started a love affair that would last forever.

The video of Gorgonio and the trapped foxes was broadcast on the evening news.

During this time, the poachers were swiftly and secretly moving from the tundra cabin to the regional warehouse. It was mostly Theron and Venancio who did this; Gorgonio only showed up once to order them around, then vanished on the excuse of checking the trap lines. It was already early evening by the time they completed the move.

The interior of the storage facility was dreary and grey and the air was musty from enclosure and disuse; it had corridors lined with storage chambers which created a labyrinth. In addition, the only illumination came from lighting that buzzed furiously and flickered, as windows in the building were sparse. The floor was concrete, while the walls were unpainted red brick; the only modern thing appeared to be the metal divisions between the storage units.

It did not appeal to Venancio. Standing in the center of the large storage unit where they had deposited half of their boxes, he smirked at the surroundings. "Talk about disrepair. We're expected to live in a bunch of unheated, dilapidated storage units! Look at this place...even the lights are flickering out."

"It's just some faulty wiring," Theron responded, a bit more cheerfully. "I'll get to work fixing it."

Venancio glared at him. "You're missing the point, Theron."

It was about this time that Gorgonio walked in nonchalantly, carrying - to Theron's surprise - a small bag of groceries. "Not bad. You didn't unpack anything though, you dimwits."

"You went out in the city to get groceries?" Theron was in disbelief.

"What part of being 'wanted' don't you understand?" Venancio added.

"The part that says I have to stay cooped up terrified of the cops," Gorgonio retorted, then adding, "Open the boxes."

After all the boxes were unpacked, Theron and Venancio began the laborious process of trying to find the proper location for things. It seemed that the imperfect lighting was the result of one of many defective electrical connections. They didn't notice Gorgonio step out of the room.

"Will you look at this," Venancio muttered as they tried to turn on a small television set they had plugged into the wall, "even the outlets don't work!"

"Probably needs to be replaced," Theron considered.

"You do that," Venancio snapped. "Where the hell is Gorgonio, anyway? It's just like him to leave us with all the work. I honestly hope he gets caught if he went out on the town again."
