Theron was more interested in the broken outlet. "I think I left all of my electrical stuff in the other room. I'll get it," he said, hurrying out.

Gorgonio was standing in the corridor. Leaning against one of the storage unit doors, he was immersed in scrutinizing something which he had retrieved from his pocket. It was a glass vial containing a clear liquid.

"Hey boss...I've got to get in here," Theron said, motioning to the door. He then noticed what Gorgonio held. "...What've you got there?"

"Something I swiped from somewhere," Gorgonio replied indifferently, but not before Theron could get a look at the label.

"Chloroform?" said Theron.

"Yes, chloroform."

"Why do we need that?"

"Practicality eludes you," Gorgonio responded cryptically. "This happens to be a rather useful little chemical."

"I imagine so...to doctors," Theron answered.

Gorgonio's cell phone rang and when he picked it up, he saw it was Ulrich's phone number. "Fuck," he muttered. "...Yes?"

"How could you have been so stupid?!" the governor's voice berated from the other line. "Letting yourself get filmed by a couple of news reporters out looking for a story! You are one of the most complete idiots..." Gorgonio held the phone away from himself as Ulrich shouted. When he heard silence from the other end, he brought the phone back to his face and spoke into it:

"Look, we've already moved everything out of the cabin and into the warehouse. ...yes, that includes the furs."

"At least you have some sense, however meager," Ulrich said. "I'm signing those foxes off the endangered species list tomorrow and when that goes into effect election night, you're just going to be one of many legally hunting foxes, whether anyone likes it or not. I've already spoken with the ambassador...the meeting tonight is cancelled."

Roxanne nonchalantly padded into the governor's office as he continued speaking. "You'll give Qiang this week's merchandise at the next meeting, along with the usual supply."

"Done," said Gorgonio, "and where do we pick up our money?"

"You'll get that at next week's meeting."

"What?! Since when do we have to wait to get paid?"

"If you want to keep this job then I'd suggest you learn some patience!" The cat was staring intently at the curtains which draped on either side of the office's windows. Roxanne flattened her ears and, extending her claws, leapt and climbed up the fabric. "You'll get paid at the meeting next Friday, same as always. In the meantime, Gorgonio, you get more of those fox pelts; otherwise I'll lose my patience with you!"

At that instant, there was a loud crash as the curtain staff fell; Ulrich turned around to see a lump underneath the curtains. Roxanne poked out her head and purred at Ulrich.

"Damn you, cat!" Ulrich snapped at her as she gracefully shook off the curtains and with a swish of her tail, calmly and indifferently padded out of his office.

Chapter 16 - Expenditures

Samantha and Dave continued their investigating relentlessly at the station. Geronimo joined in half-heartedly. After seeing how close they had come to being shot on the tundra, he had begun rethinking the excitement of the journalism profession. Now that he had a taste of how real the danger was, he couldn't comprehend why his humans seemed ever more intent on persisting with the story.

It was late in the day when Samantha received another phone call at the office, from Roxanne. The TV news crew met her at the casino's roulette wheel.

"Denise is paying the hunters through a phony company." Roxanne got right to the point. "She heads a firm called 'Nortenya Landscaping', which has a regional contract to supposedly plant trees along Nortenya's highways. The only people her firm employs are the three poachers. Incidentally, the highways have no trees."

A look at the regional expenditures - which they had gotten before to see if money was being laundered by some other means - confirmed the existence of Nortenya Landscaping, and that it was being paid over $500,000. Documents on file showed the business was listed as belonging to Denise Ralston, and her only three employees - Seth Gorgonio, Luke Theron, and Virgil Venancio - combined, earned the exact amount the firm was getting from the region.

Early next morning, Samantha and Dave drove to the address listed for the business and found an unmarked office in a Vaharis shopping center, with only a table, two chairs, and a telephone inside. The door was locked.

When Samantha placed a telephone call to the treasurer's office, the secretary told the reporter that Denise was on her lunch break. So the two journalists decided to go in person to her office.

As they got off the elevator on the second floor, they turned the corner and there was a lobby area with a secretarial desk, a bookcase to her right, and behind her a long corridor which led to the treasury offices.

"May I help you?" the secretary asked as they walked up.

"Yes, I had called on the phone earlier; Samantha West from WCAT television news?" said the reporter. "We have some questions we'd like to ask Ms. Ralston..."

"I'm sorry, Ms. Ralston isn't in right now. She's in a meeting."

"When will the meeting be over?"

"I can't say."

Samantha was, by nature, an observant person. She noticed the woman's nervousness and concluded that something was amiss.

"Thank you. Perhaps we'll come back at a later time," the reporter answered.

Dave glanced at her, but said nothing.

The pair turned around and walked back to the elevator and as they turned the corner, Dave said, "What's the scheme, Sam?"

The reporter's green eyes sparkled with excitement. "Just wait and see," she said.

The two stayed in the elevator area hidden around the corner. Samantha peeked out every now and then towards the lobby desk; and within ten minutes the secretary got up and went into a side door marked 'restrooms'.

"Now" said Samantha, "Get the camera rolling."

She quickly walked past the desk and into the corridor with Dave following close behind.

The first office they found was the one they were looking for; the sign on the wall said: Denise Ralston, Treasurer.

Denise was standing near a window, smoking a cigarette and turned her head in time to see the reporters walk in.

"What the hell are you doing in here!?" she yelled, her face getting flushed.

"Just a few minutes of your time, Ms. Ralston," said Samantha, quickly adding, "We wanted to know why a firm you own is being paid over $500,ooo by the region for trees it never planted?"

"No comment," Denise retorted, seeming surprised.

"Why is that complete sum going to your only three employees, one of which happens to be wanted by the authorities for poaching arctic foxes? Doesn't your company have any other expenses?"

"None of your damn business. Get out of my office." snapped Denise.

"It's the people's money, and therefore it is my business to report it," Samantha snapped back.

"I don't give a fuck about 'the people'. My high level in society doesn't answer to the lower masses" Denise was fuming.

"Do you mean that you deny the funneling of money that is taking place out of the region's Treasury department and ending up in the pockets of a wanted poacher?" the reporter persisted.

"Fuck you bitch!" Denise screamed.

Samantha smiled and said, "You represent your 'high level in society' very well."

"Security!" Denise yelled at the top of her lungs, but before any guards arrived, Samantha and Dave had left the office, walked past a very astonished secretary and entered the elevator.

"Dave." Samantha looked at her trusted photographer.

"Sam." he answered, "Every word and picture was captured on film."

"Let's see her try to deny her words," she responded.

Governor Victor Ulrich glanced up from the television as Denise stormed into his office. Roxanne was seated on a sofa to the side of the room; she growled as the treasurer, holding the fox stole, approached Ulrich.

"This is the last straw," Denise said indignantly, "I have had enough of those pesky, good-for-nothing journalists poking around!"

"All journalists are pesky and good for nothing," Ulrich interrupted, indifferently lighting a cigarette. "Which of the many are we talking about?"

"Don't be snide." Denise was furious. "It's that television reporter Samantha West! She actually dared to waltz into my office and question me! I want you to do something about her. Hell, I want to deal with that gossipy bitch personally..."

Her voice trailed as she glanced at the television set. Channel 8 was playing the film of Samantha confronting her in the office, and her outraged reaction.

"I've told you to maintain your composure," Ulrich responded casually when she pointed to the TV.

"If you had paid attention to me, they wouldn't have found out how we were laundering the money," Denise demanded.

"Denise," said Ulrich, calmly, "As you said, they're journalists. Journalists are always going to annoy. That's what they do. Sooner or later they'll either get bored of investigating, or their editor will. Besides, that reporter can't do anything about us. Even if she discovered the whole conspiracy, what good would it do? People trust us, Denise."

"They wouldn't if they knew," Denise responded.

"They won't know, but even if they did they can't do anything, nor would they. I'm too revered by the public to be brought down by a news story. Nortenya is mine, soon all of Sarrilla will be, and no one can stop me."

"Fine, I see your popularity is going to your head. When we're all standing in court then we'll see how influential you are getting us off lightly," Denise said, swinging the fox stole over her shoulder and walking briskly out of the office.

Samantha's voice came from the television: "...One of the three employees of Nortenya Landscaping is listed as Seth Gorgonio. We couldn't find anyone by this name in the city directory...however, according to a source within the governor's mansion, this is the same person who was identified as being involved with the arctic fox poaching. Reporting Live, Samantha West, WCAT 8 News."

This made Ulrich turn back towards the television, analyzing the reporter's words. "She has an anonymous source," he considered aloud. "Someone here is tipping off the press."

At this point, Roxanne leapt on the desk and scratched behind an ear.

"Get off my desk, you're shedding fur everywhere, and get out of my office!" Ulrich yelled at the cat.

Roxanne calmly jumped off the desk, hissed at him, and ran out the door.

Meanwhile, the hunters had gone into Hammond Forest early that morning to trap more foxes. The fur exchange meeting was election night, and they were short on their quota of fox pelts. Arctic foxes were becoming scarcer, and with each one they caught their rarity increased. Gorgonio headed in one direction, while Theron and Venancio headed in the other.

Venancio glanced down at the snow and noticed some pawprints. "These fox tracks look fresh. Theron, go after them; I'm going to check the other trap line we set over there."

During this time, Ivan and Natasha were padding through the snow, their jaws full of lemmings. They found lemmings easily all around the forest and after catching some to eat instantly, they determined to get some to cache away for later. After the famine earlier that winter, the present profusion of the rodents was like a bonanza to the arctic foxes, and they were trying to take full advantage of it until the inevitable population crash of the lemmings.

It was Ivan and Natasha's tracks the hunters had encountered. Theron followed the trail to a section of the woods bordered on one side by a creek, which had frozen over, and a line of small bushes. Here, he saw the foxes walking along and he crouched down to stay out of sight. Those are the same two foxes we keep meeting.

The foxes had not noticed him, and from where he was hiding, he had a clear shot at them, but as he lifted the rifle he felt a sudden pang of pity for them. He had never noticed how small these animals were.

"Theron!" He could hear Venancio coming and in a sudden decision, he brushed the rifle against the dry leaves to make a loud noise. The foxes turned to look at him and froze. He waved them off, and they ran away.

Venancio came up behind him in the same instant that the foxes fled into the bracken. "What the fuck, Theron!" he snapped, infuriated, "you almost had them!"

"The rifle jammed," Theron said. Inwardly, he felt at peace knowing that he had spared the lives of the innocent animals.

It was then that Gorgonio arrived, carrying not one but five fox skins.

"Well, you've had good luck hunting," Venancio observed, "unlike some of us. Where'd you find so many of them?"

The lead poacher glared at Venancio. "Don't tell me you didn't catch any of those animals."

"Hey, it was his fault," Venancio immediately spoke up, gesturing to Theron. "He had a clear shot at two foxes and he didn't fire."

"My rifle jammed!" Theron insisted. "Besides, you're the one placing traps where the rangers can find them!"

"You morons," Gorgonio scoffed. "How hard is it for you two to skin a couple of damned foxes? Or do I have to do everything? Theron, take these back to the warehouse and make sure everything's ok over there." Turning to Venancio, he said, "You and I are going to finish checking the traps."

Theron was glad to leave; the whole business of poaching was making him feel ill.

When evening came, Gorgonio and Venancio returned to the warehouse. The hallways were immensely dark, due to the fact that the lights were off, but when Gorgonio went to switch them on they remained off. He looked up at the wire mesh that ran across the ceiling and realized the lights had been removed. A faint glow came from one of the storage units down the hall, and he walked over to it, irritated.

In one of the warehouse's abandoned storage units, the hunters had found a couple of chairs and a table, both oaken and of an antique design, which Denise said were hers; however, as she presently had no use for them they were left in the warehouse. Sitting at the wood table was Theron, tinkering around with one of the long fluorescent lights. He had it connected to a nondescript black box with some kind of meter and dial on the front, and which was plugged into the wall outlet. Two wires ending in copper rods snaked out of the device; Theron was holding them to the light.

Sensing Gorgonio's presence at the entryway, Theron glanced up.

"What the hell are you doing?" Gorgonio demanded.

Theron lifted the wires. The fluorescent light went dark. "I was trying to fix the lighting," he said, placing the wires on the table. "It seems it's the wiring that's bad...the lights seem to work fine."

"I don't give a shit," Gorgonio complained. He was eyeing the device on the table and after a short pause he spoke again, his voice less accusatory. "That thing you have there..." he began.

"It's a power source," Theron said proudly.

"A what?"

"Well, it's a transformer with a dial to regulate the electricity...you plug it into the wall and it amplifies the alternating current from..."

"Never mind, I don't care." Gorgonio impatiently said. "What about these copper things...?"

"They're electrodes. ...Don't!" Theron warned as Gorgonio reached for them, but it was too late. Gorgonio jerked back, his hands gripping the copper. The needle on the meter rose only slightly, but his reaction was violent and agonized.

"Get them off! Get them off!" he screamed, and Theron pulled the plug out of the outlet. Gorgonio released the electrodes and fell backwards onto the floor.

"Are you OK?" Theron asked.

"Damn you!" yelled Gorgonio. "I could have gotten electrocuted! Hook the lights back up and put that shit away!"

Theron didn't respond and did as he was told.

That evening, the reporter and her cameraman went out again. When Samantha and Dave arrived at the plaza in front of the governor's mansion, they found that their competitors, Channel 5 and Channel 13, had arrived earlier than they had.

"Damn it," Dave remarked, as he parked the news van on the side of the plaza, "There go all the good camera angles."

"We've got a lot to cover, Dave," said Samantha. "Not only do we need the footage of Ulrich signing the foxes off the endangered species list, but Devon wants this story about the ice rink opening for the 11 o'clock newscast."

"I still say we should just go on the air saying Ulrich's a crook and leave it at that," a familiar feline voice chimed in from the back of the news van.

"Geronimo," Dave said.

"I'm not even surprised anymore," sighed Samantha.

There was already a cluster of press cameras around a podium which had been set up in front of the ice rink. It was a dual event: the opening of the new ice rink, and the delisting of the arctic fox. Samantha and Dave would be covering both, but the more important event was the delisting.

They found a spot on the side, where Dave set up the tripod and camera. Samantha took the microphone, on a small stand, and placed it on the podium alongside the competitors'. She made sure that the Channel 8 microphone flag was visible on-camera. It was windy and very cold. The governor arrived half-an-hour late, as politicians were so apt to do when holding a press conference outdoors.

Governor Victor Ulrich gave some remarks about the ice rink, and then turned to the matter of the arctic foxes. He gave a showy speech about the spectacular thing that he had done of reviving the dwindling arctic fox numbers, and in clear defiance he also spoke of the boon this would be to local furriers and the hunting tourism that would come to Nortenya. Geronimo listened attentively to the speech. This was the first time Geronimo had seen Ulrich in person, and the cat could immediately sense there was something dishonest and untrustworthy about the governor.

Under the lights of the press cameras and to the applause of his political adherents standing behind him, Ulrich signed the remaining document to remove the arctic fox from the endangered species list. Only Samantha and Dave seemed to fully comprehend that he was signing the animals into extinction. In one week, Friday at midnight, the foxes would be classified as just another fur-bearer and Governor Ulrich would almost certainly be celebrating his second term in office. If there was any doubt of his winning the election, his being the one who ostensibly brought the arctic fox back from extinction sealed it in the polls. Samantha and Dave had a new deadline.

After the paperwork was signed, there was a brief opportunity for the press to ask questions. A newspaper reporter asked something about how much funding the region had given towards the ice rink construction, but that was all.

Samantha asked, "Governor, is there any concern that delisting the foxes now, with poachers after them, might be a bad idea?"

"The foxes have recovered," replied Ulrich. "Certainly it is an affront, and my office is doing all we can to bring these criminals to justice. The fox population is abundant and thriving and we have not seen any negative impact. Anyone else?"

It was a clearly scripted answer.

There was silence, and as Ulrich said, "Ok," and turned to leave, Samantha spoke up again:

"Any comment on the fact that one of the poachers was found listed as an employee of a landscaping company owned by treasurer Denise Ralston?" All the media turned their attention once again to the governor.

"No," Ulrich answered bluntly.

"What about the...?"

"Ms. West," Ulrich smiled in an almost hostile way, "Arctic foxes recovering is a rare piece of good news. I hope you are not trying to misrepresent this happy event to get higher ratings."

Just like we all hope you're not lying about the foxes recovering to get higher poll numbers. It was a tempting retort, but Samantha caught herself. She knew her place was to report what was happening and let the viewers decide, not to give her opinion.

As everyone dispersed, Samantha and Dave walked around the ice rink. There were already people skating on it. Geronimo chased after the two journalists.

"I'm going to do my stand-up segment on the ice," declared Samantha.

"You don't know how to ice-skate," Dave pointed out.

"I'll hang on to the banister," replied Samantha.

Samantha seized hold of the railing and tentatively walked onto the margin of the rink, holding her microphone with one hand. She turned to Dave, who had the camera focused on the skaters; Geronimo was sitting underneath the tripod.

"I'll walk towards you," Samantha told him.

"Ok," agreed the cameraman. "I'll start on the skaters and then I'll pan over to you."

"Take one," announced Samantha.

She began speaking as the camera's white light covered her:

"This ice rink is one of several projects receiving regional funding..."

She cut off with a small gasp as she fell down.

"Take two," Dave said matter-of-factly.

"It's not as easy as it looks," Samantha acquiesced.

Samantha tried to get up but fell again. She had slid away from the railing. "Dave, help me up," she said.

Dave tried to grab her hand but couldn't reach her.

A yap made Samantha glance over. Ivan and Natasha were both sitting on the ice, watching them. They padded over, their fur-covered paws providing traction just as when they had first met Geronimo. "You can't get up...?" questioned Ivan.

"I guess not," answered Samantha.

The two foxes grabbed hold of her sleeve and pulled her to where she could once more grab hold of the railing. "Thanks," said the reporter.

"Arctic foxes, here in the city?" It was Ulrich. He was standing a short distance away, flanked by his bodyguards, and watching the two fluffy critters.

"They're my friends," offered Geronimo.

"Fine quality fur," he said pensively, ignoring the cat’s comment. “They’re in their winter prime.”

Ivan flattened his ears and, with a swish of his tail, he and Natasha trotted off. The vixen whispered to her mate, “That man frightens me.”

Ulrich spoke to the journalists. "It's remarkable how you befriended those animals...much the same way as you've befriended someone close to my office."

When neither Samantha nor Dave spoke, he went on, "I would very much like to know who."

"Journalist's ethics," Samantha said. "We never reveal our sources."

"So I've heard," Ulrich replied.

With a motion to his entourage, the governor left.

Chapter 17 - City foxes

Ulrich arrived at the governor's mansion in a bad mood. Instead of going to his quarters for dinner, he went to his office.

"News reporters are a nuisance," he grumbled.

He picked up the phone and dialed. Gorgonio the hunter, answered it.

"Yeah, what."

"I have a small task for you," said the governor.

"We're still trying to fill your quota for the week..." began the hunter.

"This will tie in nicely with that," interrupted Ulrich. "There are two stray foxes running around in the city. I want you or one of your men to pick them up. Their fur is excellent."

Gorgonio hesitated, then questioned, "In the city? I've never seen a fox or any other wild animal wander in."

"Well, they're there, I saw them tonight around the skating rink; and what's more, it seems that those pesky reporters West and Candid know them. Find those foxes and kill them. I want those furs," ordered the governor.

"Ok." Gorgonio answered simply, and heard the phone line hang up.

"Venancio! Theron!" he called out to his partners.

The two men came into the room.

"What are you yelling about?!" Venancio yelled back, "I'm not deaf you know."

Theron leaned back against a table, stuck his hands in his pockets and said nothing.

"I've got a chore for you," Gorgonio told Venancio.

"More? Theron and me barely got finished packing that last batch of hides," was the response.

"Whatever," Gorgonio seemed annoyed. "Ulrich saw a couple of foxes running around in the city near the skating rink and wants us to get them. Good quality fur, he says. I want you to go get it done."

"Why me? Why not Theron, or you?"

"Because, you dimwit, I got cops looking for me...and I need Theron here to finish some repairs." Gorgonio said glancing at Theron, who remained silent.

Venancio did not answer. He turned around and grabbing a revolver, checked to see if it was loaded and hid it in his inside jacket pocket. "Let's hope they're still wandering in the same area," he said, and went out the door.

The city skating rink was full of people when Venancio arrived. He looked around but saw no signs of any animals. He got back in the truck, drove around for a few blocks and then he saw them. Foxes. Two arctic foxes sitting underneath a tree in a small park that served as an oasis in the city.

He parked his truck out of their line of sight, and walked slowly towards them.

The foxes, Ivan and Natasha, were resting, but their senses were alert and they both picked up their ears. Ivan raised his nose to the air and sniffed. "Human. Approaching," he said to his mate.

By now, Natasha was also smelling the scent. "Yes, it's male."

"His intentions are not good," said Ivan.

Natasha nodded her head in agreement.

The two foxes got up and ran as fast as they could in the opposite direction of the hunter, but Venancio saw them and gave chase. They fled into the city area but the hunter was determined and kept up.

The animals ran past stores, and through small crowds of people who eyed them with interest but didn't try to discover what the chase was about. Then they came to a corner and as soon as the foxes turned it, they almost ran into Geronimo and Roxanne who were walking around.

With no time to spare, they ran past them, meeting their eyes as the thought of danger crossed their minds. The cats picked up on the thought, and chased after the foxes, passing them and motioning for them to follow.

Roxanne and Geronimo took them to an alleyway where the side door of the coffee shop was, and there, sitting near the warmth of the heating vent, was Zachary, the ranger's dog. He was waiting for his human who had gone in to speak with the owner of the coffee shop.

Zachary looked up with surprise when he saw the bunch of critters run over to him with their fur frizzed.

"What's happening?" he asked.

"Not much time to explain," responded Ivan, "We're being chased and it looks like one of the hunters that tried to capture us the other day."

"In the middle of the city? Hide," said the dog. "I'll stand guard while you cats distract him."

"Of course. We'll sit here with the dog and make the hunter think that he's been chasing us all the time," purred Roxanne.

"That human is so stupid, he'll believe it," added Geronimo.

"And...just in case he has doubts," snarled Zachary, "my growling fangs will persuade him."

The foxes quickly hid behind some garbage cans and the dog positioned himself in front of them, while the cats sat before the dog and waited.

They didn't have to wait for long. Venancio turned the corner within minutes and found himself looking at an angry dog and two cats.

"Cats?" he said looking at them. "No. I'm sure I was chasing foxes."

He thought for a minute, then reached for his gun. "Maybe you know where the foxes are...tell me."

He pointed his revolver at the animals, but before any one of them could leap at him, the back door of the shop opened, and out stepped Ranger Jovan Conway. "What's going on here?" he asked, pulling out his own gun.

Venancio gave no answer. He turned and ran all the way back to his truck.

Conway didn't give chase. He put his gun back in the holster and patted his dog on the head, checking on the cats as well. He saw the two foxes emerge from behind the trash bins.

"So that's it," he said. "You foxes have lots of friends ready to help you, but I don't think you should be wandering into the city area anymore."

"You're right." answered Ivan.

"We'll stay in the forest," added Natasha.

"Come on," said the ranger, "I'll drop you off at my cabin. You can stay there, or go to the reporters' place. I heard you've been staying there lately."

"Thank you. That'll do nicely," said Ivan.

"You cats did the right thing," said Conway, "and of course, my faithful dog," he added, petting the dog's head. Zachary wagged his tail happily.

The two cats padded off and soon met with Samantha and Dave, who were walking down the sidewalk to the news van. The journalists had stopped by a store to buy some groceries before returning to the cabin.

"Geronimo, there you are!" Samantha said cheerfully.

"We got you some of those sardines you like," added Dave.

Geronimo purred loudly and turned to Roxanne. "Would you like to come to the lodge and eat with us?"

"Thank you, but my human Mabel will be missing me," Roxanne purred back. "I'll see you later, Geronimo."

Roxanne touched noses with Geronimo and bounded off towards the governor's mansion.

Back at the storage warehouse, Venancio had returned. He sheepishly walked into the room where Gorgonio was sitting.

"No pelts," Gorgonio observed.

"They've got these other animals helping them," Venancio tried to justify. "Two cats and this big wolf-dog..."

Gorgonio would have none of it. He banged his fist on the table and thundered:

"Fuck it, Venancio, I don't care who they've got helping them! The governor wants those foxes. From the sound of it, they're the same two foxes that keep evading us and I want their skins if only as trophies! Do you understand me?"

"Well, it can't be done," responded Venancio, looking defiantly at Gorgonio.

Theron walked in and, ignoring the scene before him, simply stated, "All the electrical outlets are functioning properly."

Gorgonio looked from Venancio to Theron and back, saying, "We'll deal with this fox issue later. If Ulrich asks, we'll say we're still hunting them and to hell with it."

Chapter 18 - The Longguo Ambassador

Samantha and Dave had only two days left to verify all that their anonymous source had said. The election was tomorrow, and with it arctic fox hunting season would officially open. The matter of Denise and the landscaping company had made for an interesting investigative report, but it did not prove definitively that the poachers were being paid to hunt foxes, nor did it address the involvement of Ulrich or the Longguo government. There was no document - public or at the very least, obtainable - which they could use as proof of the corruption, so what remained was what Samantha had wanted to leave for last: the confrontation interviews.

Both the reporter and her cameraman knew these would not be easy tasks. It was one thing to simply get the statements of Ulrich and Qiang; it was quite another to try to trick them into revealing the corruption - and consequently, verifying Roxanne's account. Neither was certain what would be done if this also failed...airing an incomplete report consisting solely of an anonymous source's charges was out of the question. Nevertheless, Samantha and Dave remained positive and determined to reveal the truth somehow.

It was common newsroom knowledge that the ambassador generally did not grant interviews to foreign journalists. Samantha ascertained this was likely because of the straightforwardness of these interviews - the inquiries mostly relating to the human rights abuses taking place in Longguo, and the distrust between Longguo and Sarrilla. If Qiang only wanted the favorable coverage that his country's censored news media gave, then Samantha would pretend to be doing a sympathetic human interest story. They had the perfect one...the upcoming anniversary of the present Longguo regime's capture of power. Hinting over the telephone that this was the story she was covering was enough to secure an interview with Ambassador Qiang for later that day.

They were more blatant with Governor Ulrich. Samantha dryly informed him over the phone that her news network had potentially damaging information it would be airing, which behooved him to give an explanation. They got the interview with Ulrich scheduled before Qiang's.

The sun was shining brightly that day and the weather was becoming warmer. Samantha and Dave were able to forgo their winter coats, the reporter wearing her typical office attire and the cameraman with a hooded sweater.

They left Geronimo at the TV station and made it to the governor's mansion early. They had the camera rolling as they were waved into his office by his secretary, and they found him seated at his desk, watching television. He was channel-surfing with the remote control, but upon seeing the pair he returned the television to WCAT's channel and shut it off.

"Ms. West; Mr. Candid." His pale blue eyes held an evident dislike of them, yet his voice was smooth and maintained the charm expected of a politician running for re-election. "I was told you had received some...incomplete information?"

"It's complete," Samantha told him. "All we'd like to have is your explanation of why."

"Well, then?"

"We have proof you're the one financing the fox poaching, and that you're involved in the poaching ring in which the furs are sold to a foreign dignitary. Do you have any comment on that?" bluffed Samantha.

"Certainly," said Ulrich. "You have everything mixed up. The information you have is entirely false."

"Why is it false?"

"That information is rather sensitive," he said, with a glance at the camera.

"You're not the Minister of Defense," Samantha squinted at him.

"Ms. West," said Ulrich, almost as if trying to explain something rudimentary, "I am prepared to offer you a complete explanation, but only if that explanation is kept off the record. Surely," he added with another sharp glare at the camera, "you don't want to be airing an untrue story?"

Samantha eyed him suspiciously; he glared back at her, well aware that he had the upper hand. Eventually, Dave murmured to Samantha, "I'm shutting the camera off."

He clicked it off, and Samantha sighed. Ulrich looked satisfied. "All right," Samantha said, "What is this 'sensitive' information?"

Ulrich leaned back, visibly more relaxed now that they were no longer recording. "Samantha West," he began, retrieving a small box of cigarettes from his pocket, "I understand your desire to cover this story. The media isn't all that different from any other business. It's all a matter of consumers...high TV ratings." He offered her one of the cigarettes; when she declined, he lit it with a small lighter and began smoking. "Scandal has always been a favorite of your profession. The masses adore it. And you - both of you - recognize opportunity. You notice the story where the rest only see politics. In that way, you aren't that different from most entrepreneurs; though you've been successful in your field for more than that. I've seen quite a few of your news stories, and I am well aware that together you are one of your station's greatest assets. Candid, your films are very thorough, and they make an excellent accompaniment to West's talent, and - if I may say - beauty? ...Do you always work on stories as a team?"

"Cut the flattery and get to the point," Samantha hissed.

"My point is, Ms. West, that certainly you must realize your potential goes beyond the meager rewards of news reporting. A reporter's salary isn't that much. Certainly not befitting you."

He stood up from his seat and walked around to where they were. "Haven’t you ever wanted to travel? On pleasure, not business. Go shopping maybe; get yourself a fox coat..."

Samantha glanced over at Dave, who was visibly annoyed, but turned to look the governor straight in the eyes at this remark.

"...Arctic fox?" she asked.

Ulrich smiled, without saying a word; almost as if suggesting that if she so desired it, he would procure the fur coat for her. "So perhaps we can come to an understanding," the governor said. He walked back to his desk, and sat down. "I have been known to be quite generous. Say...50,000? Each."

There was a pause as the offer sank in. "Why, governor," said Samantha, "when you put it that way..."

Ulrich seemed content, as if he was certain he had won the two journalists over. Samantha, however, was not finished. "...I start to realize how scared you really are about the truth. What's so terrifying about a few prying questions from a TV reporter? Do you really think you can bribe us? I'm a journalist, Ulrich...not one of your PR propagandists."

"I suggest you reconsider my offer, Ms. West," Ulrich said tersely. "I'm not going to make it twice."

"Go to hell," said Samantha.

Dave's affronted look at Ulrich's offer told him the photographer felt the same as Samantha. The governor smiled again, though almost in amusement as he looked down at the cigarette he held. "Talent," he mused, "but no foresight." He gave Samantha a furious glare. "Seeing as I can't reason with you, consider this advice. Drop the poaching story."

Samantha glared back at him. "Or...?"

"...Let's say WCAT will be airing a very touching memorial for two of its most beloved journalists." Ulrich's voice was low, but he kept his gaze fixed on Samantha.

Samantha didn't flinch. "Forgot that Sarrilla has freedom of the press, have we?"

"One of the most obsolete parts of the Sarrillian constitution," Ulrich retorted.

"Care to repeat that on the record?" Dave responded as he switched the camera back on. Its bright light shone over the reporter and the politician, who were still facing each other; like a cat with her back arched, daring a much larger wolf to pounce. There was silence for a moment, until finally Ulrich looked straight at the reporter and snarled, "No comment."

"Of course you don't," Samantha whispered.

"Get the hell out of my office." he added.

Samantha and Dave turned and left.

From the governor's mansion, Samantha and Dave headed straight to the Longguo Embassy. There was little time to stop and have lunch, although even if there had been, they knew it was better to get to their second interview quickly. Should Ulrich have decided to contact his business associate about the pair's investigation, they would no longer have the advantage of surprise.

They arrived at the Longguo Embassy and were told curtly by a guard to wait. Shortly afterward, Qiang came out personally to greet them.

"Ambassador Qiang Xue?" said Samantha.

"Samantha Verity West, very pleased to meet you," he replied in a pleasant voice, shaking her hand. More sharply, he said to his secretary in Chinese: "Get cups of tea." When she wordlessly turned to this task, he spoke again to the reporter, "Won't you come into my office and sit?"

He's very polite now, Samantha was thinking as she and Dave stepped into the ambassador's office, a 180 degree difference from what they're saying back at the newsroom. No doubt it's because he thinks we're here doing some uncritical feature story. I can just imagine his reaction when he figures out what we're really covering. She sat down at one of the chairs at the desk while Dave set up a camera and tripod; as the ambassador was sitting down, she glanced at her notepad and said, "So, it's been a year since the Longguo revolt?"

"Correct," the ambassador affirmed.

"And what do you feel has been accomplished in Longguo since then?" Samantha added, "What improvements have occurred because of it?"

Qiang seemed delighted with her question. "We have a new and better society," Qiang began, "Production is up at our factories; our economy is strong and vibrant..."

His long speech praising the benefits - real or imagined - that came from the coup d’état in Longguo, lasted for what seemed to Samantha like an eternity, during which time she patiently took notes and kept an eye on the secretary, who was preparing the tea. She glanced over at Dave, who looked just as bored as she was; when Qiang finally finished, she jumped to ask the next question.

"What about business overseas? ...There's a lot of trade between Sarrilla and Longguo, isn't there?" asked Samantha.

"Yes, Sarrilla is one of Longguo's greatest trade partners," Qiang answered.

"Including arctic fox pelts?"

There was stunned silence for a moment, during which the only sound was when the telephone outside his office began to ring, and the secretary quickly left the teacups to answer it. When Qiang remained speechless from astonishment, Samantha dropped her voice down to a whisper. "Now, let's be frank, ambassador. We know the Nortenya governor, Victor Ulrich, is selling you the fox skins which you ship to Longguo. It doesn't matter to me; I've always rather admired Longguo's system and so I'm not extremely interested in your buying the furs. I'm more interested in what this means as far as Ulrich goes."

"Ambassador Qiang?" It was the secretary, holding the telephone receiver and standing at the office doorway. She spoke in their native Chinese language. "The governor of Nortenya is on the line; he would like to speak with you."

"Tell him to wait!" Qiang snapped at his secretary, in the same language. "I'll be at the warehouse office at 11 p.m. tomorrow; he can explain about these journalists then!"

"Yes, Ambassador," she said, turning wearily back to the telephone receiver.

Qiang turned back to the reporter, who was staring expressionless at him.

"I have no idea what you are talking about," Qiang told her in a docile voice.

"No idea?" Samantha persisted.

"None." Qiang seemed irked.

"So then you have no knowledge of the fact that your embassy is shipping arctic fox pelts to Longguo?"

"No comment."

"What about the secret business arrangement you have with Governor Ulrich? Doesn't that undermine whatever trust your embassy was trying to build between Longguo and Sarrilla?"

"No comment," Qiang retorted. "Who has been telling you these lies?"

"No comment," the reporter quickly responded.

The diplomat glared at her. His secretary walked in at this point with the tea, as Qiang told Samantha: "You unscrupulous reporters have no reverence for those in power. In my country," he added, the look in his eyes hinting at some unspoken cruelty, "we have special ways of reasoning with your kind."

"This is not Longguo," said Samantha calmly. "In Sarrilla we have freedom of the press and speech. Our people are an informed, educated society that takes truth seriously...not to mention humane treatment of all living things."

"Get out," ordered Qiang.

He was surprised to see a smile spread across the reporter's face.

"Thank you for your time, ambassador," Samantha said. "Have a nice day."

That being said, the reporter and her cameraman left the office.

Once they were outside, Samantha turned to Dave and grinned. "Let's go get something to eat, Dave," she said. "We just got our story."

The two journalists went to the Chinese restaurant where they had previously waited for Washburn. They ordered food, and as they were waiting, Samantha explained:

"Ambassador Qiang said he would be at the warehouse at 11 p.m. tomorrow, and that he expects Governor Ulrich to explain our investigating then. Tomorrow is a Friday, and if the warehouse is the same one where the poachers were spotted and Washburn was shot..."

"...that means we've got the time and place for the fox fur exchange," Dave finished.

"He said it was an office within the warehouse," elaborated Samantha.

"Roxanne told us there was an office in the regional warehouse," the cameraman said. "Sam, if Qiang knew you spoke Chinese, he would kill you."

When the waiter came with the food and drinks, the manager was following. "...If Ambassador Qiang says he wants these journalists dead, then you do not question it," he was insisting to the waiter. "One sip of these drinks and the paramedics won't get here in time to save them." He turned to Samantha and Dave and in a rather coy way asked, "...How is everything?"

"Very good, thank you," she responded. The waiter set the plates and drinks down and walked away with the manager following.

Samantha was poking at a chunk of chicken, and when Dave reached for the goblet she said urgently:

"Don't drink anything, Dave. It's poisoned."

Dave lowered the glass in a disconcerted way and turned to look towards the kitchen. The waiter and manager were at the kitchen entryway talking in hushed voices. "Poisoned?" he whispered to her.

"Apparently it's enough for the ambassador to know we're investigating," replied Samantha.

"What do we do?" asked Dave.

"We've tried everything, Dave. There are no documents, no other sources, and no way of tricking anyone into talking. There's only one way to reveal the corruption," Samantha realized. "We need to go to the meeting tomorrow night and film it."

There was silence. Neither Dave nor Samantha were eating. Dave finally said, "We should just go and eat somewhere else."

The two got up and headed towards the front desk to pay. After Dave had paid the bill, he held the door open for Samantha and saw the manager looking at them sternly.

As they went through the doorway, Samantha turned and spoke to the manager in perfect Chinese, "Have a good day."

From outside of the restaurant, they could hear the manager yelling in Chinese, too indistinctly to be understood.

During all this time, Geronimo had escaped from the TV station and had run off to the governor's mansion, in the hopes of meeting up with his humans. As he padded around the snowy mansion grounds, he let out a faint hiss.

Where are they...?

"Meow," a familiar voice mewed. Geronimo looked up to see, perched on a bare tree branch...Roxanne. "Hunting for something?" she asked.

"Searching for my humans," Geronimo replied.

"You just missed them," Roxanne told him, "They were here recently; they left after having a hissy fit with Victor."

"What happened?"

Roxanne leapt down from the tree. "Victor tried to pay them money to stop investigating. They hissed at him and then he hissed back and threw them out of his office."

"Damn, and I missed it!" Geronimo growled. "Do you know where they went?"

Roxanne lifted a paw and gestured for Geronimo to look across the street; Geronimo turned and saw a Channel 8 news van parked on the curb here, with Samantha and Dave seated inside.

"Thanks Roxy," purred Geronimo, and scampered off.

Inside the news van, Samantha and Dave were eating burgers that they had ordered. Geronimo leapt in through the open window and landed on Samantha's lap.

"Purrrrrr..." Geronimo sniffed at the burger that Samantha was eating.

"Geronimo, we told you to wait at the TV station," Samantha said.

"Cats gotta roam," Geronimo answered, and flipped over on her lap to look at her upside down. "Can I have some?" he asked, reaching towards the food with a paw. Samantha gave him a piece of beef.

"You know, it's been a while since I called Leandra," Samantha remarked to Dave. "It's been one thing after another...and now the manager of a restaurant tried to poison us..."

She said this very naturally, and it took a moment for Geronimo to realize what she had said.

"Wait...they tried to poison you?" Geronimo was flabbergasted.

"Apparently on orders of the Longguo ambassador," explained Samantha.

"Obviously they want to censor our reporting," Dave said.

"What kind of human is he, anyway?" Geronimo meowed.

"A corrupt asshole," Samantha waved it off matter-of-factly. "Apparently they decided to act on the death threat Ulrich gave us."

"You received a death threat?" Geronimo was even more astounded.

Samantha didn't seem fazed at all. "Come on, let's get back to the newsroom. We still need to edit the interview footage."

As the news van drove off towards the television station, Geronimo couldn't keep from worrying that their investigative journalism was becoming a potentially lethal risk.

Chapter 19 - Geronimo’s worry

When Samantha and Dave arrived at the newsroom, Samantha sat down to adjust her report. Ever since they had first met Roxanne, she had been writing and revising a draft of the investigative story.

"It's starting to come together," Samantha remarked to Dave, who was standing behind her watching as she wrote the script. "We can put the clip of the warehouse meeting here."

"Presuming we get it," responded Dave. "There's still a chance they change their meeting place."

"That's what I'm concerned of," acknowledged Samantha. "The foxes are officially off the endangered list on midnight Friday. If we want to catch Ulrich at his corruption, this might be our last chance. He'll be able to dismiss anything we film after midnight as a legal business transaction. It might still be an interesting story, but there wouldn't be any proof Ulrich was involved in it beforehand or that he delisted the foxes to appease Ambassador Qiang."

"Hopefully Ted will let us stake out the warehouse," Dave said. "With so much going on with the election, he might want us somewhere else."

"That's true," Ted's voice broke in. They turned to see their editor watching them expectantly.

"Ted, we've finally got a lead in our investigation," Samantha told him. "I heard Ambassador Qiang say he was going to be at a warehouse office at 11 tonight. Our source told us they typically exchange the furs at night on Fridays, and we've heard a lot about a regional warehouse on Watt Street," continued Samantha. "We'd like to go to there and see who shows up and what they do."

"Everyone's supposed to show up there?" asked Ted.

"Everyone except Denise Ralston," responded Samantha.

"Samantha, all the polls are projecting Ulrich will be the election winner. We're going to do the usual continuous news broadcast starting from 11 o'clock onward as the votes are tallied up. We need everyone here at night to help with the news coverage," Ted said. "The Irving campaign is holding their election night rally at the Black Fox Casino, while Ulrich's is being held at the convention center. We need entire news teams at both locations to give live reports...and I want you two, plus two of the local reporters, covering Ulrich's party."

"This is our last chance," Samantha insisted.

"You've been following this story for over a month now," Ted pointed out. "Most of your leads have turned up cold. Are you sure there's even a verifiable story there?"

"Positive," Samantha replied. "That's why we've got to show up tonight."

"They have the corruption so well hidden, in order to bring it to light we'll need to film them in the act of trading the furs." added Dave. "If we get them on tape, we can report it."

There was a tense silence between them for a moment. The determination of both Samantha and Dave was evident, a sort of passionate energy to reveal the truth, and their editor understood it implicitly.

"Go for it." Ted said finally. "However, I still want you to cover Ulrich's election night rally. I expect you two there by 11:30 at least to give a report as the votes start coming in."

"All right," said Samantha.

"If you don't show up at the convention center," Ted told them, "and the candidates are giving their speeches and I haven't heard from you, I'll want to know why."

He sounded stern, but both Samantha and Dave knew their editor was concerned for them. What they were planning to do was risky, should they be caught.

"We'll show up," Samantha smiled.

The afternoon turned into evening and darkness fell over the city. Ted walked through the newsroom surveying the staff, who was there and who wasn't. He saw Samantha and Dave still at work at a desk. "It's getting late. You guys have been here since early today; go home and get some rest. You've got another long day tomorrow," he said to them.

"Ok Ted, thanks," answered Samantha.

Geronimo, meanwhile, had snuck away. All this time, he had been aimlessly exploring the newsroom, but at some point he escaped downstairs to the TV station's lobby. Here he waited until someone coming inside the building left the door partially open.

"Freedom!" he yowled, and bolted out the door before anyone had the chance to close it. He ran as fast as his legs could go. He felt free and was enjoying the run; until he reached the corner, turned...and almost bumped into Roxanne. Both cats screeched and jumped backwards trying to avoid a collision.

They both stood there in surprise until Geronimo finally said, "I had a wild kitty moment."

Roxanne answered back quickly, "You hit the nip, haven't you?"

"Maybe," answered the tom, sheepishly.

Roxanne purred. "I decided to prowl over here because things are getting overly hectic at the mansion. You know how the elections are tomorrow night? Well, Victor's been practicing his speeches ad nauseum and conferring with his campaign manager and PR agents. They keep discussing something about how much confetti they should throw when he wins."

"Confetti is fun," Geronimo pointed out.

"It's the one highlight of having to attend the election night rally," Roxanne sighed. "Mabel and I have been to a bunch of events already, and they're predictable. Everyone knows he's going to win; his opponent can't catch up to him in the polls. Besides, the election night parties are always so noisy."

"Roxy," said Geronimo, "do you have anything to do tomorrow morning?"

"Not really. Why?"

"I was hoping you could drop by the cabin tomorrow early in the morning," meowed Geronimo. "I wanted to discuss something with you and the foxes Ivan and Natasha...about my humans' investigation."

"What about it?"

"They almost got killed earlier," Geronimo hissed.

Roxanne twitched her tail. "I was concerned about something like that."

"I've got to get them to stop this investigating," meowed Geronimo. "The whole thing seemed fun...to try and stop the poaching...but this is getting out of hand. The minute they start receiving death threats and attempts on their lives..."

"I can see what you mean," Roxanne considered, stretching. "Look, I'll drop by the cabin around sunrise. We can figure something out then, but I doubt your humans will approve."

"Either way, I've got to do something to protect them," Geronimo answered. "Thanks, Roxanne."

Around this time, Samantha and Dave walked out of the TV station. Roxanne mewed a greeting as she and Geronimo hurried towards them.

"Where are we going?" asked Geronimo, padding over with his tail held high.

"Heading back to the cabin," replied Dave.

"So no investigation stuff?" Geronimo questioned hopefully.

"Not until 11 p.m., anyway," Dave answered.

"We're going to ambush the gangsters tomorrow night, right in the middle of their meeting," Samantha announced.

"It's dangerous," Geronimo meowed. For the first time in his life, the tomcat had the distinct realization of his humans' mortality. "You might wind up getting shot...like almost happened a week ago when we saved Ivan and Natasha."

Samantha and Dave exchanged a glance. "Ger, you know our profession was never the safest," said Dave.

"Can't you let someone else finish investigating?" he mewed.

Samantha squinted at him. "If everyone thought like that, no one would do the story. We have an obligation to our viewers to ensure the truth gets revealed. Somebody's got to take the risk and expose the corruption. If we don't, who will?"

Geronimo flattened his ears. "I don't see how it's worth risking your lives."

Samantha crouched down to where he was and stroked him on the head. "Geronimo, democracy lives by truth, and the free press is the guardian of that democracy. We swore to it; and we have a job to do...but I want you to be safe. Please...whatever happens...stay out of trouble."

Geronimo twitched his tail but didn't respond. He cast his gaze down at the sidewalk, towards his striped, grey paws.

Roxanne swished her tail. "I'll see you tomorrow, Geronimo," she meowed, and scampered off.

Within an hour, the reporter and her cameraman arrived at the cabin where they were staying.

Later, Dave looked out the window of the bedroom. From the second floor, the forest was quite visible and the northern lights was putting on quite a show in the sky. Samantha was standing in front of a mirror, brushing her hair, and glanced over to him. Dave glanced back.

"These celestial lights really make me think about how complex our planet is," he said.

Samantha put the brush down and walked over to the window. "Yes," she answered, "Our planet is itself a living being and people must live in harmony with it."

Dave turned to her and they hugged each other. They stood there together, in each other’s arms, for a long time in silence, looking out at the aurora borealis display. Not much needed to be said between them. They loved each other and had loved each other for a very long time. They both knew the adventures and dangers that were part of their profession, and held a deep belief that every moment in life should be lived with passion and good memories, cherished.

Dave took Samantha's face in his hands and looked into her eyes. Her green eyes shone with the light that reflected from the night sky. He kissed her, and she kissed him back.

"I love you," they both said at the same time, and they laughed. He picked her up, carried her to the bed, and they kissed again, their warm bodies enveloping each other.

Outside, the night sky was alive with brilliant color; the northern lights swaying amidst the cold night air.

At the Longguo Embassy, Ambassador Qiang Xue was on the telephone.

"My son, you're a clever scientist; your research is of tremendous importance. Do what the emperor tells you to do. There's a second call on the line. I will call you back." Qiang answered the other call. "...Yes?"

"Ambassador Qiang?" The restaurant manager's voice seemed tremulous. "I apologize for bothering you in your very important work... The two journalists are still alive. They did not drink the poisoned beverages..."

"You unreliable idiot!" Qiang was enraged. "Don't think you won't be punished for such lamentable stupidity!"

"No...please! I beg your forgiveness, most honorable ambassador! There was no way I could have known the lady spoke Chinese!"

Qiang thought about this briefly. "Very well," the diplomat at last said, seriously. "But bear in mind that I shall not tolerate any further mistakes."

When he hung up the telephone, he turned to one of his guards and said:

"The two journalists have not been silenced. See that the manager of the Hao Chi restaurant is silenced in their place. He failed in his assignment. Failure is inefficiency."

Chapter 20 - Geronimo’s mission

It was Friday, and election day. The sun was just beginning to filter through the pine trees that morning as Geronimo and the two foxes sat in the clearing outside of the cabin.

Geronimo proposed that this morning he, the two foxes, and Roxanne meet to discuss the matter of Samantha and Dave's investigation becoming dangerous. It was logical, since they all had a stake in it; Geronimo, however, did not tell Ivan or Natasha that Roxanne was the anonymous source, but rather that she was a friend of his and as the governor's house-pet she knew Ulrich would act on his threats. The foxes agreed that the issue was an important one.

The sound of rustling in the bushes made the critters alert. Roxanne emerged from the underbrush into the clearing.

"Hi everyone," she purred.

"Well, we're all here," meowed Geronimo, as he leapt onto the hood of the news van. "We may as well start the meeting."

"What exactly is this thing about your humans?" queried Natasha.

"As we know, Samantha and Dave are investigating the poaching," Geronimo began. "I'm worried about them. Just yesterday they got a death threat from Governor Ulrich. Then they were nearly poisoned at a restaurant."

"When Victor gives a threat like that, he intends to carry it out," Roxanne hissed. "Even more so if they don't back off of their investigating. Remember Ranger Conway? The only reason he didn't make another attempt on his life, is because Conway decided to give up."

"Samantha and Dave are dedicated to their jobs," Geronimo explained, "so dedicated that they seem willing to put themselves in harm's way for it."

"I see where this is going," Ivan said.

"Exactly," hissed Geronimo. "Tonight they're planning to ambush Ulrich and the poaching ring at a meeting they're having over at that regional warehouse."

"That's like suicide if they get caught," observed Natasha.

Geronimo nodded. "I can't let my humans put themselves in any more danger."

"You're right about that," Ivan agreed. "We can't let the feeders get shot."

"Yeah...and more than just being feeders, to me they're family," Geronimo added. "I know how important stopping the poachers are, but it might end up killing my humans."

"Unless we convince your humans about how serious this is getting," reasoned Roxanne. "I don't like Victor, and I'd like to see him get punished...but not at the expense of anyone's life."

"So what's the plan?" barked Ivan.

An hour or so later, Geronimo flexed his claws as he watched Samantha type the number 30 at the end of her script. She was writing up a news report on the pre-election polls. According to the polls, Ulrich would win by a landslide. Geronimo was only half paying attention to what his human was writing, however. He was reviewing the plan he and the other critters had come up with that morning to stop Samantha and Dave from getting in harm's way.

There's nothing we can do until later, though, Geronimo thought, and turned his attention elsewhere. He began observing everyone in the newsroom. He knew it was election day, and the newsroom would be in its usual flurry of activity by nighttime as the votes were counted, but at the moment there was little activity. Other than the surprise of hearing that the manager of the Chinese restaurant had been shot to death earlier in the morning - another reporter had been sent out to cover that - not much else had been happening besides the routine reports on the pre-election polls. Most everyone was sitting around, either typing scripts or editing video.

"Looks like it's a slow news day today," observed Geronimo.

"Don't say that!" Samantha chided. "It's a journalist superstition. It means a huge story will break and we'll have to spend overnight covering it."

"Oh." Geronimo licked a paw.

"We've already got the election coverage all night," Dave, who had walked over to Samantha, shrugged. He was carrying two mugs of coffee emblazoned with the network's logo; he handed one to Samantha. "It's just stating the obvious."

"Maybe," said Samantha with squinted green eyes as she grasped the coffee mug with both hands and sat back in her chair. "But I don't want to take any chances of us getting called off on another story, with our stake-out planned for tonight."

The rest of the day passed with nothing eventful, and when nighttime came Samantha and Dave went to give a live report from outside one of the polling places, announcing the close of the voting period.

"Can't I come?" Geronimo meowed as they were waiting for the elevator heading down. "Purrrrrlease?"

"No, Ger," Dave replied. "We're heading from there to the warehouse. It's too dangerous for you to tag along."

"Stay here at the TV station," Samantha told Geronimo. "If all goes well, we should be back by 1."

"If all goes well," the tomcat pointed out.

"Don't be pessimistic, Geronimo," Samantha smiled, trying to cheer him up. "We'll be back before you know it."

Geronimo said nothing as the elevator doors opened and his humans stepped inside.

When the doors had closed, the cat scampered away. He ran down the hallway outside of the newsroom until he reached a small window. The Siamese-mix tomcat leapt up, pushed the window pane open and escaped onto a section of the roof, judiciously closing the window behind him with a paw.

At the governor's mansion, Ulrich was in his office organizing some papers on his desk. As he stood up and headed toward the open door, Denise walked in.

"Have you got the envelope?" he asked her.

"Yeah, here," she answered, handing it to him.

Ulrich opened the manila business-sized envelope and counted the bills quickly. He took some dollars out of the batch and handed them back to Denise, "Take these, and put them back," he said.

"What's this?" asked Denise, waving the money. "A tip for me?" she asked half-jokingly.

"Like hell," answered Ulrich. "Those morons haven't been bringing in enough fur pelts and I'm docking their pay."

"Bad idea Victor. They might decide to blackmail us," she said.

"I didn't ask for your opinion, bitch. And what do you mean us? This isn't your racket," he responded.

Denise was visibly angry and yelled at him, "Without me, you couldn't get this business arrangement going. I'm not getting grabbed by the authorities just because you don’t want to pay those idiots you hired!"

Ulrich slapped her hard across the face and grabbed her by the hair, "Listen, bitch. I'm the boss, yesterday, today and tomorrow. Remember that." He released her and went out the door.

Denise put her hand to her cheek and with an intense look of hatred, said to herself, "We'll see about that, Governor."

Outside, Ulrich was getting into his car and the chauffeur walked over to greet him. "Sir, I was on my way home, but if you need me to drive you somewhere..."

Ulrich interrupted him. "No," he said abruptly, and got into his car and drove off.

When Ulrich arrived at the warehouse, he noticed that the ambassador's limousine was already there. "Fuck," he said to himself. "I hate it when he gets here before I do."

Close by, the WCAT Channel 8 news van was pulling up to the curb. From inside the vehicle, Samantha and Dave could see the governor get out of his car and lock it.

"I hope this goes well," Dave remarked. "If we get spotted, we're history."

"We've got no choice, Dave," replied Samantha. "We'll just have to sneak close enough to get the shot of them with the furs, and then sneak away before they realize we're there. Where's my microphone?"

Dave turned toward the back of the news van, and then muttered, "Oh, great."

Samantha looked over to see four determined critters sitting in the back of the news van. "Geronimo!" exclaimed Samantha.

"...and friends," purred Roxanne. Geronimo had both front paws on the microphone bag, while Ivan, Natasha and Roxanne were clustered around the camera bag.

"We're here to stop you from putting yourself in unnecessary danger yet again," announced Geronimo.

"We don't have enough time for this," said Samantha. "If we don't get over there now, we'll miss getting them on camera."

"But Samantha...!" Geronimo yowled.

"Geronimo, this is something we have to do." Samantha told him. "You'll understand why, some day."

She tugged the microphone bag loose from his claws and quickly retrieved the microphone from inside. The foxes yapped and Roxanne hissed, but the photographer also got the camera out of the other bag. Samantha and Dave jumped out of the news van, closing the doors behind them, and hurried to connect the microphone cable to the camera before racing off towards the warehouse. Geronimo leapt to the dashboard and watched his humans run off.

"We tried," barked Natasha.

Hiding near the warehouse, Samantha and Dave were immersed in filming the governor as he entered the storage building. The TV news crew snuck closer to the door, where they could barely overhear voices inside the building, fading into the back. The news reporter motioned to her cameraman to come around the side of the building, where they carefully stepped through the icy remainder of the snow. This entire side of the building was windowless, except for a lone window surrounded by overgrown holly bushes. "What if they changed their exchange place to deep inside the building, where we have no way of seeing?" Dave whispered to Samantha as they approached the window.

At that moment a light came on in the window; Samantha and her companion pressed themselves closer to the wall. They heard the Longguo ambassador speaking and as Samantha held the microphone near the window, Dave began filming the scene inside. "I must admit after you cancelled our meeting, I was beginning to doubt whether you were still interested in business."

"Would I really shirk profit?" said a voice that sounded like the governor's.

"Speaking of profit," a clearly annoyed Gorgonio spoke up, "you haven't given us our part of the money for hunting those foxes last week."

Ulrich glared at Gorgonio. "You'll get your half. Bring the merchandise."

Gorgonio turned his gaze to Theron and Venancio, who were standing on the side; both left to get the crates of furs.

From what Samantha and Dave could see from the window, those present were Ambassador Qiang and two of his bodyguards, Governor Ulrich, and Gorgonio; apart from Theron and Venancio, who brought in first one, then two wood crates. They placed them atop the table in the center of the room and opened one, revealing numerous arctic fox pelts. They seemed to gleam white in the dim illumination of the warehouse. Qiang examined the furs and, apparently satisfied, placed his suitcase on the table and opened it. Inside were rows and batches of cash, clearly visible from the window.

"Payment includes that for other crate," said Qiang.

"Very good," said Ulrich, taking the suitcase. He shook Qiang's hand. "Nice doing business with you."

"As always," said Qiang. "You are now leaving to the election night party?"

"Yes," responded Ulrich. "We're ahead in the polls. It should be a landslide victory."

"Your country is so inefficient, with its periodic elections," said Qiang dismissively. "In Longguo we appoint officials as needed. No use catering to the dumb masses."

Gorgonio, who had his arms crossed and was leaning against the wall in annoyance, impatiently said, "And now..."

Ulrich half-threw a bulky manila envelope at him, which Gorgonio caught easily and proceeded to count the bills inside. At that moment, Denise Ralston walked through the door, dressed for the election party in a sparkling, midnight-blue evening gown. She was wearing the arctic fox stole.

Qiang glanced over at her, visibly angry. "Why is she here?"

Ulrich seemed surprised as well. "What the hell are you doing here?!" he snapped at her. "You're never to show up at these meetings!"

"Oh really?" she scoffed. "I'm the one laundering the money and embezzling it out of the regional funds to pay these poachers of yours. And you don't think I have the right to drop in?"

"What the hell is this?" Gorgonio suddenly broke in, showing Ulrich the envelope furiously. "This is for one crate of furs, not two! You owe us money for poaching those damned foxes! Not to mention for that job shutting up the wildlife minister that I did a month ago!"

Theron looked taken aback, and the words escaped him from astonishment: "...you tried to kill Washburn?!"

"...and a fine job you did of it," Ulrich snarled, ignoring Theron, "since Washburn's alive and talking!"

"I made him sign those papers you wanted to take the foxes off of the endangered list," Gorgonio retorted. "It's not my fault those reporters showed up."

"It is your fault that you didn't make sure he was dead!" Ulrich countered. "It's a wonder you're even able to hunt foxes being so inefficient. Or are they already dead of starvation by the time you remember to check your traps?"

"The pot calling the kettle black," sneered Gorgonio. "If you weren't so full of yourself maybe you'd remember that people don't work for you for free!"

The governor whipped out a revolver he had hidden inside his coat and aimed it at Gorgonio. "What did you say...?"

Gorgonio raised his hands disarmingly and took a step back. "Nothing."

"Sam, we'd better get out of here," Dave, outside, whispered to Samantha.

Samantha had not taken her eyes off the unfolding scene inside the building, but at Dave's words, she stepped back to leave.

She was suddenly taken off balance as her heel caught on the microphone wire. Dave tried to catch hold of her but she fell backwards into the holly bush with a gasp.

The loud crash of the leaves made everyone inside look unanimously in their direction; Samantha and Dave froze.

There was silence for a lingering moment. "Run for it!" Samantha shouted to Dave.

The television crew made a dash for the news van as Ulrich gestured with the revolver for the poachers to go after them.

Samantha and Dave leapt in and, slamming the doors shut, put the van sharply into reverse. The tires screeched as the vehicle pulled back. Geronimo and Roxanne let out a caterwaul as inertia forced them about, while Ivan and Natasha scrambled for a hold on something.

Gorgonio sprang out of the building, lifting his rifle and firing two or three shots at them, when without warning Ulrich arrived. He pushed the rifle's muzzle down to point at the asphalt ground. "No, you fool! Don't kill them!"

"What the..." Gorgonio protested.

"The photographer was recording," said Ulrich. "I want that videotape and I want to know who tipped them off!"

With a disenchanted smirk, Gorgonio again fell in pursuit.

The TV news van halted suddenly as the diplomat's car blocked their escape route. Dave shifted gears and hit the acceleration pedal; the van sped forward. From the back of the van, Geronimo let out a hiss.

Samantha hurriedly took the TV camera from where it was placed beside Dave. "We've got to save the tape, Dave," she said.

"Hide it in the back somewhere," Dave told her.

She shut off the camera and ejected the videocassette as the hunters' pick-up blocked their second exit. Their speeding TV news van was now trapped between two cars and an imminent crash with the warehouse's brick wall.

With a sudden movement, Dave hit the brake; the news van skidded sideways and the reporter and her cameraman were thrown forward in their seats.

This was enough time for the poachers to arrive and rush over. Gorgonio pulled open the unlocked door and he and Venancio forced Dave out, while Samantha ducked into the back of the news van with the camera.

Samantha placed the camera on the table before the broadcasting equipment and looked around for a place to hide the videotape. Turning at the sound of a meow, she saw Geronimo and Roxanne. They had hidden underneath the driver's seat, where they could cling to it with their claws and avoid being thrown about the automobile; both cats had wide black eyes. The two foxes were under the passenger seat, their bushy tails swishing from side to side.

"Take this to the TV station, Geronimo," Samantha whispered, pushing the tape under the driver's seat before the cats could respond. "Whatever you do, don't come back."

"But..." Geronimo protested.

"Don't come back," Samantha reiterated. She turned back to the camera, seizing a blank tape that was on the rack here and loading it into the camera just as Gorgonio appeared inside the news van.

The lead hunter aimed his rifle at her. "Hand me the camera, or else you won't be alive at five."

He underestimated Samantha.

She placed one hand on the camera's handle but as he got closer, she grabbed a folded tripod with her other hand and hit him over the head. He let out a surprised cry and doubled over with pain.

"This just in, you son of a bitch," Samantha snapped and tried to push her way past him with the camera. Gorgonio grabbed her arm and when she spun around, he pushed her back against the broadcasting equipment and the antenna lever, the latter of which was thrust upwards from the impact. He seized her as she fought to get loose; her jacket was pulled off in the process.

Freeing herself, she tried to make her way past the two front seats again, this time managing to get outside before a blow from behind caught her off guard, and she shrieked, seizing her leg at the hip. Gorgonio had hit her with the rifle.

Geronimo nearly leapt out of his hiding place at the sound of his human's cry. "Let me at him!"

"No, Geronimo!" Roxanne hissed, biting down on his collar to pull him back. "He'll kill you!"

Gorgonio forced the camera away from the injured Samantha, and then hurled her cruelly against the side of the news van. She gasped as she fell to the asphalt.

Gorgonio handed the camera to Ulrich, who had approached along with Qiang and Denise.

Ulrich ejected the videocassette, tossing the camera carelessly to the ground and, as Samantha watched, he tore the film out of the cassette, pulled a lighter out of his pocket and set the film ablaze. He threw this on the ground too, and then roughly pulled Samantha to her feet.

Samantha stared rather forlornly at the remnants of the film smoldering on the asphalt. It occurred to her how close they had come to destroying the actual tape they had recorded and not just a blank one. It also occurred to her that she and Dave were likely going to be killed now that the evidence had supposedly been dealt with. Where is Dave? She couldn't see him anywhere.

Ulrich's gaze was cold. "All right, Samantha," he snarled, "I said to drop the poaching story, but you were set on having your exclusive. You're going to get more than a story now."

"Haste may lead to later ill." It was Ambassador Qiang. "An ancient rule states: You do not just kill your enemy, but the one who warned your enemy."

"Meaning, her anonymous source within the governor's mansion," said Ulrich, as Samantha struggled to get her arm loose from his grip.

"Who else would have told her so much about our business?" asked Qiang. "...or told her where we were meeting?"

"You told me where the meeting was yourself, Ambassador Qiang," replied Samantha in perfect Chinese.

Qiang was momentarily in shock. "Perhaps I did make the error of speaking in front of you at the embassy, and you learned of the warehouse meeting by overhearing me. However, I did not tell you that Longguo was involved. You would not have come to the embassy to begin with without someone having told you that."

"...and how about you damn reporters showing up at the hunting cabin?" interjected Gorgonio. "Our address wasn't exactly common knowledge."

"You're going to name your source," the governor told the news reporter.

"Not happening," said Samantha.

"I don't think you realize what kind of a situation you've gotten yourself into," countered Ulrich.

"I have a pretty good idea," she replied. "Either way, my anonymous source is staying anonymous."

"Oh, you won't reveal your sources," Ulrich smiled sarcastically. "Isn't that cute. The intrepid reporter, bound by her profession's ethics. Do you think that your source would remain silent if they were in your situation? I'll ask once more, nicely." Suddenly, the governor seized her by the nape of the neck, shaking her so harshly that she had to suppress a gasp. "Name your source, Samantha West! Name him or we'll make you!"

"Go to hell, you fascist son of a bitch!" she retorted.

Ulrich fixed his gaze on her, and Qiang broke in:

"Perhaps our young newswoman needs a bit more persuasion."

"Perhaps so," said Ulrich, turning back to Samantha.

"...and when I can't be 'persuaded'?" answered Samantha fearlessly.

"You will be," Ulrich responded dryly, and threw her violently to the side.

When she fell against the hood of the news van, she noticed something motionless on the ground. With a plummeting feeling, she realized it was her cameraman. His eyes were closed, and he didn't stir.

"Dave!" Samantha screamed out his name, devastated. "What have you done to Dave!?"

Everything happened so fast, Samantha didn't have a chance to react. Gorgonio had retrieved the glass vial of chloroform, poured some of the anesthetic on a handkerchief and grabbed her from the back. As he clapped the handkerchief over her nose and mouth, almost smothering her with it, she realized what he was doing and struggled helplessly to release herself from him. Yet what seemed even harder to Samantha, was not breathing in. It was an enticing scent; a soft, sugary-sweet fragrance that was mysteriously out of reach, tempting to inspire.
