Dizziness and drowsiness began to take hold of her, as first hearing and then vision began to fade, and at last she passed out, overpowered within moments by the quick sleep of the chloroform...

The others watched as her eyes closed and she went limp in the poacher's arms.

Ambassador Qiang reached down and picked up the reporter's press ID card. It had fallen on the ground from where it had been clipped to her skirt. "We must move fast. Take them into the building," the diplomat demanded.

The governor turned his attention to the hunters and ordered, "Hurry up, before that drug wears off."

"I told you that TV reporter would cause trouble," Denise irately told Ulrich.

Ulrich ignored her statement. "It's getting late. We ought to get to that election-night rally if we hope to preserve our image. Of all the times those stupid journalists had to show up, it had to have been tonight!"

"I can easily dispose of them," Gorgonio offered.

"No," Ulrich ordered him, "Then we'll never get the information we want. We'll be a couple of hours at the rally, so stay here with them until we get back. Don't kill them. And don't..." he added when a smirk crossed Gorgonio's face, "...do anything drastic."

"That takes all the fun out of this," Gorgonio complained. "Don't you want us to get them to talk?"

"I'll do that myself," Ulrich responded through clenched teeth.

As they dispersed, Ambassador Qiang studied Samantha's press card, along with Dave's, which he had also taken. Without saying anything, he put them in his coat pocket and left.

Inside the news van, the critters were still huddled under the seats, their eyes wide. Geronimo was looking down, despondently, at the videotape.

She's trusting us to get this to the station, he thought. With the fur rising along his back, Geronimo was suddenly struck with the painful awareness that the tape he had before him might very well be Samantha and Dave's final report.

Chapter 21 - Election Night

The darkness of the forest was mitigated only by the green glow of the northern lights above, which reached down through the pine branches to be reflected by the cold, melting snow. Geronimo, Roxanne, Ivan and Natasha were all somber as they trudged through the woods. They had crept out of the news van when they heard silence outside and, fearing being sighted, went into the forest. It was a detour from the direct city path to the WCAT television station, but the only sure-fire way they knew to safeguard the film which had been entrusted to them.

Geronimo held the videotape. The cassette was of a small, portable type that was not much bigger than the palm of one's hand, but for a cat, transporting it was an effort. After a while the jaws began to ache and breathing became hard. Seeing the struggle, Ivan offered to carry it at some point, and Geronimo relented and let the fox take it.

At last they reached a small clearing, with a slope overlooking the tundra, and a clear view of the aurora above. They stopped here for a rest. The world seemed noiseless, without even the singing of birds. Geronimo fluffed his fur against the cold, which had grown sharper since they had set out.

"What Ulrich said was true," Roxanne's voice broke the silence. "Nortenya is his, soon all of Sarrilla will be, and no one can stop him."

"Well, your humans were kind to try to help us," Ivan sighed. "They ended up giving their lives for it."

"I'm sorry, Geronimo," said Natasha, nudging the tomcat with her muzzle.

"I don't understand." Geronimo kept reviewing the scene in his mind. "Why would they put themselves in that danger? Why? They knew going there to film was dangerous."

"Journalists do stuff like that," replied Roxanne. "I heard a bunch of them are jailed in other countries."

Pawsteps made the critters alert. They looked towards the bushes to see Zachary, the park ranger's Husky dog.

"Zachary!" meowed Geronimo.

"I went out for a walk," he said. "I couldn't help but overhear...the news-people...your humans...?"

"They've been kidnapped," Geronimo sighed.

Zachary's head drooped. "...I'm sorry."

"They left us this tape," Geronimo continued. "It was Samantha and Dave's last request that it be taken to the TV station."

"The WCAT TV station? That's a long way off."

"We can't even go directly," added Natasha. "You know the regional warehouse on the outskirts of the city? That's where they were grabbed, so we've had to loop around through the woods to avoid being seen."

"If I carry the tape and run, I can probably get there faster than you could," barked Zachary.

"Thank you, Zach," said Geronimo, his eyes glistening with emotion.

The canine grabbed the videocassette and with a muffled woof, ran off into the woods.

"I'm going back to save my humans," Geronimo announced when Zachary had left.

"You're going to what?" Roxanne mewed.

"My humans have been good to me," Geronimo meowed. "I can't let them die without even trying to rescue them."

Ivan thought for a moment. "It's because of them, startling the hunter, that we're still alive. We owe them our lives," he said. "All right," he added, "I'm in."

"I'm in too," Natasha agreed. "It'll be a way to get back at those evil people for all the harm they've done to us foxes."

Roxanne hissed. "You're acting like lemmings."

"Roxanne..." began Geronimo.

"Geronimo, think about how ludicrous this is!" she hissed. "Two cats and two foxes going up against several armed men. And after how long dragging the tape here took us...I'm sorry, but your humans have probably been killed by now."

"They haven't," Geronimo meowed. "I sense that they're still alive. But if we don't do something fast, they will be."

"Geronimo," she said, "it's not worth risking your own life. Let someone else do it."

"If we don't, who will?" questioned the tomcat.

All the critters were speechless for a moment. "I think I get why they did it now," Geronimo said at last. "It was their job, kind of like our job as cats is to attack rats even though they can attack us back."

"What do rats have to do with this?" prompted Roxanne.

"We attack rats because it's for the common good. Rats harbor diseases," explained Geronimo. "This poaching problem was something that had to be dealt with for the common good. Someone had to take the risk, because if no one did the corruption would just keep getting worse and worse until all of Sarrilla would be under Ulrich's power, and then it wouldn't be foxes alone in trouble. Even the other humans would be. There would be no freedom for anybody..."

"That doesn't apply here," interrupted Roxanne. "Someone else can do this. The police, maybe."

"I thought the police chief was one of the people Ulrich was paying," pointed out Ivan. Roxanne gave a frustrated hiss.

"You're missing the point. You're going to end up getting killed."

"Not if we play our cards right," Geronimo meowed. "Roxy, we need your help to get inside without being seen. You know the inside layout of the warehouse."

"I saw a map of it once, that Denise had," Roxanne answered. "That building is a maze!"

"But you'd know how to sneak in!" Geronimo persisted.

"Hypothetically, yes," said Roxanne, flattening her ears. "Practically, I want no part in this."

"But Roxy..." Geronimo's mew went ignored as Roxanne bounded away.

Geronimo chased after her a short distance, until they were out of hearing range of the two foxes. Roxanne turned around to face Geronimo, her back arched.

"I'm heading to the election night party to hear that asshole Victor's acceptance speech. Mabel is probably concerned that it's late and I'm not there. I'm sorry about your humans, really...but we can't do anything for them anymore."

"All right Roxanne," Geronimo hissed. "If I can't convince you, I can't convince you. But realize my humans will probably die to protect your identity. The least you could do is help me, help them."

So saying, he turned and ran back to the foxes, leaving Roxanne gazing up at the northern lights, thinking.

While Zachary ran towards the city, Geronimo and the two foxes returned to the storage place. As they raced through the forest the only sound was the rustle of their paws through the snow and bracken. Their lithe forms were outlined against the pine trees, their breath visible in clouds of mist. Far into the city, WCAT news editor Ted Hughes was watching the various clocks on the newsroom wall. They displayed the hour in different time zones worldwide, with their time zone in the center. It was almost midnight, and the entire newsroom was a flurry of activity for their election-night broadcast. Ulrich had won a second term. His election to parliament next election cycle was assured, the political analysts and commentators all said, and his name was among those being spoken of as potential candidates for the prime minister's office in a few years. His popularity was outstanding, and a correlation was made between it and his having seemingly helped the arctic fox recover.

Yet Ted was becoming increasingly worried about the whereabouts of Samantha and Dave. "We'll lead the next block with the governor's rally and then his opponent's one, before we flip to the round table commentators," Ted was saying as he handed papers to a producer, who hurried off to the news studio. Ted glanced again at the clocks on the wall.

"...Where are Samantha and Dave?" he muttered to himself. "They should have called in hours ago!"

"Still no word from your reporters?" asked Devon, who had walked over from the studio.

"I'm worried what could be wrong," Ted answered.

"Maybe they forgot to call in," Devon considered.

"No," said Ted, "they're not like that."

As if on cue, Devon's secretary called from his office, "Mr. Gao, telephone."

"Thanks," Devon replied as he walked over to the desk and picked up the telephone receiver. "Hello? ...speak up, I can hardly hear you."

"Devon, it's Todd. I'm at the rally." The reporter on the other line was speaking over a background of zealous chants "Governor Ulrich! Integrity and Humanity!"

"And...?" asked the news editor.

"Samantha and Dave aren't here. They haven't called us, either. Are they at the station?"

"What? No, they aren't here. I haven't heard from them since..." Devon's voice trailed off.

At that point, Ted walked over and said, “Devon, let me talk to Todd.”

Devon handed the phone receiver to him, and Ted spoke quickly. “Todd, are Samantha and Dave there?” Ted asked.

“No, I haven’t heard from them, and the governor's about to speak,” added Todd.

Ted thought for a moment and recalled that the pair were last heading to investigate the rendezvous between the governor and the fox poachers. "They should still be at their last assignment," he said. There was silence. “Todd, go ahead with the broadcast. Call in if they show up,” the editor said, and hung up the phone.

He looked over at Devon, and the solemn look on his face said what they were both thinking. They both knew what Samantha and Dave had been investigating and what the disappearance of a reporter on that sort of story usually meant.

At the Longguo Embassy, the glittering black limousine with the Longguo flags, pulled up to the front of the building. Moments later, the distinguished ambassador would enter his office and toss the press cards on his desk; atop sprawled embassy paperwork professing only peaceful relations between the governments of Longguo and Sarrilla. Governor Ulrich, meanwhile, was stepping onto the stage at the election-night rally, to the glorifying cheers of the crowd. Not a single person could suspect the admired governor, the winner of the election; or his treasurer Denise Ralston, who sat at a table directly before the stage, the fox stole wrapped about her shoulders as she sipped champagne. The picture of high society, the darlings of good family, and the lead criminals of the poaching ring.

All this was unseen by the critters, who knew only the desperation they felt to reach Samantha and Dave...and the sense that although the journalists were still alive, somehow they would be too late.

Chapter 22 - Inquisitor’s First Degree

Darkness, total darkness. As the chloroform began to wear off, Samantha West began to gradually come out of the stupor she had been cast into. It felt like floating in nothingness. She could faintly hear people's voices around her, the sounds of talking in the background, and as she blearily opened her eyes, she felt a terrible pressure about her head. There was still a dull pain where she had been struck on the hip, but it was subsiding. The room she was in was dimly lit and shadowy; a very small room, enclosed tightly by metallic divisions - one of the warehouse storage units, she quickly discerned - and a red brick wall towards her back, the latter of which she could barely see out of the corner of her eye. The outskirts of the room were hidden by shadows, as the only light came from an ominously buzzing low-wattage lightbulb hung overhead from the ceiling's rusty wire mesh, and filtered in sporadically from the flickering fluorescent lights in the corridor. This only dimly illuminated the windowless room.

"Samantha! ...Samantha!" It was Dave's voice. She looked over and saw her photographer, seated a small distance to her left. He had a bruise on the side of his face, as if he had been punched; he was more worried about her, however.

"Dave...?" she said drowsily. "You're alive."

"They knocked us out, it seems, with chloroform," answered Dave.

Samantha was groggy, yet she recognized a voice in the distance and when Gorgonio stood in front of her, she nearly jumped in surprise, discovering in consequence that she was held down in some fashion. As her vision began to regain itself, she saw that she was sitting in an antique oaken chair; her wrists had been tied with rope to the armrests, her ankles were also bound, and she was restrained to the back of the chair with an encircling rope about her upper arms and middle. She soon realized Dave was in the same predicament, and seated in a similar chair. To her right, much closer than Dave, was a heavy oak wood table that appeared to be the match of the chairs; this was entirely bare except for the empty glass bottle of chloroform. There was a small stack of cardboard boxes in one corner of the room, but not much else.

Samantha began tugging vehemently against the ropes, and Gorgonio dismissively gestured to them. "Don't bother trying to break free - you can't. For that matter, calling for help is useless. The walls are so thick you wouldn't be able to tell if there was a storm outside."

Samantha's green eyes flashed defiantly at him, and he continued with a smirk, "Now that our enterprising little TV news crew is awake from the chloroform, we can get on with this. Samantha West, you and your coworker are powerless. If you want to live, you'll do what we want."

"I can't reveal my sources," said Samantha simply.

"Don't give me that bullshit; you can and you will," Gorgonio snapped. "After all, your camera guy here works behind the scenes. You have to stand in front of 8 million viewers. I wonder how long it would take you to get back on the air if you refuse to cooperate."

"Is that how that happened to Dave?" Samantha's green eyes seethed with anger.

"No, that was for the fun of it," Gorgonio sneered. "It's obvious you're the only one who knows the source; you're the reporter, after all."

He grabbed her by the collar of her blouse, and Dave spoke up, "We're a team. I know who the source is, just as she does."

"Really?" Gorgonio demanded. "Name the snitch then."

"We...can't." Dave replied, his eyes briefly meeting with Samantha's. "It's against our professional ethics."

The words sounded small, and Gorgonio seemed to find them amusing. He released Samantha's collar. "Wait until Ulrich gets back," he told them maliciously, "then we'll see whether your ethics mean more to you than your lives."

How much time had elapsed? Samantha's thoughts seemed to return infallibly to this. There was no window in the dark storage unit, no clock, no way of knowing if they had been there for minutes or hours. There was only her growing sleepiness which hinted at the lateness, yet she had not even the slightest perception of how long she had been unconscious from the chloroform to begin with. She might have asked Dave about this; however, there always seemed to be at least two of the hunters in the room with them at any given moment.

They were presently in the room with Gorgonio and Theron. Theron was standing at the doorway, a mixture of boredom and discontent reflected on his face. Gorgonio stood to the side, leaning against one of the metallic walls that divided the storage units. Once or twice, he spun the cylinder of a revolver he held in an idle manner, showing off the fact that he was passing time waiting for the governor. Neither one had spoken to the hostages since the exchange of words when they had come to. Dave fidgeted uncomfortably in his seat but stayed quiet, while Samantha had been tugging again at the ropes; somewhat weary from these unsuccessful efforts, she turned her attention to their captors.

"You know what strikes me as odd?" she said.

Gorgonio glared at her, and she went on without caring, "How you ever got hired by the governor. How'd you get the clout?"

"Shut up," he responded.

"Do you honestly think you'll get away with this?"

"Yes," came Gorgonio's answer.

"That's because you're an idiot," Samantha replied. "We're journalists. We were investigating a news story. Can you imagine the headlines if we turn up dead?"

"You will if you don't shut the fuck up!" Gorgonio shouted at her.

"Sam, don't antagonize them," Dave whispered to her.

"Why not?" she answered her photographer in a louder voice. "They're going to kill us either way."

"Yeah, but we don't have to rush them," Dave answered.

"All right," Gorgonio interjected, snapping the cylinder back into place and walking over to Samantha. "You want to talk? Then talk." He grabbed Samantha by her hair, and held the gun to the side of her head. "If you don't tell me who your source is by the time I count down to one, you're dead."

"You think that'll make me tell you?"

"Ten..." he began counting, "nine...eight...seven..."

Although Samantha couldn't see Dave, she could sense his tension; letting out a small sigh, she focused her attention on the wall in the corridor, beyond a visibly surprised Theron, and tried to relax. The muzzle of the gun felt astonishingly cold against her skin.

"...six...five...four...three..." - Samantha heard a sharp click - "two...any last words?"

"None," Samantha said, feigning indifference.

"One," said Gorgonio.

There was a pause that seemed to last centuries, when at last the trigger was pulled. There was only another click.

"Well," Gorgonio said bemusedly, as he released her, "will you look at that! Talk about a cheap game of Russian roulette. I forgot to load it with bullets!"

Samantha gave him an irritated look from narrowed green eyes; Dave, whose nerves appeared shattered from what had occurred, snapped at him, "Leave her alone, you rat."

"If you care so much about your little girlfriend," Gorgonio answered, "then why don't you tell us what we want to know?"

Dave didn't respond.

Gorgonio smirked and glanced from one to the other.

"You scum," he sneered at them. "You're the ones who posted my face all over the news broadcast. Thanks to you I haven't been able to show myself in town."

At that moment, Venancio stepped into the room carrying two paper bags which smelled of food. "Anyone hungry?" he asked.

"Yeah! Let's eat!" yelled Theron.

"It's about time you got back...let's go to the hallway with the food." ordered Gorgonio.

Venancio glanced at the hostages and asked, "What about them?"

"To hell with them," answered Gorgonio, "They can't escape, besides, we'll be back within minutes." The three men left the room, leaving Samantha and Dave alone. Dave looked at the floor in silence, while Samantha looked around the room trying to assimilate all her surroundings; perhaps out of habit she wanted to remember every detail of her captivity. Dave's voice broke through her thoughts. "They will kill us, you know." he whispered.

Samantha didn't respond. She was thinking about her sister Leandra, back on Tropical Island. I haven't called her for about two weeks. She's probably wondering how I'm doing. Her thoughts faded into happy memories of her childhood on the island.

Outside in the corridors of the warehouse, the hunters were sitting on the floor, eating. Theron spoke first.

"Shouldn't we, at least, offer them water?" he said.

"What the hell for?" snapped Venancio, "They're gonna die anyway."

Theron felt angry and yelled back at him, "Yeah right, so you be the one to tell Ulrich that they died 'cuz you wouldn't keep 'em hydrated! Sorry Gov, no info!"

"You damn bastard!" shouted Venancio and dropping his sandwich, threw himself at Theron, smacking his face. Before Theron had a chance to react, Gorgonio intervened.

"Stop it, assholes! Actually, the kid's got a point. We need to keep 'em alive till Ulrich gives the order to get rid of them. Theron, take them some water."

Theron rubbed his cheek and giving Venancio an angry look, grabbed a thermos and a cup, and went over to the room where the hostages were.

He found the two, trying to pull themselves free. They glanced up at the doorway as he walked in.

"Are either of you thirsty?" Theron offered. "I've got water."

Dave gave him a distrustful look, and Samantha cynically replied, "No doubt you've laced it with cyanide."

Theron poured some of the water in the cup and drank it. Samantha and Dave glanced at one another. "Ok," Samantha said.

Theron could tell, although they refused to admit such, that they were both thirsty. He refilled the cup and went to Samantha. "Don't let Gorgonio and Venancio get to you," Theron told them, keeping his voice low. "They'll talk a lot of shit, but they won't do anything without Ulrich's orders."

"That's small comfort," Samantha murmured.

She drank some water and looked at Dave; Theron walked over to him and poured more water into the cup. "I've seen some of your news reports about the poaching," Theron continued. "You're both very determined to protect that source of yours, whomever he or she is."

"If you expect us to tell you who our source is," said Samantha, "we won't."

"I'm not," Theron replied, letting her photographer drink. "I'm actually kind of impressed. I'm sorry we're putting the two of you through this."

Samantha eyed him warily for a moment, until at last she said, "You don't really agree with all of this, do you."

It was more an observation than a plea, and it caught Theron somewhat by surprise. "No...I don't," he responded, honestly.

"Then why go along with it?" asked Samantha. "Won't you help us escape?"

Theron looked over his shoulder worriedly, remembering that the others were still outside in the corridor. "I can't," he whispered. "As much as I want to, I can't. Truth is...I wish I had never gotten involved in this fox hunting thing to begin with. They're gangsters, and they won't hesitate in killing me if they suspect that I'm thinking of turning against them."

"You can still get out of this," Dave told him. "We'll tell the police you helped us..."

"What's taking so long!" Gorgonio's voice at the doorway made Theron freeze. "They drank enough water. Are you trying to drown them?"

"Trying to get them to talk," Theron swiftly lied.

"You're going about it all wrong. ...By the way, isn't it drafty in here?" Without warning, Gorgonio grabbed the thermos out of Theron's hands and hurled the water at Samantha's face. She gasped.

"Stop it, Gorgonio," Theron said. "They already know they're being held hostage. Why do we need to harass them any more?"

"Because I damn want to," he responded.

Dave looked over at Samantha worriedly. She gave a small sneeze but said nothing. The water was icy.

Roxanne reached the convention center after Ulrich had finished his speech. The sounds of a boisterous party, loud music and triumphant voters celebrating their candidate's win, could be heard coming from inside.

As she approached the building, she saw the governor exiting. The cat ducked underneath some nearby bushes and watched.

Denise walked outside after him, still wearing the fox stole around her shoulders. Roxanne hissed at it, but she didn't notice. "Overall, we've had a successful evening," the regional treasurer smiled.

"Now that I've won re-election I'm only a few steps away from the prime minister's office...although I may change the office title once I've liquidated parliament," Ulrich considered.

"What position will you give me as the new, sole ruler of Sarrilla?" asked Denise.

"Would you like to be head of my new propaganda ministry? Once we begin swallowing some of the other countries I'll need someone to suppress any dissenting opinions. You know Qiang says that's important to stay in power."

Roxanne was astounded. She knew Ulrich harbored dreams of unbridled power, but this was unbelievable. Just then Mabel came out of the building and, noticing the conversation, stayed near the entryway.

"Are you going back to the warehouse?" Denise asked Ulrich.

"Yes, I am. Stay here, and try to maintain our good image for those idiots out there. Once I'm through with Samantha West I'll be heading back to the mansion."

Denise went back into the building. Roxanne was thinking about this when Mabel stepped forward. Ulrich seemed only mildly surprised to see her.

"Samantha West," said Mabel cautiously, "She's the TV reporter."

"How observant," Ulrich sarcastically replied, retrieving and lighting a cigarette.

"Are you holding her hostage?"

"Yes, along with her photographer, until they tell me who snitched about my fur trade business," Ulrich smirked. When he saw the upset look in her eyes, he casually said, "Surprised, Mabel?"

"Victor," Mabel said, "I knew you were carrying on with that bitch Denise Ralston, and how you gave her that fox fur stole while you were still trying to delist the foxes; I knew that diplomat from Longguo had approached you one day about something that was most likely unethical at the least; but I never thought you were capable of kidnapping."

"I'm capable of more than kidnapping," he responded, "and if you think of trying to tell someone, you and that alley cat of yours will never live to do so."

Mabel looked frightened, and it took a moment for her to say: "I won't."

"Don't wait up for me," Ulrich said, as he turned and walked off.

Roxanne flattened her ears as Mabel retreated into the building. The cat looked back inside at the rally, where Ulrich's supporters were partying as if they had succeeded in some great deed, completely unaware of Samantha and Dave's plight or even the fact that they were celebrating the re-election of a fascist. She turned in the opposite direction and saw Ulrich driving off, his car becoming smaller as it vanished down the street...

It was a sudden decision. Roxanne chased after his car. Ulrich did not notice the longhaired cat racing down the street. Her paws pounded on the asphalt as she bounded after the car, her tail swishing behind her...desperation rose as the car picked up speed, and with a leap, she landed on the back hood of the vehicle. She nearly fell off as the car swerved. Before he could notice the cat, she crawled up onto the car roof and crouched there, the wind buffeting her black fur as he drove swiftly towards the warehouse.

"Geronimo was right," she mewed to herself.

Chapter 23 - Inquisitor’s Second Degree

Ambassador Qiang returned to the warehouse with his two bodyguards. When he walked in, he glanced around the room where the hunters and their hostages were, and declared in a loud voice, "The most inept way of doing things. In my country this would never be."

"What's he talking about?" said Venancio to Gorgonio.

"Don't make any difference to me. I get paid by the governor," Gorgonio answered.

"Maybe so," snapped Qiang. "But I pay the governor. Remember that."

At that moment, Governor Ulrich walked in. Ignoring the conversation, he walked straight to where the reporter and her cameraman were sitting, and spoke to Samantha.

"A pity you had to miss my re-election party. It was a grand show. I doubt they'll soon forget my victory speech. I’m sure it made great video on your news program."

He's so self-congratulatory it's annoying, Samantha thought. "You're profiting off of the public's ignorance," she pointed out.

"Is that another affront to your pious sense of ethics?" laughed Ulrich. "Why do you care so much about the public?"

"Really, governor? You obviously do care, because you're always worried about getting their votes," she quickly answered.

"That's debatable but irrelevant." Ulrich dismissed the remark. "You were uncooperative about naming your source earlier. I imagine your accommodations here have made you reconss here have made you reconsider your stance."

"As I told you...I won't reveal my anonymous source," Samantha reiterated.

"Nor will I," added Dave.

"If you don't," Ulrich snarled, "I can assure you that neither of you will live to report another news story."

Samantha sighed. "Go ahead and hold me at gunpoint, like you did to Mr. Washburn...or like Gorgonio here already did to me while you were out making long-winded speeches. You'll get the same answer from both of us...We won't reveal our sources."

"She's stubborn," Gorgonio said.

"Psychological threats can only accomplish so much," Ambassador Qiang interjected. "She knows fully well you won't kill her. How could you? You want the information she possesses."

"If she won't talk she's of little use," responded Ulrich without removing his sharp gaze from Samantha.

"Certainly, but in my country, she would undoubtedly talk," the diplomat stated. "Our methods are more efficient."

Governor Ulrich looked over at him, and then at the poachers. With a quick motion, he silently called the small group out of the room and into the corridor. "You stay here," Gorgonio told Theron before walking out and leaving him alone to guard the hostages.

Everyone else walked a short distance away from the storage unit to be out of earshot. Ulrich turned to Qiang. "So what's your new idea?"

"Hardly a new one," the ambassador corrected. "In Longguo we have certain expertise in interrogating people, and we have perfected our methods. All she needs is the right sort of motivation."

"Whatever we're going to do, it's going to be crude. We have neither the equipment nor the know-how for your country's sophisticated motivational methods," Ulrich responded haughtily.

"Actually...we have both," Gorgonio interrupted.

They all looked over at him. When Ulrich spoke, his voice was cold. "What did you have in mind...?"

Gorgonio smiled, apparently enjoying the thought that they were asking for his input.

In the storage unit, Theron was fidgeting with the rifle he held, curious as to what the others could be saying in the hallway. Dave spoke softly to Samantha.

"I guess this will be it," he said.

"We've done a lot of good stories together, Dave," Samantha replied. "At least we're going, as a result of having done what we love."

Samantha gave a small sneeze. The water that had been thrown on her had almost entirely dried, leaving her chilly.

"That's true," said Dave. Neither of them spoke for a moment. "Did you manage to do what we talked about?" He was referring to the videotape.

"Yes." Remembering that they were in the room with a guard, she looked over suspiciously at Theron.

Theron was barely paying attention to the two journalists. Instead, he was standing at the doorway, trying to determine what the rest of the group was discussing. They were some distance down the hall, speaking in hushed tones, and Theron could not hear what they were saying.

"You know how Geronimo loves to help with our stories," she said. "He's always eager to come to the TV station..."

Dave thought about the statement for a moment. He nodded in understanding. "He's a smart cat," the photographer said.

The reporter gazed silently at the ropes binding her. For a moment she wondered if the videotape had arrived at the newsroom yet. Samantha could imagine the look Denise, Qiang, and Ulrich would have on their faces when they saw the film being broadcast; the only thing she felt saddened about was knowing she and Dave probably would not live to report the investigative story themselves. She tried guessing who Ted and Devon would assign to that story.

"Samantha..." It was Dave's voice. She looked over at him and saw his eyes glistening with emotion. "I love you...Samantha," he whispered.

"David..." she answered softly, "I love you too."

Their private moment was interrupted by Theron clearing his voice and saying, "Hey, someone's coming."

"Theron!" Venancio's voice called. He appeared beside Theron at the doorway and jerked his head as if for him to go. Theron glanced at the reporter and cameraman briefly and then slipped out into the corridor, where he found the others. Ulrich spoke swiftly and pointedly.

"Gorgonio tells me you know about electricity."

This made Theron alert, mostly because he had not expected the remark. "...Yes."

"What level of electricity is lethal for a human being?" Gorgonio asked.

"Depends on whether it's AC or DC," said Theron.

"What does that power source device of yours generate?" he persisted.

"Alternating Current."

"Well, then."

"100 milliamperes," Theron replied promptly.

They stared at him, and he added awkwardly, "...for at least three seconds. But you'd feel a painful shock with far fewer milliamps."

"I thought electricity was measured in volts," Gorgonio questioned.

"Volts are electric potential," Theron explained. "When it comes to an electrical shock, it's the amperage - that's the rate of electron flow - that will tell you what effect it'll have on the body..." He stopped as Gorgonio glanced at the others and gestured towards him, as if proving something to them.

“You see what I mean?” Gorgonio said.

An uneasy feeling came over Theron. "Why the sudden interest?" asked Theron.

"I'll tell you why," Gorgonio smirked maliciously, "Because you're going to wire a makeshift version of the electric chair. Give that insolent news reporter a few good jolts. See if then she won't talk!"

"That's...torture." Theron said slowly.

Ulrich answered him with a calm voice:

"Yes. It is."

Theron suddenly felt very afraid, but he said nothing. Almost in a daze, he obediently walked down the hallway to where he kept his electrical supplies.

Governor Ulrich unceremoniously returned to the storage unit, followed by Qiang, Gorgonio, and the bodyguards.

The journalists looked up at him in silence.

"This is your last chance," Ulrich said sternly. "Name your source."

"Never," responded Samantha.

Theron entered the room and walked over to the table situated next to the hostages. All eyes turned to what he had brought in. It was a rectangular black box that on its front had a small switch and a little green light, apart from a dial with a capital V underneath which had numbers around it from 100 to 1,000. What was more impressive, though, was what was beside the dial. It was some sort of meter with a scale running from 0 to 100. A slender needle rested at zero, and two gilded letters on the face of the meter read: mA.

Samantha did not take her eyes off the contraption. Although she instinctually knew this was something evil, or which at the least would be put to ill use, she was at a loss as to what precisely it was.

Still fearless as ever, and with the same curious, impassive manner as she had when interviewing, Samantha asked:

"What is that?"

"You'll find out," Ulrich told her.

Theron plugged the gadget into the wall socket and flipped the little switch; immediately the small green light flashed on.

"Sam," Dave turned to look at Samantha, "They're planning electro-shocks...Do you understand?"

Samantha looked into his eyes and answered calmly, "Yes. I understand perfectly. They will try torture."

"War may be an art, but torture is a science." Qiang said, almost as if giving a lecture. "We have found in Longguo electric shock one of most effective methods of interrogation..."

"I hate you," said Samantha.

No one responded; the governor merely looked at Gorgonio and motioned towards Samantha with his steely gaze. Having apparently resigned herself to the futility of the situation, the reporter didn't struggle as the lead poacher rolled up the sleeves of her blouse.

"I'll find your breaking point...no matter how long it takes," said Ulrich.

Samantha glanced up and said, "In that case, please hold your breath."

"Set the electricity to the level where she'll begin to feel pain," Ulrich ordered Theron.

"But this is inhumane!" Theron insisted.

At this outburst, Samantha and Dave kept their heads down, but all the others turned to stare at Theron with surprised and bewildered looks.

"Do it or you'll die," Ulrich growled at him.

There was a moment when Theron looked unsure; then, Theron took the two electrodes and touched them lightly to Samantha's arms. The skin where the copper contacted seemed to tingle slightly. Glancing at the meter, Theron lifted the wires and adjusted the dial to a higher voltage. He gave an apologetic look towards Samantha before wordlessly handing the cables to Ulrich and stepping aside.

"Ms. West," said Ulrich, "unless you tell me what I want to know, you will experience a lot of pain."

"Go ahead. I'll still never tell you," she replied swiftly.

Gorgonio had been watching impatiently. He didn't like the hostages and felt no remorse.

"Let me do it, governor," he said.

Ulrich beckoned him over and without looking away from Samantha, handed him the two electrodes.

"Motivate her to talk," he ordered.

In the blink of an eye, Gorgonio pressed the ends of the wires to her arms. The jolt of electricity that reached Samantha made her gasp and jerk back suddenly, but the restraints held her down. It was a penetrating, needle-like sensation that entered at one copper rod to traverse her arms and chest to her other hand, as if the energy deliberately sought the second connection. The shock seemed interminable, and when the wires were lifted she let out another breath, almost gratefully. The power had been on for only three seconds.

"Six milliamperes," Ulrich, who had glanced at the meter during the shock, dryly observed. "Theron said the lethal point is one hundred. You've seen what only six is like. If you insist in your stupidity we could go at this for hours, Samantha. You'd do best to act reasonably and tell us who your source is."

"You're the stupid one, if you think you can torture me into talking," Samantha retorted.

The words had no sooner left her lips, that Gorgonio again placed the electrodes on her arms. The needle on the meter once more flew up to mark 6 milliamperes, and Samantha clenched her teeth to bear the shock. She did not gasp this time nor make any outcry, and kept her eyes shut; as the electrodes were lifted she gave Ulrich a furious gaze, like a cat forced to tolerate some indignity and plotting revenge against the people responsible.

Ulrich gave her a patronizing look, as if her refusal to divulge the information was simply postponing an inevitability and her doing so was illogical.

"Tell me the name of your source."

"No," came Samantha's resolute answer.

The ambassador, who had been silently watching the proceedings along with his bodyguards and the hunters, now broke in.

"You are wasting your time protecting your informant. If you feel that your job informing the public is so important, what good are you to anyone if you are dead?"

"What good are any of us at informing the public if our sources don't trust us?" retorted Samantha. "Real reporters don't just broadcast press releases, we need sources to dig up news...and sources don't come forward unless they know we'll keep their secret. We need our sources to act like a free press should."

She flinched as Gorgonio shocked her again, rather arbitrarily, and when he broke the circuit she glared at him.

"I'll ask the questions," Ulrich snarled to Qiang under his breath.

"You have no experience as an inquisitor," Qiang told him.

Gorgonio, still standing ready at the dial, spoke up. "Let's raise the electricity and see if we can get her to scream!"

Ulrich gave him an unconcerned nod, as if telling him to go ahead; to which the lead hunter eagerly twisted the dial higher. Dave, who unable to free himself had been watching what they were doing to Samantha, spoke. "You're savages. What have we ever done to you?"

"Besides snooping into stuff that's none of your damn business?" said Gorgonio.

"It's ok, Dave," Samantha told her companion.

"I would just as soon release you if I could," Ulrich said. "Wouldn't you much rather be at home now, resting?"

"Unfortunately, you won't let me go," replied Samantha.

"I could...if you would identify your source."

"I don't reveal anonymous sources."

"That's easy to say," Ulrich answered, "but it's quite different when you're faced with your mortality. This is going to become very ugly soon, once the number on that meter starts rising, and when you truly realize you're being tortured to death you might just rethink things."

Samantha noticed his voice grow softer. "You must have family or friends somewhere who are worried about you. Surely, you don't want to die in this dismal place, without ever seeing them again. All you have to do is name your informant, and we'll forget you ever stumbled across...my business investment."

"Even if that were true, I'd still never name an anonymous source," she said.

"Why? Because you see it as a betrayal of your profession's code of ethics?" Ulrich smiled, a mixture of sarcasm and egotistic superiority. "You refuse to burn a source over an idealistic presumption that doing so would cripple the newsgathering ability of the press, and the public's precious right to know can never be sacrificed. Is it really so worth it as to get fried yourself? I swore to an oath too, Samantha, a ludicrous little formality that said something about upholding the Sarrillian constitution and all it stands for. Tell me," Ulrich asked her, "do you see me distraught over breaking that oath?"

"Your greed corrupted you," she said.

"Like your professional ethics will kill you," he retorted.

"Ethics are the roots of civilization," said Samantha.

"...and we are uncivilized? Perhaps." He turned dismissively to Gorgonio. "Raise the current."

The sight of the dial being turned to a higher setting was somehow itself agonizing, yet Samantha stayed silent.

Ambassador Qiang spoke to the governor again at this point, apparently disregarding the victim's presence.

"It will make little difference whether you continue that act of saying you will spare her life. If it has not worked by now, it will not work at all. We are more efficient in Longguo. When she feels the electricity scorching her body, begins imploring us for death so as not to suffer any more...then she'll talk."

"To hell with you. I'll never talk," Samantha said.

"You are worthless," answered Qiang. "Just like the people out there, who are useful only as long as they can serve the upper class."

At this point Ulrich interrupted, visibly annoyed at the thought that Qiang was trying to out-boss him.

"...I'll admit it, you're not going to leave here alive whether or not you identify your source - but doing so will make things easier for you." Ulrich's gaze became colder. "I can make the last few moments of your life be spent in excruciating agony.”

“I’ll never reveal my sources,” Samantha answered.

When the electrodes touched her arms, the needle moved upward a bit more, marking 10 milliamperes; searing pain made her jerk upright in a terrible spasm, her hands clenching themselves into fists which even by effort she could not reopen. She screamed and, when the switch was finally lifted, fell back trembling.

“Who's feeding you information?" Ulrich persisted.

“Fuck you," Samantha answered through clenched teeth.

10 milliamperes, again. She screamed once more. The pain was intolerable.

When her body drooped after the electric shock, it was Gorgonio who spoke, his voice sardonic.

“Gives a whole new meaning to ‘Reporting Live’, doesn’t it?”

Samantha looked up at him, and he laughed.

Dave was watching with disbelief, but at this he looked directly at the lead poacher. “In all my years as a news photographer…I never thought I would meet someone who enjoys inflicting such cruelty.”

“Shut up!” Gorgonio snapped at him.

Dave ignored him. “You have a dark soul.”

Gorgonio flipped out the switchblade, and in an icily calm voice, answered:

“I’m not as bad as you think I am. I’m worse.”

Dave focused his eyes on him and, without a blink, retorted, “You’re a damn sadist.”

Angry, Gorgonio leapt at Dave, seizing him harshly by the collar; he would have struck him with the knife if Ulrich had not interjected.

“Stop! That’s enough, Gorgonio! Don’t waste your time with him.”

Gorgonio was not satisfied. “Why the hell do we need the camera guy, anyway? She’ll name the source eventually.”

"Think, you idiot" responded Ulrich. "If you kill him at this point where will you put him while we persuade her to talk? We might as well deal with them at the same time, then dispose them together."

Samantha and Dave looked at each other momentarily; with the realization that this might be their end. Nothing but a miracle could save them.

Down in the lobby of the WCAT television station, people were surprised to see a large Husky dog run into the building, pushing open the doors with his paws, a videotape clutched in his mouth. The elevator doors were open at the moment, presenting the perfect opportunity for Zachary the dog to leap in and hit the button for the newsroom floor with a paw.

When the elevator reached its destination Zachary ran out, into the busy newsroom, directly towards the editor's office. Devon and Ted were both there; and stood up in surprise when the dog skidded to a halt in front of the office entrance and placed the tape on the floor. Zachary looked exhausted, as if he had run many miles without pause. The dog lay down, panting, and looked up at the men.

"Who's Ted, the editor?" Zachary asked.

"I am," said Ted.

Zachary gave the videotape a small push towards him with his nose, and Ted lifted the tape from the floor. On the tape's label, handwritten, were two names:

Reporter: Samantha West
Photographer: David Candid

Ted could only look at the videotape, unable to speak, his disbelief overshadowed by the tragic knowledge of what this certainly meant; Devon, looking at the tape from over his shoulder, had fallen silent also. Zachary's low woof broke into their thoughts.

"They wanted that brought here."

Chapter 24 - Inquisitor’s Third Degree

The warehouse towered before Geronimo, Ivan, and Natasha, like an enormous mountain to the small animals. Standing on the fringes of the woodland, there was something ever more forbidding about it to them.

"I insist, this place is scary," said Natasha.

"How do we know your humans are still here?" asked Ivan. "They could have been moved out."

"We'll have to look around," Geronimo meowed. "It's too bad Roxanne isn't here! Without her, it'll be harder to find a way in."

The critters emerged from the bushes and padded forward, evaluating the territory. Other than the door in the alleyway, there appeared to be no alternate entrance. Geronimo padded boldly up to the warehouse door and standing on his hind legs, tried to push it open, but it would not budge.

"It's locked," he hissed.

A meow made the animals stop in their tracks. They looked up and saw, perched atop a stack of storage containers, the silhouette of a cat outlined against the green flame of the northern lights in the sky.

"Roxanne!" purred Geronimo.

She leapt down to join them. "Geronimo, you win. Too much is at stake...and I can't let your humans die just because they tried to expose the corruption."

"Thank you, Roxy," Geronimo purred, touching noses with her.

"How'd you get here before us?" Ivan yapped.

"I rode back with Ulrich," said Roxanne.

"Ulrich's here?" Geronimo meowed.

"Yeah, he went inside. Later, I saw the Longguo ambassador arrive too," Roxanne told them. "Come on, I'll show you the way in."

They padded over to the holly bushes near the door but as Roxanne pawed at the opening, it became clear that it had been sealed shut. Apparently, a cinder block had been placed inside, preventing any critter from entering.

"They've blocked it," Roxanne hissed.

Miles away, the moon shone brightly over Tropical Island; its reflection giving light to the gently lapping waves at the sea shore. Leandra West couldn't sleep. She got up out of bed and sat at the kitchen table. She sat there for a long time thinking and was oblivious to the fact that her husband was standing at the doorway.

"Anything interesting happening?" he said smiling at her.

Leandra turned, startled, and returned a smile. "No. I was just thinking about Samantha and the fact that it's been a few weeks that I don't hear from her. I hope she's OK..."

Before anything more could be said, the telephone rang. Leandra answered it and heard Ted's voice on the other end.

"Lee, I wanted you to know this from us personally, before you heard it on the news..." he began but didn't finish, because Leandra spoke up.

"Samantha...Dave... I had a feeling something was happening. Ted, are they alive?"

"We...don't know. They've sent a video tape with a messenger critter. We don't want to assume the worst, but I thought you should be aware of what's going on."

"Thank you, Ted...for calling. Please keep me up to date about things," she said, trying to contain her emotions.

"You bet I will," he said, and hung up.

Leandra placed the phone receiver on its cradle and looked at Laurence, who said, "I knew this sort of thing would happen sooner or later."

"So did I," answered Leandra, "and so did Samantha."

When Ted hung up the telephone, he turned back to the control room monitors. The anchors were in the studio, the tape was loaded into one of the videocassette players; they were ready to broadcast at his word. All eyes were upon him.

"Air the tape, now!" Ted told them.

It was somber yet triumphant for everyone in the newsroom as the tape was broadcast across the nation. It was bittersweet; they had abandoned their colleagues to whatever fate might befall them so that the people might know - a journalists' farewell.

For Samantha West, it had reached that point where the inexplicable thing was not that the electric shocks would ultimately kill her, but that they delayed so long in doing so. The pain was excruciating, and her only respite from it was when Ulrich was shouting at her. She would never reveal her source - indeed the mere thought of doing so was anathema to her - and so, as time dragged on, her torturers' persistence seemed to become ever more stupid to her, just as to them, her persistence became ever more absurd.

The electricity had been left at the setting of 14 milliamperes. Higher than this would start to impede her breathing, Theron had warned, hence it had now become a sort of sadistic waiting game. Ulrich wanted Samantha to reveal her source, Samantha refused to; Samantha wanted Ulrich to give up already, Ulrich would not; and Dave watched in silent, mental anguish.

"You know, I said they would probably not soon forget my victory speech. I was wrong. In fact, I think it'll be overshadowed by my condolence speech tomorrow, when they find your lifeless bodies beside the news van outside," Ulrich said. "The dedicated TV news crew, martyrs for press freedom. I think I'll make a show of calling for your killers to be brought to justice."

Samantha didn't answer. She was becoming lightheaded from the shocks. Drops of perspiration shone on her forehead, and a thin line of sweat trickled down the side of her face.

Ulrich yelled at her, "Name the source, you stubborn fool!"

Samantha ignored him and said nothing.

Gorgonio brought the electrodes down to contact her arms again, and she screamed as the electricity was applied. The lead poacher seemed fiendishly pleased when the needle jerked up to mark 14 milliamperes.

"This anonymous source of yours isn't worth your life," Ulrich told her when the circuit was broken and she fell back shuddering. "A person's own life should be their most valued possession. What benefit do you get out of risking it like this?"

Samantha stared at him, astounded he would say such an egocentric thing. Finally, she spoke:

"You say I ought to value my own life above all else, and you ask what benefit I get from risking my life. If everyone thought like you, there would be no firemen who go into burning buildings to rescue lives trapped inside...no doctors who travel to epidemic-ravaged lands to cure deadly diseases...no soldiers who defend the country..."

"How pretentious of you," Ulrich scoffed, "to equate news-writers with the safety of the nation."

"You're wrong, governor," Samantha said, her voice soft and weary. "Democracy lives with the voice of the people...and that voice would fall silent without those who investigate so the people can know what's happening in the world, so they can make the informed choices they need to be able to make to safeguard our democracy. But of course you don't want a democracy," she continued as Ulrich gave her a wearied, somehow self-righteous look. "I've never said what I thought, because it wasn't my place as a reporter, but do you really want to know what I think? You're a coward who has to resort to tying up and torturing someone because he doesn't have the intelligence enough to recognize that he can't buy or terrify everyone...that there are ethical ideals worth fighting and dying for because they keep our nation from devolving into a slave society with someone like you at the top!"

"You think you're perfect," Ulrich snapped.

"Perfect?" Samantha said, "Is that why you think of your own benefit instead of the benefit to humanity, your own life instead of the lives of others...? I'm certainly not perfect, but if it makes me elitist to believe in this concept of self-sacrifice, then so be it. No matter what torture you put me through, no matter if I was the last being in this world to stand for freedom, I will always firmly believe that the people have a right to know!"

There was a momentary silence in the room, and then Ulrich turned to Gorgonio and said:

"Shock her."

As the current ran through her, she screamed. Dave watched unable to do anything. He felt ill. It sickened him to see the metal flash of the wires touch her skin; her screaming helplessly until they broke the electric circuit. The constant barrage of insults being hurled at them, the intense stress of watching someone he loved being tortured, all these things within the small confines of a warehouse storage room. His stomach was upset yet he couldn't have the relief of throwing up. Dave was growing angry and angrier.

Soon he could not hold back his ire anymore, "You bastards!" he yelled at the crooks, "It's so easy for you to treat a woman this way...Bet you don't have the balls to fight me like a real man would. Untie me, and see if you can!"

Ulrich looked at him in surprise. Dave's face had changed from the time they had caught him. His usual complacent demeanor had come to seem vicious.

"Seems the cameraman is willing to die for his friend. How nice...however, I'll deal with you later," answered the governor, and turned his attention back to Samantha.

"You think your little news report could have brought me out of power?" he began, "You think your anonymous source can do it? Even if he went to a dozen other newspapers and TV stations...no, even if I had let your precious videotape air, it would be dismissed by the public, the instant they saw it. You're naive; you place too much faith in them, so stop saying so much shit and give me the name of your source."

Samantha took a deep breath and began to recite, "I do solemnly swear to uphold freedom of press and speech, and the right of the people to know...to report the news truthfully and fairly, and to forego any activity which may compromise my ability to do so...and to safeguard all sources of information to whom I have vowed confidentiality...until my last breath."

No one spoke. They all stared at her, shocked that she would be so steadfast in her ideals; all were amazed except for Dave, who thought to himself, That's my Samantha. Loyal to the end.

A motion from Ulrich made the pain resume. It was hopeless not to shriek, yet when Gorgonio removed the electrodes she repeated the oath. At intervals, she cut off with an agonized cry as Gorgonio interrupted her with the electric shocks, but she persisted:

"I do solemnly swear...to uphold freedom of press and speech...and the right..."

"...the right of the people to know...to report the news truthfully..."

"...and fairly...and to forego any activity which may..."

"...compromise my ability...to do so...and to safeguard...all sources of information...”

“…to whom I have vowed confidentiality...until my last breath."

When Gorgonio lifted the wires, she collapsed, shaking; her heart jumped ahead in tachycardia. She noticed the ropes binding her right arm had loosened somewhat, perhaps from the repeated convulsions. Ulrich bent over her and said, "It might very well be your last breath."

Without warning, Samantha pried herself free and in a swift motion, slashed her fingernails across Ulrich's cheek. Ulrich raised his hand to his face, taking a step back as Samantha reached to her arm trying to pull off the binding ropes, but before she could, Gorgonio and Venancio jumped to her and tied her back down. Samantha struggled but it was to no avail. When she was secured to the chair, Ulrich stepped forward and smacked her face so hard she let out a sharp cry.

"Bitch!" he said. "You're too feisty for your own good."

Theron had at last become disgusted with the whole thing. "Do any of you have a cigarette?" he asked.

Ulrich stopped rubbing his cheek, reached into his pocket and retrieved a pack of cigarettes, which he threw at Theron without saying a word.

Venancio sneered at the younger hunter and asked, "Since when do you smoke?"

"Since now," Theron retorted, and walked out of the room.

Ambassador Qiang turned to leave also, and a perplexed Ulrich left the hostages and followed him out into the corridor.

"You're not staying to see the outcome of this?" he inquired.

"It has been three hours," Qiang responded. "She is too strong-willed. You will never break her."

"I suppose you have some experience in this matter," Ulrich sarcastically said.

"In Longguo, I oversaw our interrogations before I was appointed ambassador to Sarrilla," Qiang replied seriously. "I have seen prisoners like her. They believe too strongly in their ideals, be they political or professional. It is the same with this reporter West. You can torture her until she dies and she still will never tell you the identity of her informant."

"Well, then," Ulrich impatiently asked, "how do you get these kind of people to talk in Longguo?"

"We don't," said Qiang. "We execute them."

Ulrich gave him an incredulous look.

The ambassador continued, "Interrogating her any more is a useless endeavor. I would shoot them both."

"We don't all have diplomatic immunity," the governor scoffed. "The tape might have been destroyed but I'd still like to know who the source is."

"That matter is entirely up to you, but I believe you are wasting your time," Qiang said.

Qiang left quickly and Ulrich walked back into the storage unit. Samantha had recovered slightly; she was no lotill pale. She was sitting back in the chair, and when she saw Ulrich again she tried to move her head forward, however weakness and dizziness made this difficult and she leaned back again, giving Ulrich a piercing look.

Outside, Theron was leaning against the wall beside the doorway. He took a cigarette out of the box, lit it with a match and started to smoke it. He saw Qiang exiting the building, muttering something in Chinese to his bodyguards as they walked to the limousine.

When they had driven off, Theron turned back to the cigarette. The early morning weather was chilly, and the sky was still dark. Out here, it was impossible to hear the interrogation in the warehouse, and Theron shivered at the quiet and stillness. The only sounds were the rustling of the bushes and pine trees.

Theron had developed an intense dislike for Ulrich and the others. He felt really bad for the journalists and wished he could do something to help them. His mind thought over and over about the torture Ulrich had demanded be inflicted. Damn the day I got mixed up with these people, he thought.

All of a sudden, he noticed four pairs of glowing eyes watching him from the holly bushes. He froze.

"Theron!" It was Roxanne. As she padded out of the bushes with her tail up, a distrustful fox-growl warned: "He's one of the hunters!"

"Oh, ffftt! He doesn't agree with the others!" said the cat.

Theron crouched down to stroke her as the other animals crept out of the bushes. A suspicious Geronimo had flat ears, while Ivan and Natasha had their fangs bared. "Roxanne, what are you doing here?" Theron asked her.

"Saving my friend Geronimo's humans," Roxanne announced, swishing her tail to gesture towards the Siamese-mix tomcat.

"The TV news crew?" Theron hadn't realized that Samantha and Dave had a pet.

"Yes," meowed Geronimo. "Are they all right?"

"Well, they're still alive," Theron said plainly. He looked at the small band of determined critters. "There are only four of you," he observed. "How do you plan to rescue them?"

"We're going to attack by surprise," Geronimo replied.

Theron thought about this for a moment. Critters attacking...it's so unexpected, it might actually work, he realized.

"Wait," Ivan suddenly yapped, "I recognize you. You're the one who prevented us from being shot the other day."

"Why did you do that?" questioned Natasha.

"I’ve had enough of the poaching," Theron sighed. "I never realized how far the governor would go. I'm so sorry for all the havoc we've been causing you foxes. I wish I could reverse it somehow, but the best I can do now is to help you rescue your human friends."

“It's a start,” Geronimo mewed. “I hope we’re not too late. If my humans have been killed, all hell is going to break lose in there, because I’m not going to just sit back and let it go unpunished.” He ended his statement with a hiss.

Theron nodded. "You have to hurry," he said, opening the door behind him and leading the animals in.

Chapter 25 - Thaw

What struck Geronimo foremost about the warehouse interior was how pitch-black it was. It was so murky, it was difficult even for his feline eyes to see.

Theron walked ahead of the little group of critters, leading them down the hallway. As they rounded a corner, there was more light, although it flickered at intervals. "Samantha and Dave are being held in one of the storage units, towards the end of the corridor," Theron told them.

At that very moment, Venancio walked out of one of the rooms, and Theron hurriedly pushed open one of the other doors. "In here!" he whispered, and the critters all ducked into the storage room. It was small and barren except for a stack of crates that reached almost up to the ceiling. The wire mesh running along the top of the ceiling was broken here.

"What the hell are you doing?" Venancio's voice was heard out in the hallway as Theron closed the storage unit door.

"Coming back inside, to make sure no one short-circuits my electrical equipment," Theron said, feigning a lack of sympathy for the journalists.

"So why'd you open this door? What's in there?" Venancio demanded, and knocked against the metal wall that served to divide the storage room from the hallway. All the critters flattened themselves to the ground.

"I can open whatever door in here I want," Theron answered. "What do you think is in there, arctic foxes? The whole place is empty."

Just then, another sound made all the critters jump. Geronimo's fur stood on end when he heard his human, Samantha, screaming.

"What are they doing to her? We have to find a way over there!" Geronimo hissed.

"I heard someone in there," Venancio declared. Pushing Theron out of the way, he pulled open the storage unit door and looked inside.

There was nothing there, except for the stack of crates reaching up to the ceiling.

"Well?" questioned Theron.

"Come on," Venancio said in a bad mood and turned around, walking away leaving Theron to shut the door. Theron pushed the door forward but left a crack open, in case the animals needed a way out.

From above, precariously standing atop the wire mesh, the critters watched Venancio and Theron walk down the corridor. The cats and foxes went unnoticed by the people below. "You're really paranoid, Venancio. You were acting as if I was hiding someone in there or something."

"Shut up, Theron."

The critters exchanged a nervous look. "Step lightly," Roxanne purred, "One wrong step and we'll go crashing down."

Geronimo took the lead, walking gingerly with Roxanne and the two foxes following. He tried whenever possible to step on the support beams as opposed to the wire mesh itself, but there were areas where this was impossible. Whenever this happened, the mesh sagged down.

Before long, they began to hear Ulrich's voice speaking, and they came to the storage unit where the hostages were being held. The critters stared down into the improvised torture chamber, not entirely sure what it was that they were witnessing.

Samantha was hurting. She was resolute in her goal to not let Ulrich win. She refused to reveal her source, no matter the pain or ultimate cost. With each surge of electricity coursing through her body, she grew more silent and finally, her head fell forward.

Ulrich spoke. “The pain will end as soon as you tell us the identity of your source.”

A weary Samantha shook her head from side to side.

“You will eventually,” Ulrich scoffed. “Again with your stupid professional ethics. Do you realize how that sounds?” He leaned over her, grasping her arm, and she winced with pain. “Ethics, are flimsy changeable rules that were meant to be broken, created and governed by those in power.”

There was some self-evident fallacy in this reasoning, Samantha could tell, but in her exhausted state she could not discern what that was. How long had this torture been going on? She glanced at Ulrich’s hand, noticing his wristwatch and found – with a certain measure of surprise - that she could no longer tell the time. She was aware that the symbols surrounding the clock’s face were numbers with the direction of the hands conveying meaning, yet those numbers were as a cipher – significant yet unintelligible.

Ulrich observed her gazing dizzily at his watch but ignored it. “You think that the public’s right to know outweighs your suffering, isn’t that right? Well, let me be the first to tell you that your ethics are outdated.” He smirked and stepped away from her, “You must learn that whether the public hears or not, it makes no difference. I am a very powerful man; the people believe in me and will not heed your words.”

Samantha interrupted. “The people don’t know the real you,” she said, noticing for the first time, how tired her voice had become.

A pause here, and Ulrich stared at her pensively – then spoke. “The common people have no say in whether I go down or not, they have no power…the rich have the power and the control, and they will keep me here for as long as their purposes are met.”

Samantha felt sick. The electric shocks were taking effect, but her strong will prevailed. She remained silent and Ulrich grabbed her face with both hands, forcing her to look at him. “Your suffering is worthless, don’t you see? You will die here, your cameraman will die here, and the corruption will persist forever. I hold a seat of power and intend to climb the ladder up until I become prime minister. Once I am prime minister, there will be no opposition. Your ludicrous notion of the people’s right to know, will be as forgotten to the public as you will be to them in a few weeks. The corruption is entrenched as tundra locked in permafrost.”

He released her and Samantha’s mind drifted beyond her own memories, to a timeline where always the tyrant tried to suppress the defiant; the dictator proving that men were more savage than beasts and yet, no human could ever prevent the sunrise. When she at last spoke, her voice was low and clear, yet it held a fearless tone that was unmistakable. She looked directly into his eyes and a small weak smile crossed her face as she replied:

“Go on, kill me. Even permafrost thaws in the sunlight.”

Ulrich stared at her in complete surprise. This response of hers had taken him totally off guard, and this angered him. He pushed Gorgonio out of the way, grabbing the wires from him and twisting the dial to its highest setting.

Samantha closed her eyes in sickening expectation, but the shock that followed was unlike all the others they had inflicted on her. When Ulrich touched the electrodes to her wrists, she was seized with burning pain; her body stiffened and her eyes flew wide open. It was a horrible sensation that radiated down her back and felt as though it would tear her apart. The meter's needle had swung full-scale, to mark 100 milliamperes, and unable to progress remained quivering on the spot. The sinister crackle of the electrical current could be heard in the absence of the reporter's screams. She couldn't breathe.

Her cameraman had gone pale and was watching, appalled and helpless, as a thin wisp of smoke rose from the device and from the wires where they contacted Samantha's wrists. Above, the critters could not believe the extent of the cruelty; they were uncertain as to when they should take action. Theron could stand it no longer, and with a quick movement of the hand, pulled the plug out of the outlet. Just as suddenly, the needle fell back to zero and the reporter slumped in her seat, eyes closed.

A visibly distraught Dave remained speechless.

Ulrich removed the electrodes and looked up in fury to see a defiant Theron facing him.

"Yes, governor," he said tersely, "I pulled the plug."

Ulrich pushed Theron to the ground, saying, "You fool! How dare you!"

Gorgonio's voice made the governor glance back towards Samantha. "She looks dead."

Ulrich placed his hand on Samantha's neck for a brief moment and announced, "There's a heartbeat. She's only fainted."

Hearing those words were a relief for Dave; he took in a deep breath and exhaled slowly.

Ulrich was angrier than ever and said, "As soon as she wakes up again, I'm going to make that damn reporter wish I had killed her..." His cell phone rang, interrupting him, and he answered it brusquely, "Yes, what is it?"

"Victor, it's all over the news," Denise's voice came on the other line. "We've got to leave Sarrilla. The police were at my apartment..."

"What...?"

"The tape, Victor! It was on Channel 8, along with those reporters' pictures saying that they've gone missing."

"That can't be," he said hoarsely.

"It can very much be. It’s on TV right now. It’s been played over and over on all the channels. This is a disaster, Victor. There's no way your public relations team is going to get any of us out of this one. Half the public is crying that you're a murderer destroying the environment, and the other half is saying you've betrayed your constituents' trust. Not to mention the press is calling you a..."

"You're no saint yourself!" he snapped furiously. "To hell with what the press says. They're the ones stirring up all this trouble with that fucking tape. I still want the name of that anonymous source who tipped them off so I can personally..."

"Are you kidding me? You just don't get it. Our careers are ruined." Denise was adamant. "Forget about your glorious re-election win. They're talking about impeachment. Are you still at the warehouse?"

"Yes."

"Well, get out of there. The cops are going to fall on that place like a band of hawks, and the media's bound to be right behind them. I was able to get out of my apartment by a stroke of luck."

"Where are you?"

"On the highway." There was a background sound of a rotor slicing through the wind. "Oh shit! It's a news helicopter! I'll call you back."

Denise hung up, and Ulrich was still in a daze as he put the cell phone away. Gorgonio was looking quizzically at him.

"That damn tape's on the air," announced Ulrich.

Samantha was coming to, and she weakly looked over at the governor. There was an acrid taste in her mouth, and her entire body felt numb and hurt. A burnt smell still lingered in the air. She turned to Dave and managed a small smile; her cameraman winked an eye at her and whispered to her:

"Our tape aired."

Ulrich saw this and his stunned reaction to the tape's broadcasting gave way to hatred for the hostage TV news crew. He looked at Gorgonio and gesturing to the reporter and cameraman ordered, "Kill them, and when you're finished with them," he added, pointing to Theron, "take care of him."

"That'll be my pleasure," Gorgonio smirked.

Theron seemed to be in a state of shock, watching speechlessly as Gorgonio flipped open the revolver and loaded it. Samantha and Dave just gazed at each other accepting their fate; neither one said a word, not even when the cylinder snapped back into place and the gun was aimed point-blank...

"Mrreeowwrrr!" Geronimo screeched, slamming his weight onto the wire mesh and plummeting down onto Gorgonio's head. The cat sank his claws in and held on for dear life, hissing. The gun fired, and missed by inches.

"Now!" growled Ivan, and he and the other critters leapt down, snarling and caterwauling, onto the astonished criminals below. As a growling Natasha began snapping at Venancio, a flat-eared Roxanne attacked Governor Ulrich. He reached for his gun, but Roxanne took a flying leap and latched onto his arm, sinking her claws and fangs into his skin. He dropped the revolver and tried to pry her off.

Gorgonio forced the yowling Geronimo off and reached for his rifle, only to be bitten on his leg by Ivan the fox.

"You damn canine," he snapped, trying to kick him. Ivan yapped and dashed out of the storage unit. Forgetting about both Geronimo and the hostages, Gorgonio ran after the fox, and Geronimo raced after Gorgonio.

Theron, meanwhile, had leapt up. Taking Gorgonio's switchblade from the table, he hurriedly cut off the ropes binding Dave. The cameraman jumped out of the chair but almost fell down, both from the beating he had received earlier and from having been seated for so long. "Help Samantha," Dave said.

As Theron released Samantha, it became evident that she could barely move from weakness. She tried to reach up and grab Dave's sleeve to pull herself out of the chair, but her arm fell and she felt a jab of pain. Gazing dizzily at her arms, Samantha realized that besides sore marks left on her wrists by the ropes, there were red burns where the electrodes had contacted her skin.

"Dave," she said. Her voice, expended by her pained cries during the torture, had become so soft as to be nearly inaudible.

The cameraman helped her up, holding her from collapsing, and she leaned on him. The reporter was shivering, her heart still beating with unusual rapidity. Somehow, after all of those electro-shocks, what she felt was terribly cold. "Come on, Sam," Dave said reassuringly.

He helped her to the entrance of the storage unit, and Theron pointed down the corridor. "Go down this way and turn left at the end. The exit is there."

"We won't forget you helped us," Dave told him.

Suddenly, Theron felt himself grabbed by his collar from behind, and as he turned around he saw it was Venancio. Natasha, meanwhile, was biting Venancio on the leg but it didn’t stop him from hitting Theron.

"I always knew you couldn't be trusted, you asshole!" Venancio snapped at the younger hunter.

"Go!" Theron waved Samantha and Dave off, and punched Venancio.

Ulrich saw the journalists leaving, but he was tussling with Roxanne. "Get off of me, you dumb animal!" he yelled at her. "You're getting kicked out of the governor's mansion too, no thanks to that newswoman and her unnamed source!"

He pushed the cat off, and she faced him as she landed on all four paws. Her back was arched and her fluffy tail was frizzed to double of its usual size; Roxanne’s ears were flat and her fangs bared in a ferocious hiss.

"I'm her anonymous source!"

He stared at the cat incredulously for a moment, shocked into silence. She continued hissing:

"Who else do you think would have known all your secrets? You underestimated me; you were so stupid you didn't think a simple housecat would listen and reveal your corruption to the world. I'd had enough of your cheating on Mabel, of your treatment of me, of your thinking you could do any cruel thing you wanted with impunity. That's why I not only became Samantha's source...I called her at the TV station to begin with!" said the cat, launching herself at Ulrich with a caterwaul.

The governor caught Roxanne by her amethyst collar and hurled her backwards. She collided with Natasha, who was helping Theron fight Venancio, and the two critters toppled into a stack of empty cardboard boxes. One of the boxes fell on them, trapping them underneath.

Ulrich grabbed his revolver, which had fallen to the floor, and ran after Samantha and Dave. The thought of his being undone by an animal was too much for him, as was the idea of his being politically discredited in the media. For all the harm he had caused, he blamed Samantha for having exposed him and he refused to let her return to her career while he spent the rest of his life in jail.

Chapter 26 - Revenge of the lemmings

Ivan ran into the forest, ducking bullets from Gorgonio's rifle. Bounding over a creek, the poacher's footsteps sounded more distant and the fox turned to see. Gorgonio could be seen far back among the pine trees, but Ivan appeared to be evading the hunter.

Ivan continued running and at last he reached the Whirlpool River gorge, which continued winding through the forest until it eventually divided the city and the woodland at a point farther down. The fox could just make out the Vaharis city lights some distance away, contrasted with the sky's natural pale blue light as the sun began to rise over Nortenya.

Realizing he could go no farther, Ivan ducked behind a large boulder. Here he stayed, trying to quiet his breathing.

Gorgonio came closer to where the fox had seemingly vanished. He glanced around, then looked down at the ground. Here, deep in the forest, the air was colder and much of the snow had not yet melted. Marked in the snow for all to see, were Ivan's pawprints.

With a smirk, the hunter stepped behind the boulder where Ivan was hiding and pointed his rifle at him. The fox was now trapped between the boulder and the cliff, with his only escape route blocked by Gorgonio.

Before he could shoot, Ivan jumped at him. He batted the fox with the rifle, and the animal fell over the edge of the cliff. Ivan managed to catch onto a narrow ledge halfway down with his claws and pull himself up.

Ivan looked up, his bushy tail swishing from side to side. Unbeknownst to Gorgonio, Geronimo had caught up and seen everything.

The poacher raised his rifle and aimed at the fox, and in the blink of an eye Geronimo leapt with a yowl to Ivan's defense.
