Gorgonio was struck in the back by the cat's sharp claws, and with a cry struggled to get the caterwauling Geronimo off. He succeeded, and the Siamese-mix cat was tossed roughly down where Ivan had been beside the boulder.

"All right, if you want to be such a hero I'll kill you first." the poacher smirked, snapping back the rifle's safety catch.

Geronimo braced himself for the shot, when suddenly...unexpectedly...there was a squeak.

Gorgonio looked down, almost bewildered, to see what creature would dare interrupt him, and saw a lemming.

It was seated on his shoe, looking up at him.

He kicked it away. Geronimo flinched to see the small animal being thrown back with such force.

There was another squeak, and the hunter turned to see a second lemming perched on his shoulder.

"What the fuck...?"

The lemming bared orange, jagged fangs and began chirping angrily.

Suddenly Gorgonio was assailed by lemmings, leaping out of the bushes and hurling themselves at him. There were hundreds, thousands of the fluffy little rodents. Chirping together in a fearsome noise, they swarmed him, biting wherever they could sink their fangs into. Geronimo watched in disbelief as Gorgonio yelled, dropping the rifle, and tried to pull them off. They were too small to shoot, there were too many of them to push away, and more kept coming, scurrying out of the bushes; a multitude of vicious, vengeful lemmings with one unified objective.

The poacher stumbled back, trying to somehow flee from the lemmings, and in so doing reached the edge of the cliff. With a horrified scream, Gorgonio fell backwards, into the gorge, down into the raging whirlpools and sharp rocks below, with hundreds of rodents still clinging to him. The lemmings still on the land squeaked triumphantly, and in large numbers hurled themselves off of the cliff after him. They spread their paws out as they flew down into the violent rapids.

An astonished Geronimo was taken by surprise when he heard a squeak near his paws. He looked down to see the lemming he had helped escape from the branches in the city, now pregnant. The lemming twitched its whiskers delightedly.

"We lemmings never forget," she said scurrying off, into the woods and away from the cliff.

As the rush of lemmings dissipated, Geronimo noticed Ivan. The fox was pressed against the side of the cliff, staring out to the waves where the lemmings and Gorgonio had vanished.

"Ivan!" Geronimo meowed.

"Didn't we say lemmings were vicious?" Ivan prompted. "Geronimo, you'd better go back to the warehouse and check on your humans."

"How will you get back up?" the tomcat asked.

"Don't worry, the park rangers will get me out of here," said the fox. "They’ll lower a basket down and pull me up. You need to make sure your humans are ok."

Geronimo nodded and ran back towards the storage facility.

During this time, Samantha and Dave had made their way out of the warehouse. As they stumbled outside, they found the news van where it had been left. Upon seeing it, though, the TV reporter and cameraman collapsed on the asphalt.

The antenna transmitter was up, and entangled in power lines above.

They looked up at it despondently, just as Governor Ulrich ran up to them and got in their path. He pointed his revolver directly at Samantha, and Dave tried to shield her.

"You fucking bitch. You think you can destroy my career, do you?" Ulrich snarled at her. "You and your cameraman will still die, and when I'm done with you that treacherous feline Roxanne will lose her nine lives for acting as your anonymous source."

There was a sound of cars screeching. Ulrich looked up to see police cars, an ambulance, and another Channel 8 news van, coming up the street. He turned back to the two journalists, who were huddled together on the asphalt gazing wordlessly at him.

"The thaw might have begun, but you'll never live to see the spring." Ulrich smiled. "You're signing off for good, Ms. West."

Samantha's emerald green eyes locked with his pale blue ones, and weak as she was, her voice somehow regained its strength, as if she was once more reporting live on the air:

"Back to you, governor."

Suddenly a meow was heard and from the holly bushes, Geronimo ran out towards Ulrich. Ulrich reacted instinctually, backing away, and in so doing put his hand on the news van behind him.

There was a flash of light, the crackle of electric current traveling from the power lines down the antenna mast, through the news van and through Ulrich to the ground, and he yelled as his hand seized hold of the door handle. He was trapped in a convulsion, and as his other hand jerked the gun fired upward. A parallel bolt of electricity arced out from the power lines, colliding with the bullet in mid-transit. Samantha and Dave stared at the spectacle in shock as the police, paramedics, and other reporters rushed over. The governor was screaming as smoke began to rise from where he was contacting the news van.

As the other reporters filmed, one of the policemen broke open a metal case on one of the electric poles and pulled an emergency switch. In an instant, Ulrich collapsed limply onto the asphalt. His eyes were closed, and he didn't appear to be breathing as the paramedics hurried over.

Geronimo padded to where Samantha and Dave were. He purred and rubbed against them, his tail up.

Inside the warehouse, Theron and Venancio were still struggling. Venancio reached for the revolver that Gorgonio had dropped, but Theron pushed it away. Roxanne and Natasha, still trapped under the box, found a crack in the cardboard and tried to see what happened as the fight unfolded.

The two men fought like wild animals, punching and kicking until Venancio finally grabbed hold of the revolver. They both struggled for the gun and it went off, hitting Theron. He fell back on the floor, bleeding from his shoulder.

Venancio aimed the gun a second time at Theron and said, "This is your end."

Before he could shoot, a dozen police officers rushed through the doors shouting, "Police! Drop it!"

Venancio looked from the police standing with weapons drawn at the entrance of the storage unit, to Theron, and back...and dropped the revolver. As the police handcuffed him, Venancio glared at Theron but said nothing.

Paramedics rushed over to Theron, who was clutching his arm in pain, and after a quick inspection of the wound, one of the medics said, "The bullet will be taken out at the hospital."

"It hurts like hell," said Theron.

A police officer interrupted. "Chloroform," he said, holding up the empty vial with a plain label.

Theron spoke up, "It was used to kidnap the news reporters."

"Well, the hospital uses it to relieve pain," added the police officer. "This must be the vial that was stolen from there."

Theron turned his attention back to the paramedics. "How are the reporters?" he asked. "Are they all right?"

"They're alive," answered one of the medics, "They'll recover."

Meanwhile, Samantha and Dave were being attended by other paramedics and questioned by investigators. Dave told the authorities how Theron had helped them towards the end of the ordeal by cutting their ropes and showing them the way out. Samantha, despite the onset of laryngitis, whispered her affirmation that Theron felt regret of everything and had told them that he himself was trapped. The police investigators told the pair that this was going to be taken into consideration at the time of Theron's trial, and they would ask the judge for leniency. They also told them that Denise Ralston had been captured fleeing on a highway, and that they might never have located her if not for the Channel 8 news helicopter spotting her car from the sky.

Ulrich was declared dead on the scene.

Chapter 27 - Diplomatic immunity

The city was in a whirlwind of activity. The news was out about the governor's corruption, illegal business arrangements, and his death. Amid the noise and rushing about, Conway had picked up Mabel and the two had driven over to the TV station. They found Ted just as he was leaving.

"Mrs. Ulrich," the news editor said, surprised, "I'm sorry about your husband passing. I heard it was a combination of the electrical shock and fright that caused a heart attack."

"Please call me Mabel," she answered, "Maybe it sounds a bit cold, but there's an old saying that people reap what they sow. In any event, he was a bad man, Ted."

"How are Samantha and Dave?" Conway jumped into the conversation, as he bent down to pet his dog Zachary.

Ted walked out the door, holding it open for them and said, "They're at the hospital, hurt but alive. I'm headed there now."

"We'd like to come, if you think that's ok," Mabel added.

"Oh, I'm sure that'll be ok," answered Ted.

They all headed to the parking garage, Ted to his car and Conway, Zachary and Mabel to theirs, but before they could drive away, a Channel 8 news van drove up. As the reporter, Todd, and the cameraman got out of the vehicle, two familiar looking cats hopped out with them. It was Geronimo and Roxanne.

Ted opened the car door for Geronimo and the tomcat leapt inside.

"Take me to the hospital, Ted" said the cat.

"Exactly where I'm headed," he answered, driving off.

"Roxy!" Mabel exclaimed, picking up her cat and holding her close, "I was so worried about you. Where have you been?"

"It's a long story, madame" the cat said, "I'll tell you soon."

Conway smiled at them, and his dog Zachary, who was in the back seat, barked with joy.

Across town, Samantha and Dave were admitted to hospital; Dave insisting that he be in the same room with Samantha. She received treatment for the burns that the electrical shocks had left on her hands and arms, with a topical ointment that not only facilitated healing but left no scars. While Samantha was being examined, another doctor checked Dave. He had a bruise on the side of his face that would heal on its own, and since he had been punched in the ribs, it was difficult for him to move quickly without feeling pain; however, there were no bones broken, only cracked, and this could also heal on its own. The doctor recommended at least two weeks rest for both Samantha and Dave, and they were told they would recover soon.

"Ms. West was extremely lucky," explained a doctor, "The electric shock of 100 milliamps might've killed her if it had happened at the time her heart was partially constricted, because the heart would've been forced to close instead of opening. The heart's rhythm would be disrupted and a heart attack typically follows."

After they were stable in their rooms, Leandra, Samantha's sister, called the hospital and was relieved to find Samantha was alive and was able to whisper "hello." A series of visitors and well-wishers also paraded through, Ted being one of them, carrying a purring Geronimo which he put on Samantha's bed. The cat curled up beside Samantha and purred even louder.

"You guys have a knack for getting yourselves into trouble," their editor said.

"Occupational hazard," Samantha whispered with a small smile.

"The whole newsroom sends 'Get Well Soon' wishes," Ted told them. "The entire region seems to be in an uproar over what Ulrich was doing, and they are grateful to you two, in particular, for the revelation."

"That's great, Ted." said Samantha, "I can't wait to get out of here so that I can finish the report."

"Are you kidding? You need a vacation first," replied Ted.

“I promise we’ll take a vacation, but we at least want to do the follow-up,” said Samantha.

“We’ve been working on this report for so long,” added Dave. “This is our story and we’d like to see it to the end.”

“I agree with you,” replied Ted, “you will do the follow-up, but the doctor said to rest for several days. The Longguo ambassador has been ordered deported and the Sarrillian prime minister just announced diplomatic relations with that country have been severed. Are you sure you can report impartially on this?"

“Yes,” Samantha and Dave said emphatically and simultaneously.

Ted smiled and nodded his head.

That night at the hospital, Samantha tossed and turned. Dave was with her in the room and he went to her, shaking her awake gently.

"Samantha, it's me; it's all right," Dave said. He held her comfortingly, and she moved closer to him.

"Dave," she said, her voice still a whisper, "We were back in that torture chamber..."

"It's only a nightmare, Sam," he replied. They were both silent for a moment. Samantha was shivering.

"It's freezing in here," Samantha murmured.

"You have a fever," Dave told her gently. "The nurse said it's 102. She said she was coming back with medicine to lower it."

They sat there together, holding each other in silence, until a nurse came in bringing a tray with medicine.

"Oh, you're awake. Good. You need to take this to lower your temperature," she said, handing Samantha a small paper cup with a pill in it. "Do you want to swallow it with water or juice?" the nurse asked.

"Water is fine. Thank you," answered Samantha.

After taking her medicine, Samantha lay down again, Geronimo the cat snuggling close to her. Dave stroked her hair until she fell asleep again and then he lay down in his own bed, feeling exhausted but at peace.

Three days later, Samantha and Dave had both recovered sufficiently to leave the hospital. It was also the day when the Longguo ambassador was scheduled to leave Sarrilla. Both countries had cut diplomatic ties and Ambassador Qiang Xue had been declared persona non grata on Sarrillian land.

Samantha's arms were still bandaged from the electro-shocks, and Dave was still bruised; nonetheless, they went to the airport to cover the event.

The wind was chilly, but the snow had entirely melted and the trees were beginning to sprout the buds of leaves. They set up their camera and tripod on the tarmac with the other journalists; Samantha was giving a live report. They had managed to get a position right in front of the stairs leading up to the airplane entryway.

Upon seeing two large wood crates being loaded onto the airplane, a newspaper reporter piped up:

"What's in the crates?"

"No comment," snapped one of the diplomats.

"Furs?" asked another.

"No comment!"

The thought irritated Samantha. No one had found the fox furs that they had filmed at the warehouse. It was likely that Ambassador Qiang had taken the furs back to the embassy while she and Dave were chloroformed. In fact, the crates being loaded onto the airplane looked like those exact crates with the fox pelts. There was nothing anyone could do; under international law, just as the ambassador had diplomatic immunity which allowed him to walk out of Sarrilla unpunished, the baggage could not be inspected.

Ambassador Qiang was the last to board the airplane, parading past the line of television cameras with a smug air about him. Samantha and Dave tried to hide their anger.

He paused as he reached where they stood, and, almost as an afterthought, reached into his coat pocket and retrieved two items: Samantha and Dave's press ID cards.

"I believe these belong to you," Ambassador Qiang smiled.

Samantha took the press cards from him wordlessly. The other journalists there were snapping photographs and filming the moment; all the cameras trailed on the TV reporter and the corrupt diplomat. Dave, too, focused his camera on Samantha and Qiang, but there was the same disgust in his eyes as in Samantha's.

Without saying any more, the diplomat climbed the steps. Samantha and Dave could only watch as he entered the waiting airplane.

"He's getting away scot-free," said Dave. "He's the one who instigated everything, and he's the one who ends up going unpunished."

"He'll be punished someday," answered Samantha with conviction. "Our job was to reveal the truth."

Inside the airplane, as the propellers roared to life and it began coursing down the runway, Qiang looked out at Sarrilla's thawing spring landscape. He could see, sitting a distance away on a hill overlooking the airport, the two arctic foxes observing the aircraft as it departed southward to Longguo.

There was a shudder through the airplane. Qiang felt a chill course through his body and a sudden, unexplainable fear accompanied by a sense of deja vu. "This moment," he whispered to himself, "I dreamt of this moment last night...my death." His eyes grew wide with terror...

"No...!" he screamed.

On the tarmac, the other journalists had begun dispersing, but Samantha and Dave lingered. They had followed this story relentlessly, had nearly been killed for it, and so it was natural to them that they should remain until the airplane had vanished into the sky. Dave's camera was following the diplomat's airplane as it left, while Samantha, holding the microphone, was reporting:

"Once the airplane leaves Sarrillian airspace, diplomatic ties between Sarrilla and Longguo will officially be broken. As it heads off towards Longguo, it...it looks like there's smoke coming from the airplane."

It was smoke. Samantha stopped talking, lowering the microphone, and she and her cameraman watched as the airplane took a nosedive and spiraled down, colliding with the mountain cliff in an explosion of fire.

Samantha and Dave were speechless, their camera focused on the remnants of the airplane, as the other journalists rushed back. Everyone was talking at once, reporting on the air what had just occurred, but not Samantha and Dave. For the first time in their journalistic careers, they were so incredulous as to be at a loss for words. As the realization sank in, a smile crossed Samantha's face.

"Divine justice," she murmured.

Miles away, the imperial palace of Longguo sprawled amidst a vast Asian garden. In a glass case inside the palace, a rattlesnake was coiled. The emperor was here, looking out one of the large palace windows at the surroundings, when another man stepped into the room. He was about 30, dressed in a suit, tie, and vest, and wearing sharp, rectangular glasses that framed an analytical gaze. There were two guards with him, along with a general, all in Longguo's formal military attire.

"You sent for me, your majesty," the man said, bowing.

"An unfortunate tragedy, Dr. Qiang Shui," the emperor told him, though he seemed impassive. "I wanted to be the one to inform you. The airplane your father was on, returning to Longguo from Sarrilla, crashed upon taking off. No one survived."

The ambassador's son stared at him in shock and appeared distraught. "...What? No, it can't be. Surely there must be a mistake...!"

"There is no mistake," the emperor said, still nonchalant.

"Those Sarrillian swine!" Shui exclaimed, his sorrow turning into anger, "They must have done something to the airplane. I shall see that whoever is responsible for this, will..."

"No, Doctor, you will have nothing to do with the situation." The emperor's stern command made him avert his gaze to the ground. "I will personally oversee the investigation of this tragic accident. I want you to place all your attention in your research. Your experiments are of the utmost value to the empire."

Shui said nothing; he took out a gold pocket watch and opening it, gazed in deep thought at the clock face. "The irony...bitter irony..." he said, unable to hide his emotion. "Do you know what I succeeded in doing in one of those experiments? One of my subjects had a fear of flying on airplanes. I eliminated it entirely."

The emperor frowned, and the general seemed amused. The emperor said, "Doctor, trifles such as that are useless for our purposes. I understand you are a scientist but you shouldn't let yourself get overly enthusiastic."

"Yes, your majesty," he replied, ever more disheartened.

"The ones to blame for your father's death are the two Sarrillian journalists who began looking at our fur trade business," the emperor stated. "If it weren't for them, your father would never have gone on that airplane, and he might well be alive. Think of that when you do your research."

The rattlesnake began shaking its tail, creating a harsh noise. Shui closed the pocket watch and put it away, glancing at the snake. "What are their names?" he asked.

"Samantha Verity West and David Candid."

The scientist was pensive. The emperor dismissed him with a gesture, and he bowed and left.

The general lingered, and when the ambassador's son was gone, the emperor turned to look outside again and scoffed:

"He must not be told we sabotaged the plane. Revolt always begins by truth, and is often fueled by vengeance."

The general bowed low, and said, "Your majesty, I bow down before your greatness to request the privilege of asking a question."

The emperor gave him a sideways look. "Speak."

"Wasn't Ambassador Qiang loyal?"

"The ambassador was loyal, but not astute," explained the emperor, turning back to the window. "I was earning billions from the sale of those furs. It was a most profitable enterprise. He failed in hiding the business arrangement, and he failed in killing those two journalists when he had the chance. Failure is inefficiency."

Chapter 28 - Springtime

The day after the airplane crash, Samantha and Dave went to the newsroom, where, as they had insisted, put the finishing touches on their script and edited the report. The news about the poaching and the corruption had long since been reported around the world, but as they had said before to their editor, it was their story; hence, they were given a half-hour after the evening news for their investigative report plus a segment where Ted interviewed them about their ordeal. Roxanne the cat was also interviewed, this time on-the-record without fear of showing her identity.

Samantha had secretly thought that, although it meant a great deal to both her and Dave to be able to report this, not many viewers would tune in since it was already old news. A month later, she would be pleasantly surprised to learn that their investigative story received the highest ratings ever in the network's history.

Before leaving for Tropical Island, Samantha and Dave appeared at court to testify on Theron's behalf. Theron told the entire story of how the poaching plot had begun, who was involved, and everything he knew. Venancio and Denise both pled guilty, and in so doing, Denise implicated the Vaharis police chief Meadows as one of the people Ulrich had told her to pay off with regional funds, and he was also arrested and tried.

Washburn testified about having been kidnapped and how they attempted to kill him, backing up the statements that Venancio had given about how he and Gorgonio were following Ulrich's orders.

The judge said he believed Theron deserved leniency and gave him one year in jail.

"What do you plan to do when you're released from prison?" Samantha asked him.

"I have no idea," Theron sighed. "But I know one thing...I don't want to stay around here. I've had enough of the Nortenya region."

"Well," said Ted, "if you ever end up on Tropical Island, you could drop by the WCAT television station. One of our lighting technicians is retiring soon. We could always use someone who knows enough about electricity and how the equipment works."

"But after all I've done," Theron said, surprised. "Part of the reason you almost died was because of me."

"No, part of the reason we survived was because of you," Samantha corrected.

Theron thanked them and said he would definitely consider applying there when he was free.

Conway and Mabel, along with their pets Roxanne and Zachary, had come to see the trial also. They had recently married and Mabel was pregnant. They were both beaming with happiness when Samantha went over to them, with congratulations and, ever the news reporter, had a few questions for the ranger.

"What are they planning to do with that fox stole, Denise had?" asked Samantha.

"They're going to auction it off," explained Conway. "The proceeds are going to go into a regional arctic fox breeding effort. The population has been decimated. They need all the help they can get. However, I think it’s safe to say that the arctic fox is not going to be plucked off of the endangered species list any time soon."

"That's good to hear," Samantha said.

As Conway and Mabel left, Dave spoke up, "Hopefully the proceeds really do go into helping arctic foxes, and not just into yet another corrupt politician's wallet."

"Devon has two reporters assigned to track where the money goes, just in case," Ted grinned. "If it doesn't end up with the foxes like it should, we have headlines."

"Well," Samantha said, "a new election has been scheduled a month from now. I guess we'll see what happens."

From the court building, Samantha, Dave, and their editor Ted returned to the newsroom to bid farewell to their Vaharis colleagues. They were given a standing ovation by everyone there.

Afterwards, they went to the airport to head back to Tropical Island. Geronimo was put in a carrier for the flight and brought on board with his humans, accommodations which - although he refused to admit it - were more comfortable than the cramped camera bag he had arrived in.

Ivan and Natasha, perched atop a hill, waved their tails at the journalists as they boarded the airplane. Their winter coats were beginning to shed, leaving them a grey-brown color with streaks of white. Clustered at their paws were three grey fluff-balls, their new litter of fox kits, who yapped goodbye as the airplane flew off towards the Caribbean.

A month passed and Samantha and Dave had fully recovered physically from their ordeal. They were in the middle of their vacation when they received word that - on account of their risky investigative journalism and exemplification of the profession's ethics - they had been selected as the winners of the journalism award known as the Ribbon of Truth. It was something that overjoyed both the reporter and her cameraman.

They were also pleased to hear that Nortenya had elected Egan Irving as their new governor, a man everybody knew loved and respected nature.

Geronimo’s parents, Tifarah and Butch, were overjoyed to learn that their son played a major role in rescuing their humans. Geronimo was no longer a kitten.

Leandra, Laurence, Tifarah, Butch and everyone who knew Samantha and Dave made their way to the awards ceremony that sunny, warm morning.

It was to take place on the far side of Tropical Island, and the reporter and her cameraman decided to travel there via the WCAT news helicopter with Geronimo - who finally got to ride in the helicopter as he wanted - to accept the award. It was a beautiful day; the sun shone across the island, making the sea water glimmer and the buildings sparkle. Geronimo stood up on Samantha's lap, his paws pressed on the helicopter window and purring loudly. Samantha always liked the view from up here; the accident she had been in so long ago had not changed that. Nor had the ordeal that she and her cameraman endured on the mainland dimmed their passion for their career. If anything, it had made them even more determined as journalists. Dave held Samantha, and they both gazed out the helicopter window at the island from above.

At the awards ceremony, they each received a shimmering crimson-silk ribbon with a medal depicting a sun, which Ted as their editor bestowed on them. Geronimo also received a smaller version as a collar; recognition of his saving his humans and safeguarding the videocassette.

Yet...why did it feel as if a bigger story was beginning?

~

"By looking back on the world of yesterday, we gain knowledge that gives us a better understanding of the world of today. In so doing we see how the abuse of one leads to the abuse of all, and how the voice of one can end a winter of cruelty and corruption, and so, bring the warmth of spring. Seasons are a cycle, and winter may return, but there must and will always be a voice to speak up, the sun's rays to illuminate the darkness and thaw even the deepest and strongest permafrost. In many ways this is the greatest moral of our story; the immortal differences between dictatorship and freedom, ignorance and information, and the strong courage that drives people to seek the truth, even at the greatest risk, for with truth comes freedom. Reporting Live, Samantha West, WCAT 8 News; back to you."
